when you say she's a programmer , she did do some , but the real thing is to have said the future is going to be much , much more than this .	當你說她是個程式設計師 , 她做了一些事 , 但真正的目標是 , 要知道 , 未來會比這樣更多 。
now , a hundred years later , this guy comes along , alan turing , and in 1936 , and invents the computer all over again .	一百年後 , 這個傢伙在1936年之後 , 發明了電腦 。
now , of course , babbage's machine was entirely mechanical .	當然 , babbage的機器是完全機械的 。
turing's machine was entirely theoretical .	turing的機器是完全理論的 。
both of these guys were coming from a mathematical perspective , but turing told us something very important .	這兩個人都是來自數學的觀點 , 但turing告訴我們一件很重要的事 。
he laid down the mathematical foundations for computer science , and said , " it doesn't matter how you make a computer . "	他把數學基金給電腦科學 , 說: 「 這不重要你如何製造電腦 。 」
it doesn't matter if your computer's mechanical , like babbage's was , or electronic , like computers are today , or perhaps in the future , cells , or , again , mechanical again , once we get into nanotechnology .	這不重要 , 如果你電腦的機械 , 像是babbage , 或電子 , 如今 , 電腦的機械 , 像是babbage , 或電子 , 像電腦的機械 , 像是babbage , 或電子 , 像電腦的機械 , 像是babbage , 或電子 , 像電腦的機械 。
we could go back to babbage's machine and just make it tiny . all those things are computers .	我們可以回到babbage的機器 , 讓它很小 , 所有這些東西都是電腦 。
there is in a sense a computing essence .	在某種程度上 , 計算機率是如此 。
this is called the church–turing thesis .	這叫做 「 教堂調查 」 。
and so suddenly , you get this link where you say this thing babbage had built really was a computer .	突然間 , 你得到這個連結 , 大家會說這是一台電腦 。
in fact , it was capable of doing everything we do today with computers , only really slowly .	事實上 , 電腦的速度很慢 , 只有慢慢地 。
to give you an idea of how slowly , it had about 1k of memory .	為了給你一個想法 , 它有多慢 , 它有記憶力 。
it used punch cards , which were being fed in , and it ran about 10 , 000 times slower the first zx81 .	它用用punch卡片 , 它會用punch卡片 , 它會用punch卡片 , 它會用punch卡片 , 它會用punch卡片 , 它會用punch卡片 , 它會在1
it did have a ram pack .	牠有一隻強鼠包裝 。
you could add on a lot of extra memory if you wanted to .	你可以加上更多額外的記憶 。
so , where does that bring us today ?	所以 , 今天我們來到哪裡 ?
so there are plans .	所以 , 有計劃 。
over in swindon , the science museum archives , there are hundreds of plans and thousands of pages of notes written by charles babbage about this analytical engine .	在華盛頓特區 , 科學博物館有數百個計劃 , 數以千計的頁面 , 是由查爾斯•巴布所寫的 。
one of those is a set of plans that we call plan 28 , and that is also the name of a charity that i started with doron swade , who was the curator of computing at the science museum , and also the person who drove the project to build a difference engine , and our plan is to build it .	其中一個是我們稱之為 「 計劃28 」 的項目 , 也是我創立了 「 飛機計畫 」 的名字 , 我們計畫是要建造出不同的引擎 , 我們計畫要建造出不同的引擎 。
here in south kensington , we will build the analytical engine .	在南肯斯頓 , 我們會建造出分析引擎 。
the project has a number of parts to it .	這個計畫有許多部分 。
one was the scanning of babbage's archive .	其中一是掃描寶寶的檔案 。
that's been done . the second is now the study of all of those plans to determine what to build .	這已經完成了 。 第二 , 目前正在研究所有的計畫 , 來決定要建造什麼 。
the third part is a computer simulation of that machine , and the last part is to physically build it at the science museum .	第三部分是電腦模擬 , 最後一部分是電腦模擬 , 最後一部分是電腦模擬它 。
when it's built , you'll finally be able to understand how a computer works , because rather than having a tiny chip in front of you , you've got to look at this humongous thing and say , " ah , i see the memory operating , i see the cpu operating , i hear it operating . i probably smell it operating . "	當它完成後 , 你得去看這段影片 , 說: 「 啊 , 我看到記憶操作 , 我看到記憶操作 , 我看到記憶操作 , 我看過這部影片 , 然後說: 「 啊 , 我看到記憶操作 , 我看到記憶手術 , 我看到了 。 」
but in between that we're going to do a simulation .	但在我們要做模擬的時候 。
babbage himself wrote , he said , as soon as the analytical engine exists , it will surely guide the future course of science .	babbageelf寫 , 他說 , 只要分析引擎存在 , 它會肯定指導未來的科學領域 。
of course , he never built it , because he was always fiddling with new plans , but when it did get built , of course , in the 1940s , everything changed .	當然 , 他從來沒有建造 , 因為他一直在1940年代 , 改變了 , 一切都改變了 。
now , i'll just give you a little taste of what it looks like in motion with a video which shows just one part of the cpu mechanism working .	現在 , 我要給你們看一些影片 , 說明它看起來像什麼樣子 , 像是動作中的一部分 。
so this is just three sets of cogs , and it's going to add . this is the adding mechanism in action , so you imagine this gigantic machine .	所以 , 這只是三組測量機制 , 這樣你想像這個巨大的機器 。

art , climate change , environment , film , future , humanity , media , photography	藝術、氣候變遷、環境、電影、未來、人類、媒體、攝影師 。
yann arthusbertrand captures fragile earth in wideangle	yann藝術husbertrand捕捉到全球廣泛的巨大角度 。
i have a big impact on the planet to travel here by plane .	我對地球上有很大的影響 , 是因為飛機 。
i emitted , in the atmosphere , nine tons of co2 ; that is the weight of two elephants .	在大氣層中 , 9噸的二氧化碳 , 這是兩個大氣層的重量 。
i came here to speak about ecology , and i emitted as much co2 as a frenchman in one year .	我來這裡談談生態學 , 我在一年內排放了二氧化碳 。
so what do i have to do ?	所以 , 我該怎麼做 ?
i have to kill a frenchman when i come back at home ?	在我回家後 , 我要殺一位法國人嗎 ?
i have to do my carbon offset in another way , like i do every time .	我必須用另一種方式來做我的碳排放 , 就像我每次做一樣 。
in fact my work is to show our impact on our planet .	事實上 , 我的作品是要展示我們對地球的影響 。
i'm going to show you some examples of the last pictures i've done in the last year .	我要給你們看一些例子 , 是我在過去一年拍攝的照片 。
alberta sand oil , a lot of pollution .	阿爾伯塔沙油 , 很多污染 。
you know the problem ; we don't want to believe what we know .	你知道問題 , 我們不想相信我們所知道的 。
in alberta people work nonstop , 24 hours by seven to extract as much oil as they can .	在阿爾伯塔人工作的24小時 , 七分之二十四小時 , 讓它們能做到 。
we know about the end of oil .	我們知道石油的終點 。
oil sand is not a longterm solution .	油砂不是長期的解決方案 。
but we use three times more oil than we find every year .	但我們用了三倍的石油 , 每年都比我們找到的還要多 。
we don't want to believe what we know .	我們不想相信我們所知道的 。
coral reef in new caledonia .	珊瑚礁在新加州的珊瑚礁 。

glaciers are very important for the life on earth .	冰河對地球來說很重要 。

in this accessible talk from tedxboston , richard resnick shows how cheap and fast genome sequencing is about to turn health care upside down .	在tedxboston的演講中 , 理查•雷尼克斯博士頓 , 很便宜且快速的基因組定序是要把健康照護下降 。
dna , biotech , health care , science , technology	dna、生物科技、健康照護、科學技術 。
richard resnick: welcome to the genomic revolution	理查•雷斯尼克:歡迎來到基因體革命 。
ladies and gentlemen , i present to you the human genome .	各位先生女士 , 我給你們看人類基因組 。
chromosome one , top left .	染色體 , 左邊 。
bottom right are the sex chromosomes .	底部是性染色體 。

and bone marrow is actually what we use to save the lives of tens of thousands of patients , most of whom have advanced malignancies like leukemia and lymphoma and some other diseases .	而骨髓其實是我們用來拯救數以千計的病人 , 大部分的患者都有先進的乳癌 , 像是白血病 , 和其他疾病 。
so , a few years ago , i'm doing my transplant fellowship at stanford .	幾年前 , 我在史丹佛大學工作 。
i'm in the operating room . we have bob here , who is a volunteer donor .	我在手術室 。 我們有一個bob , 一個志願捐贈者 。
we're sending his marrow across the country to save the life of a child with leukemia .	我們把他送到世界各地 , 來拯救孩童的生命 。
so actually how do we harvest this bone marrow ?	所以 , 我們要如何收集這些骨髓呢 ?
well we have a whole o . r . team , general anesthesia , nurses , and another doctor across from me .	嗯 , 我們有一個全部的團隊、護士 , 還有另一位醫生在我身邊 。
bob's on the table , and we take this sort of small needle , you know , not too big .	bob在桌上 , 我們拿著這個小型針 , 你知道 , 不太大 。
and the way we do this is we basically place this through the soft tissue , and kind of punch it into the hard bone , into the tuchus that's a technical term and aspirate about 10 mls of bone marrow out , each time , with a syringe .	我們所做的是基本上 , 透過軟組織組織 , 把這些軟體組織放到硬骨頭上 , 每次一次 , 針對10個骨髓 。
and hand it off to the nurse . she squirts it into a tin .	把牠帶到海裡 , 把牠送到海裡 。
hands it back to me . and we do that again and again .	把它帶回我 , 我們再次做一次 。
about 200 times usually .	大約有兩百次 。
and by the end of this my arm is sore , i've got a callus on my hand , let alone bob , whose rear end looks something more like this , like swiss cheese .	在我的手上 , 手上有一支手臂 , 讓腳踏上手 , 讓腳踏進去 , 像瑞士起士一樣 。
so i'm thinking , you know , this procedure hasn't changed in about 40 years .	所以我想 , 你知道的 , 這個程序已經在四十年內改變了 。
and there is probably a better way to do this .	可能有更好的方法來做這件事 。
so i thought of a minimally invasive approach , and a new device that we call the marrow miner .	所以我想出一個非常普遍的新裝置 , 我們稱之為 「 馬爾礦工 」 。
and the marrow miner , the way it works is shown here .	這裡的標示 , 用它的運作方式來呈現 。
our standard seethrough patient .	我們標準的病患 。
instead of entering the bone dozens of times , we enter just once , into the front of the hip or the back of the hip .	我們不再進入了幾十次的前面 , 我們進入前面 , 進入骨頭 , 進入前面 , 進入骨頭 。
and we have a flexible , powered catheter with a special wire loop tip that stays inside the crunchy part of the marrow and follows the contours of the hip , as it moves around .	我們有一個彈性、有彈性、有彈性的鋼鐵 , 繞著一圈環繞著它移動的軌跡 。
so it enables you to very rapidly aspirate , or suck out , rich bone marrow very quickly through one hole .	所以它讓你很快地穿過一個洞 , 很快地穿過一個洞 。
we can do multiple passes through that same entry .	我們可以多次通過相同的動作 。
and , so , very quickly , bob can just get one puncture , local anesthesia , and do this harvest as an outpatient .	所以 , 很快地 , 麻醉劑會拿到一支針筒 , 用一支針筒 , 來做這個收穫 。
so i did a few prototypes . i got a small little grant at stanford .	所以我做了一些原型 。 我在史丹佛做了一些原型 。
and played around with this a little bit .	再玩一點 。
and our team members developed this technology .	我們的團隊成員開發了這項技術 。
and eventually we got two large animals , and pig studies .	最後我們得到了兩個大型動物 , 豬研究 。
and we found , to our surprise , that we not only got bone marrow out , but we got 10 times the stem cell activity in the marrow from the marrow miner , compared to the normal device .	我們發現 , 很驚人的是 , 我們不只會得到骨髓 , 我們也得到骨髓的幹細胞活動 , 比一般裝置的幹細胞活動更高 。
this device was just fda approved in the last year .	這個裝置是fda被應用在去年 。
here is a live patient . you can see it following the flexible curves around .	這是個活病患者 , 你可以看到它追隨著彈性的曲線 。
there will be two passes here , in the same patient , from the same hole .	這裡有兩個路線 , 相同的病人 , 同一個洞 。
this was done under local anesthesia , as an outpatient .	這是在當地麻醉劑中做的事 。
and we got , again , about three to six times more stem cells than the standard approach done on the same patient .	再次 , 我們得到了三到六倍的幹細胞 , 比標準處理同樣的病人的幹細胞還要多 。
so why should you care ? bone marrow is a very rich source of adult stem cells .	為什麼你要關心 ? 骨髓是非常豐富的成年人幹細胞 。
you all know about embryonic stem cells .	你們都知道胚胎幹細胞
they've got great potential but haven't yet entered clinical trials .	他們有很棒的潛力 , 但還沒有進入臨床試驗 。
adult stem cells are throughout our body , including the bloodforming stem cells in our bone marrow , which we've been using as a form of stemcell therapy for over 40 years .	成人幹細胞在我們的身體內部幹細胞 , 包括血液的幹細胞 , 在我們的骨髓裡 , 包括血液幹細胞 , 在我們的骨髓中 , 包括血液幹細胞 , 在我們骨髓中 , 包括血液幹細胞 。
in the last decade there's been an explosion of use of bone marrow stem cells to treat the patient's other diseases such as heart disease , vascular disease , orthopedics , tissue engineering , even in neurology to treat parkinson's and diabetes .	在過去十年間 , 針對皮膚幹細胞治療帕金森氏症和糖尿病的疾病 , 包括心臟病、血管疾病、組織工程 , 甚至在神經治療帕金森氏症和糖尿病方面 。
we've just come out , we're commercializing , this year , generation 2 . 0 of the marrow miner .	我們剛剛出去 , 今年 , 我們已經出版了 , 一代2.0.0.0 。
the hope is that this gets more stem cells out , which translates to better outcomes .	希望是 , 這會讓更多的幹細胞轉化成更好的結果 。
it may encourage more people to sign up to be potential livesaving bone marrow donors .	它可能會鼓勵更多人去簽名 , 來拯救骨髓捐贈者 。
it may even enable you to bank your own marrow stem cells , when you're younger and healthier , to use in the future should you need it .	它甚至可以讓你銀行自己的幹細胞 , 當你更年輕、更健康 , 用在未來你需要它的時候 。
and ultimately and here's a picture of our bone marrow transplant survivors , who come together for a reunion each year at stanford .	最後 , 這是我們骨髓移植手術的照片 , 每年在史丹佛大學的照片 。
hopefully this technology will let us have more of these survivors in the future .	希望這技術能讓我們有更多的倖存者 。
physicist and surfer garrett lisi presents a controversial new model of the universe that just maybe answers all the big questions . if nothing else , it's the most beautiful 8dimensional model of elementary particles and forces you've ever seen .	物理學家和surfergarrettlisi提出了一個爭議宇宙的新模型 , 它是最美好的你所見過的新模型 。
physics , science , technology	物理 , 科學 , 科技 。
garrett lisi on his theory of everything	在他的理論上 , 所有東西的理論 。
whoa , dude . check out those killer equations . sweet .	沒錯 , 查看那些殺人的方程式 , 很糟糕 。
actually , for the next 18 minutes i'm going to do the best i can to describe the beauty of particle physics without equations .	事實上 , 在接下來的十八分鐘中 , 我要做的最好我可以描述美麗粒子物理學的美麗 。
it turns out there's a lot we can learn from coral .	結果發現 , 我們可以從珊瑚身上學到很多東西 。
coral is a very beautiful and unusual animal .	珊瑚是非常美麗且不尋常的動物 。
each coral head consists of thousand of individual polyps .	每一個珊瑚都有數千個個體的珊瑚 。
these polyps are continually budding and branching into genetically identical neighbors .	這些聚會會持續不斷地突破並分裂成基因相同的鄰居 。
if we imagine this to be a hyperintelligent coral , we can single out an individual and ask him a reasonable question .	假如我們想像這是個超聰明的珊瑚 , 我們就能單獨一個人問他一個問題 。
we can ask how exactly he got to be in this particular location compared to his neighbors if it was just chance , or destiny , or what ?	我們可以問他如何在這個特定的位置 , 和他鄰居的鄰居相比 , 如果只是機率 , 或什麼 ?
now , after admonishing us for turning the temperature up too high , he would tell us that our question was completely stupid .	把溫度升高 , 他會告訴我們 , 我們的問題是完全愚蠢的 。
these corals can be quite kind of mean , you see , and i have surfing scars to prove that .	這些珊瑚可能是很有意思的 , 你看到 , 我也在捕捉鯊魚 。
but this polyp would continue and tell us that his neighbors were quite clearly identical copies of him .	但這個警察會繼續告訴我們 , 他的鄰居非常清楚地描述他的鄰居 。
that he was in all these other locations as well , but experiencing them as separate individuals .	他在其他的位置也一樣 , 但把它們分離成不同的個體 。
for a coral , branching into different copies is the most natural thing in the world .	對珊瑚來說 , 分裂成不同的複製品是世界上最自然的東西 。
unlike us , a hyperintelligent coral would be uniquely prepared to understand quantum mechanics .	不像我們 , 一個超聰明的珊瑚會很獨特地準備去了解量子力學 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics very accurately describes how our universe works .	量子力學的數學量子力學非常準確地描述我們的宇宙如何運作 。
and it tells us our reality is continually branching into different possibilities , just like a coral .	它告訴我們 , 我們的現實持續不斷地分裂成不同的可能性 , 就像珊瑚一樣 。
it's a weird thing for us humans to wrap our minds around , since we only ever get to experience one possibility .	對人類來說 , 很奇怪的是 , 因為我們只能經歷一個可能性 。
this quantum weirdness was first described by erwin schrödinger and his cat .	這種量子怪異的靈感來自於erwinschrod和他的貓 。
the cat likes this version better .	貓喜歡這個版本 。
in this setup , schrödinger is in a box with a radioactive sample that , by the laws of quantum mechanics , branches into a state in which it is radiated and a state in which it is not .	在這個設備中 , 雷射和一個原始的狀態 , 被輻射到一個狀態 , 不論是被輻射到的狀態 。
in the branch in which the sample radiates , it sets off a trigger that releases poison and schrödinger is dead .	在這個樣本的中間 , 會釋放毒素和schrodinger死亡 。
but in the other branch of reality , he remains alive .	但在其他的領域中 , 他仍然活著 。
these realities are experienced separately by each individual .	每個個體都有獨立的體驗 。
as far as either can tell , the other one doesn't exist .	就如同你所說的 , 另一個不存在 。
this seems weird to us , because each of us only experiences an individual existence , and we don't get to see other branches .	這對我們來說很奇怪因為每個人只經歷一個個人存在 , 我們也沒有看到其他的範圍 。
it's as if each of us , like schrödinger here , are a kind of coral branching into different possibilities .	像我們一樣 , 像沙漠一樣 , 每個人都一樣 , 像是沙漠 , 是一種珊瑚分裂成不同的可能性 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics tells us this is how the world works at tiny scales .	量子力學的數學量子力學告訴我們這個世界是如何運作的
it can be summed up in a single sentence: everything that can happen , does .	它可以在單一句子裡說:所有事情都可以發生 。
but this does not mean everything happens .	但這並不意味著一切發生 。
the rest of physics is about describing what can happen and what can't .	其餘的物理是描述可能發生什麼事 , 什麼也不能 。
what physics tells us is that everything comes down to geometry and the interactions of elementary particles .	物理告訴我們 , 一切都經過幾何學和互動 。
and things can happen only if these interactions are perfectly balanced .	只要這些互動是完全平衡的 。
now i'll go ahead and describe how we know about these particles , what they are and how this balance works .	現在我來談談這些粒子 , 以及平衡如何運作 。
in this machine , a beam of protons and antiprotons are accelerated to near the speed of light and brought together in a collision , producing a burst of pure energy .	在這個機器中 , 一個巨大的粒子 , 和反射光的聚集在一起 , 產生了巨大的能量 。
this energy is immediately converted into a spray of subatomic particles , with detectors and computers used to figure out their properties .	這個能量會被轉換成一系列的原子粒子 , 探測器和電腦用來找出它們的特性 。
this enormous machine the large hadron collider at cern in geneva has a circumference of 17 miles and , when it's operating , draws five times as much power as the city of monterey .	這種巨大的機器大型強大的鐵粒撞擊器在大型強烈的機器中大型強大的鐵粒撞擊器在2000年6月 , 當它運作時 , 畫五倍的電力 , 像蒙特利市的大型鐵柱一樣 。
we can't predict specifically what particles will be produced in any individual collision .	我們無法預測特定的粒子會在任何個體碰撞中產生的撞擊 。
quantum mechanics tells us all possibilities are realized .	量子力學告訴我們所有可能性 。
but physics does tell us what particles can be produced .	但物理學告訴我們粒子能產生什麼 。
these particles must have just as much mass and energy as is carried in by the proton and antiproton .	這些粒子必須有許多質量和能量 , 由質量和能量所組成 。
any particles more massive than this energy limit aren't produced , and remain invisible to us .	任何粒子比這個能量限制還大 , 還不存在我們 。
this is why this new particle accelerator is so exciting .	這就是為什麼新粒子加速器很興奮 。
it's going to push this energy limit seven times beyond what's ever been done before , so we're going to get to see some new particles very soon .	它將能量限制七倍的能量限制七倍之久 , 所以我們將會看到一些新的粒子 。
but before talking about what we might see , let me describe the particles we already know of .	但在談到之前我們已經知道的粒子 。
there's a whole zoo of subatomic particles .	原子粒有一大堆的原子粒 。
most of us are familiar with electrons .	大部分人都熟悉電子 。
a lot of people in this room make a good living pushing them around .	在這房間裡的許多人都很擅長推動他們 。
but the electron also has a neutral partner called the neutrino , with no electric charge and a very tiny mass .	但電子也有一個中央的夥伴 , 叫做 「 中央區 」 , 不是電荷 , 和非常微小的質量 。
in contrast , the upanddown quarks have very large masses , and combine in threes to make the protons and neutrons inside atoms .	相較之下 , 中子的質子和中子的質子和中子的質子和中子的質子數量比較大 。
all of these matter particles come in left and righthanded varieties , and have antiparticle partners that carry opposite charges .	所有這些物質粒子都在左邊和右手邊 , 也有反粒子的伴侶 。
these familiar particles also have less familiar second and third generations , which have the same charges as the first but have much higher masses .	這些熟悉的粒子也比較熟悉第二代和第三代代代 , 相同的粒子也比較少熟悉第二代和第三代代代 , 相同的載荷是相同的 。
these matter particles all interact with the various force particles .	這些物質粒子和各種能量粒子相互作用 。
the electromagnetic force interacts with electrically charged matter via particles called photons .	電磁力與電磁力互動 , 電磁力與電磁力互動 , 粒子稱為光子 。
there is also a very weak force called , rather unimaginatively , the weak force , that interacts only with lefthanded matter .	還有一種非常弱勢的力量 , 一種弱勢力 , 與左撇子相互作用 。
the strong force acts between quarks which carry a different kind of charge , called color charge , and come in three different varieties: red , green and blue .	夸克之間的強大力量在四分之三種不同的特質:紅色、綠色和藍色 。
you can blame murray gellmann for these names they're his fault .	這些名字是他的錯覺 。
finally , there's the force of gravity , which interacts with matter via its mass and spin .	最後 , 它的質量和旋轉是重力的 。
the most important thing to understand here is that there's a different kind of charge associated with each of these forces .	最重要的是 , 要了解這裡有不同的載荷 , 和所有這些力量有關 。
these four different forces interact with matter according to the corresponding charges that each particle has .	這些四種不同的力量與物質相互作用作用 , 根據應對應荷每個粒子所產生的作用 。
a particle that hasn't been seen yet , but we're pretty sure exists , is the higgs particle , which gives masses to all these other particles .	以前還沒見過的粒子 , 但我們很確定存在 , 希格斯粒子是希格斯粒子 , 它會對所有其他粒子產生質量 。
the main purpose of the large hadron collider is to see this higgs particle , and we're almost certain it will .	大型強子撞擊器的主要目的是要看到希格斯粒子 , 我們幾乎肯定會 。
but the greatest mystery is what else we might see .	但最偉大的謎就是我們所看到的 。
and i'm going to show you one beautiful possibility towards the end of this talk .	接下來我要給各位看一個美好的可能性 。
now , if we count up all these different particles using their various spins and charges , there are 226 .	現在 , 如果我們把這些不同的粒子用不同粒子用它們的各種不同的粒子來計算 , 總共有226 。
that's a lot of particles to keep track of .	有很多粒子可以繼續追蹤 。
and it seems strange that nature would have so many elementary particles .	看起來很奇怪 , 自然界有許多基本粒子 。
but if we plot them out according to their charges , some beautiful patterns emerge .	但如果我們把它們拿出來 , 有些美麗的圖案就會出現 。
the most familiar charge is electric charge .	最熟悉的電荷是電荷 。
electrons have an electric charge , a negative one , and quarks have electric charges in thirds .	電子有電荷 , 電子有電荷 , 而夸克有電荷的三分之一 。
so when two up quarks and a down quark are combined to make a proton , it has a total electric charge of plus one .	所以當兩個夸克和下夸克被組合成一個質子時 , 它會有一連串的電荷 。
these particles also have antiparticles , which have opposite charges .	這些粒子也有反粒子 , 也有反粒子 。
now , it turns out the electric charge is actually a combination of two other charges: hypercharge and weak charge .	結果發現電荷其實是兩種電荷和弱荷的組合
if we spread out the hypercharge and weak charge and plot the charges of particles in this twodimensional charge space , the electric charge is where these particles sit along the vertical direction .	如果我們把電荷和弱荷載載在這個二維空間的電荷 , 電荷就是這些粒子在垂直方向下載荷 。
the electromagnetic and weak forces interact with matter according to their hypercharge and weak charge , which make this pattern .	電磁和弱力和弱力會互相作用 , 它會產生這種模式 。
this is called the unified electroweak model , and it was put together back in 1967 .	這叫做 「 非電力模型 」 , 它在1967年就開始了 。
the reason most of us are only familiar with electric charge and not both of these is because of the higgs particle .	我們大部分人都只熟悉電荷 , 而不是這顆粒子 。
the higgs , over here on the left , has a large mass and breaks the symmetry of this electroweak pattern .	左邊的這些希格斯 , 左邊有巨大的質量 , 會破壞對稱的對稱性 。
it makes the weak force very weak by giving the weak particles a large mass .	它會讓弱勢力非常弱 , 使弱力弱弱的弱勢力非常弱弱 , 使弱勢力非常弱弱 。
since this massive higgs sits along the horizontal direction in this diagram , the photons of electromagnetism remain massless and interact with electric charge along the vertical direction in this charge space .	因為這張圖片中 , 光子電磁力很大 , 以電磁力的位置 , 和電磁力相互作用 , 在這個圖表上 , 電磁力仍然不大 。
so the electromagnetic and weak forces are described by this pattern of particle charges in twodimensional space .	所以電磁和弱力被稱為二維空間的電磁和弱力 。
we can include the strong force by spreading out its two charge directions and plotting the charges of the force particles in quarks along these directions .	我們能包含強力的力量 , 將它們的載荷轉換成兩條載荷 , 引導它們的載荷 , 引導它們的引力粒子 。
the charges of all known particles can be plotted in a fourdimensional charge space , and projected down to two dimensions like this so we can see them .	所有知粒子的載荷都可以被放在四維空間中 , 以一個四維空間的載荷 , 這樣我們就可以看見它們 。
whenever particles interact , nature keeps things in a perfect balance along all four of these charge directions .	當粒子互動時 , 自然會維持完美的平衡 , 只要粒子互相作用 , 自然就會維持在完美的平衡上 。
if a particle and an antiparticle collide , it creates a burst of energy and a total charge of zero in all four charge directions .	如果粒子和反粒子碰撞時 , 它會產生能量和一連串的能量 , 它會產生一連串的能量 , 並在四分之一的電荷中產生能量 。
at this point , anything can be created as long as it has the same energy and maintains a total charge of zero .	在這個時點 , 任何東西都能製造出來 , 只要它有同樣的能量 , 並維持了零 。
for example , this weak force particle and its antiparticle can be created in a collision .	比如 , 這種弱勢力粒子和反粒子可以在碰撞中產生 。
in further interactions , the charges must always balance .	在更進一步的互動中 , 載荷一定總是平衡 。
one of the weak particles could decay into an electron and an antineutrino , and these three still add to zero total charge .	其中一個弱粒子可以把電子和肺結合 , 再加上0噸的電 。
nature always keeps a perfect balance .	大自然總是保持完美的平衡 。
so these patterns of charges are not just pretty .	所以這些模式 , 不僅僅是如此 。
they tell us what interactions are allowed to happen .	他們告訴我們 , 互動是如何發生的 。
and we can rotate this charge space in four dimensions to get a better look at the strong interaction , which has this nice hexagonal symmetry .	在四維空間中 , 我們能把這個空間轉換為四個維度 , 讓更好的觀察強度互相作用 , 這使得更好的觀察強度的互動 。
in a strong interaction , a strong force particle , such as this one , interacts with a colored quark , such as this green one , to give a quark with a different color charge this red one .	在一個強大的強力粒子中 , 比如這個綠色 , 一個強大的力量粒子 , 比如這個綠色 , 一個強力粒子 , 像這樣 , 用顏色的電力粒子組成 , 例如這個紅色的圓形 。
and strong interactions are happening millions of times each second in every atom of our bodies , holding the atomic nuclei together .	強烈的互動會發生在我們身體中的每一秒鐘 , 將原子核聚集在一起 。
but these four charges corresponding to three forces are not the end of the story .	但這四個載荷對三種力量並不是故事的結尾 。
we can also include two more charges corresponding to the gravitational force .	我們也能包含兩種引力力的力量 。
when we include these , each matter particle has two different spin charges , spinup and spindown .	我們包括這些 , 每一個粒子都有兩個不同的旋轉、旋轉和旋轉 。
so they all split , and give a nice pattern in sixdimensional charge space .	所以它們都分裂 , 在六維空間中產生一個很好的模式 。
we can rotate this pattern in six dimensions , and see that it's quite pretty .	我們可以把這個模式轉換成六個維度的圖案 , 看到它很漂亮 。
right now , this pattern matches our best current knowledge of how nature is built at the tiny scales of these elementary particles .	現在 , 這個模式將我們目前所知的基礎粒子組成 , 形成了最好的知識 。
this is what we know for certain .	這是我們所知道的 。
some of these particles are at the very limit of what we've been able to reach with experiments .	有些粒子在我們所能觸及的實驗中有極限的實驗 。
from this pattern , we already know the particle physics of these tiny scales . the way the universe works with these tiny scales is very beautiful .	從這個模式中 , 我們已經知道粒子物理是非常美妙的 。 宇宙和這些小規模的粒子相比是非常美麗的 。
but now i'm going to discuss some new and old ideas about things we don't know yet .	但現在我要討論一些新的和古老的想法我們不知道 。
we want to expand this pattern using mathematics alone , and see if we can get our hands on the whole enchilada .	我們想要擴展這個模式 , 使用數學 , 看看我們能否把這個模式使用數學 。
we want to find all the particles and forces that make a complete picture of our universe .	我們想要找到所有粒子和力量 , 使我們宇宙的所有粒子組成 。
and we want to use this picture to predict new particles that we'll see when experiments reach higher energies .	我們想要用這張圖來預測新粒子 , 我們希望用這張圖來預測新粒子 , 來預測新粒子 , 我們希望用這個圖來預測新粒子 。
so there's an old idea in particle physics that this known pattern of charges , which is not very symmetric , could emerge from a more perfect pattern that gets broken similar to how the higgs particle breaks the electroweak pattern to give electromagnetism .	所以 , 在粒子物理學中有一個古老的概念 , 叫做 「 粒子撞擊 」 , 它會產生電磁性 , 不對稱 , 可以從更完美的模式中 , 產生電磁性 , 產生電磁性 。
in order to do this , we need to introduce new forces with new charge directions .	為了做到這一點 , 我們需要引導新方向的新方向 。
when we introduce a new direction , we get to guess what charges the particles have along this direction , and then we can rotate it in with the others .	當我們介紹新方向時 , 我們猜測荷粒子在哪裡移動 , 然後我們就可以和他人一起旋轉它 。
if we guess wisely , we can construct the standard charges in six charge dimensions as a broken symmetry of this more perfect pattern in seven charge dimensions .	如果我們猜想 , 我們能在六個載荷中建立標準載荷 , 以七個載荷的標準載荷 , 產生標準的電荷 。
this particular choice corresponds to a grand unified theory introduced by pati and salam in 1973 .	這個特定的選擇在1973年 , 由巴蒂和薩爾姆在1973年所提出 。
when we look at this new unified pattern , we can see a couple of gaps where particles seem to be missing .	當我們看這個新未識的圖案時 , 我們可以看到一些差距 , 粒子似乎是錯失的 。
this is the way theories of unification work .	這是 「 科學工作 」 的理論 。
a physicist looks for larger , more symmetric patterns that include the established pattern as a subset .	物理學家會看到更大、更複雜的模式 , 包括建立模式來建立模式 。
the larger pattern allows us to predict the existence of particles that have never been seen .	更大的模式讓我們能夠預測出存在粒子從未被見過的存在 。
this unification model predicts the existence of these two new force particles , which should act a lot like the weak force , only weaker .	這個統計模型預測了這兩種新力量的存在 , 它應該像弱勢力一樣 , 只是弱勢力 。
now we can rotate this set of charges in seven dimensions and consider an odd fact about the matter particles: the second and third generations of matter have exactly the same charges in sixdimensional charge space as the first generation .	現在 , 我們可以把這串載荷的載荷轉換成七個維度空間 , 並考慮一個奇怪的事實:第二 , 第三代的載荷 , 在七維空間中 , 和第三代相同的載荷 。
these particles are not uniquely identified by their six charges .	這些粒子並不獨特地被六個載荷所組成 。
they sit on top of one another in the standard charge space .	他們坐在標準的電荷空間中 。
however , if we work in eightdimensional charge space , then we can assign unique new charges to each particle .	然而 , 若我們在八維空間中工作 , 那麼我們可以為每一個粒子創造出獨特的新荷荷 。
then we can spin these in eight dimensions , and see what the whole pattern looks like .	接著 , 我們可以把這八個維度放進去 , 看看整個模式看起來是什麼樣子 。
here we can see the second and third generations of matter now related to the first generation by a symmetry called " triality . "	這裡 , 我們可以看到第二和第三代 , 與第一代相互聯繫的第一代 , 叫做 「 法律 」 。
this particular pattern of charges in eight dimensions is actually part of the most beautiful geometric structure in mathematics .	在八維空間中 , 實際上是數學中最美麗的幾何結構之一 。
it's a pattern of the largest exceptional lie group , e8 .	它是最大規模的圖案 , 八分之一 。
this lie group is a smooth , curved shape with 248 dimensions .	這個謊組是平滑的 , 彎曲的形狀有248維度 。
each point in this pattern corresponds to a symmetry of this very complex and beautiful shape .	在這個圖案中 , 每個點點都對稱這個非常複雜且美麗的形狀 。
one small part of this e8 shape can be used to describe the curved spacetime of einstein's general relativity , explaining gravity .	其中一小部分是用來描述愛因斯坦的 「 重力 」 的一小部分 , 解釋重力 。
together with quantum mechanics , the geometry of this shape could describe everything about how the universe works at the tiniest scales .	用量子力學 , 這形狀的幾何形狀可以描述所有宇宙如何運作在最微小的尺度 。
the pattern of this shape living in eightdimensional charge space is exquisitely beautiful , and it summarizes thousands of possible interactions between these elementary particles , each of which is just a facet of this complicated shape .	這種形狀的形狀在八維空間中 , 每一面都只是一個複雜形狀的形狀 , 它總共有數千個可能的互動 , 包括這些基本粒子的形狀 , 它總結成千上萬種可能的互動 。
as we spin it , we can see many of the other intricate patterns contained in this one .	當我們旋轉時 , 我們可以看到許多其他的複雜模式包含在這個 。
and with a particular rotation , we can look down through this pattern in eight dimensions along a symmetry axis and see all the particles at once .	通過這個圖案 , 我們可以看到這個圖案在八個維度的位置上 , 並且看到所有粒子 。
it's a very beautiful object , and as with any unification , we can see some holes where new particles are required by this pattern .	這是一個非常美麗的物體 , 我們可以看到一些洞 , 新粒子被這個模式所需要 。
there are 20 gaps where new particles should be , two of which have been filled by the patisalam particles .	新粒子有20個落差 , 新粒子有20個落差 , 新粒子被稱為patisalam粒子 。
from their location in this pattern , we know that these new particles should be scalar fields like the higgs particle , but have color charge and interact with the strong force .	在這個圖案中 , 我們知道這些新粒子會像希格斯粒子一樣 , 但有顏色和強力的力量 。
filling in these new particles completes this pattern , giving us the full e8 .	填滿這些新粒子 , 給予我們全部的新粒子 。
this e8 pattern has very deep mathematical roots .	這個e8模式有非常深的數學根源 。
it's considered by many to be the most beautiful structure in mathematics .	它被認為是數學中最美麗的結構之一 。
it's a fantastic prospect that this object of great mathematical beauty could describe the truth of particle interactions at the smallest scales imaginable .	這個偉大的數學美麗可以描述真相對於粒子互動的真相 , 最小的尺度是很棒的 。
and this idea that nature is described by mathematics is not at all new .	大自然所描述的 , 是數學並非全新的 。
in 1623 , galileo wrote this: " nature's grand book , which stands continually open to our gaze , is written in the language of mathematics .	在1623年 , 伽利略寫了這句話: 「 大自然的祖本 , 已經寫出了這個: 「 大自然的原本 , 我們在數學的過程中被寫作 。
its characters are triangles , circles and other geometrical figures , without which it is humanly impossible to understand a single word of it ; without these , one is wandering around in a dark labyrinth . "	它的角色是三角形、圓形、圓形 , 還有其他幾何圖形 , 沒有這些 , 一個人在黑暗的實驗室裡 , 都無法理解一個字 。 」
i believe this to be true , and i've tried to follow galileo's guidance in describing the mathematics of particle physics using only triangles , circles and other geometrical figures .	我相信這是正確的 , 我也試著遵循伽利略的數學粒子物理用只有三角形、圓形和其他幾何圖形 。
of course , when other physicists and i actually work on this stuff , the mathematics can resemble a dark labyrinth .	當然 , 身為物理學家 , 我真的在做這些東西 , 數學可以組成一個黑暗的迷宮 。
but it's reassuring that at the heart of this mathematics is pure , beautiful geometry .	但這數學的心臟是純粹的 , 美麗的幾何 。
joined with quantum mechanics , this mathematics describes our universe as a growing e8 coral , with particles interacting at every location in all possible ways according to a beautiful pattern .	加入了量子力學 , 這個數學形容我們宇宙的形成 , 一個美麗的圖形 , 每一顆星球 , 都可以根據一個美麗的圖形 , 來呈現出一個美麗的模式 。
and as more of the pattern comes into view using new machines like the large hadron collider , we may be able to see whether nature uses this e8 pattern or a different one .	隨著更多的模式 , 使用新的機器 , 像是大型強子撞擊器 , 我們可能可以看見自然是否使用新機器 , 像是大型強大的撞擊器 。
this process of discovery is a wonderful adventure to be involved in .	這個過程發現是一個很棒的冒險旅程 。
if the lhc finds particles that fit this e8 pattern , that will be very , very cool .	如果lhc找到粒子的粒子 , 那會非常非常酷 。
if the lhc finds new particles , but they don't fit this pattern well , that will be very interesting , but bad for this e8 theory .	如果lhc發現新粒子 , 但它們不符合這個模式 , 很有趣 , 但不符合這個模式 , 那會非常有趣 , 但不符合這個模式 。
and , of course , bad for me personally .	當然 , 對我個人來說是很糟糕的 。
now how bad would that be ?	那會是多麼糟糕 ?
well , pretty bad .	嗯 , 很糟 。
but predicting how nature works is a very risky game .	但 , 預測自然的運作方式是非常危險的遊戲 。
this theory and others like it are long shots .	這個理論和其他類似的 , 都是長期拍攝的 。
one does a lot of hard work knowing that most of these ideas probably won't end up being true about nature .	很多努力的工作都知道大部分的思想可能不會終結對自然的影響 。
that's what doing theoretical physics is like: there are a lot of wipeouts .	這就是理論物理學的理論 。 如:有很多線索 。
in this regard , new physics theories are a lot like startup companies .	在這方面 , 新物理理論就像是新物理學理論 , 很多類似新的公司 。
as with any large investment , it can be emotionally difficult to abandon a line of research when it isn't working out .	只要有大量的投資 , 就會很困難 , 不用在工作時 , 會很難拋棄研究 。
but in science , if something isn't working , you have to toss it out and try something else .	但在科學上 , 如果你沒有工作 , 你就得要去嘗試其他東西 。
now , the only way to maintain sanity and achieve happiness in the midst of this uncertainty is to keep balance and perspective in life .	在這個不確定性中 , 唯一的方法就是保持保持平衡和觀點 。
i've tried the best i can to live a balanced life .	我曾嘗試過最好的 , 能活平衡的生活 。
i try to balance my life equally between physics , love and surfing my own three charge directions .	我試著平衡我自己的三個載荷方向 , 和我自己三個載荷的方向 。
this way , even if the physics i work on comes to nothing , i still know i've lived a good life .	順便一提 , 即使我所研究的物理學 , 我仍然知道我已經活過了好的生活 。
and i try to live in beautiful places .	我試著住在美麗的地方 。
for most of the past ten years i've lived on the island of maui , a very beautiful place .	過去十多年來 , 我住在土地 , 一個非常美麗的地方 。
now it's one of the greatest mysteries in the universe to my parents how i managed to survive all that time without engaging in anything resembling fulltime employment .	現在 , 這是我人生中最偉大的謎題之一 , 是我的父母 , 讓我長久以來沒有參與任何全職工作的任務 。
i'm going to let you in on that secret .	我將讓你們進入這個秘密 。
this was a view from my home office on maui .	這是我家在maui的景觀 。
and you may have noticed that these beautiful views are similar , but in slightly different places .	你們可能注意到這些美麗的觀點相似 , 但在不同的地方 。
that's because this used to be my home and office on maui .	這是因為這習慣我家和辦公室 。
i've chosen a very unusual life .	我選擇了一種非常不尋常的生活 。
but not worrying about rent allowed me to spend my time doing what i love .	但不擔心租容讓我花時間做我愛的事 。
living a nomadic existence has been hard at times , but it's allowed me to live in beautiful places and keep a balance in my life that i've been happy with .	生活在美麗的環境裡 , 但它讓我能活在美麗的地方 , 並且保持平衡 , 讓我生活在美麗的地方 , 並且保持平衡在我生活的平衡 。
it allows me to spend a lot of my time hanging out with hyperintelligent coral .	它讓我花了很多時間 , 讓我花很多時間在深深地探索 。
but i also greatly enjoy the company of hyperintelligent people .	但我也很享受那些超聰明人的公司 。
so i'm very happy to have been invited here to ted .	我很高興被邀請到ted

so what's happening is , as the shape is moving over spacetime , it's twisting . and the direction it's twisting as it moves is what particle we see . so it would be ca: the size of the e8 shape , how does that relate to the electron ?	所以 , 發生的狀況是 , 當它的形狀移動到電子時 , 我們會看到的是什麼 , 正如它所移動的 , 它是一粒子 , 我們會看到的 , 直到電子的形狀 , 和電子有多大的關係 。

so the way these things are explained in quantum field theory is , all possibilities are expanding and developing at once .	所以在量子領域理論上 , 所有可能性都擴展並發展出來 。

the legendary chimpanzee researcher jane goodall talks about tacare and her other community projects , which help people in booming african towns live sidebyside with threatened animals .	黑猩猩的研究人員janetcare和其他的社區專案計畫 , 幫助人們在非洲城鎮上居住野生動物 , 和其他的社區專案 。
africa , animals , biodiversity , environment , global issues , pollution , primates , science	非洲、動物、生物多樣性、環境、全球議題、污染、生物多樣性、環境、全球議題、生物多樣性、環境、全球議題、污染、生物多樣性、環境、
jane goodall helps humans and animals live together	珍庫爾幫助人類和動物活在一起 。
good afternoon , good evening , whatever .	午安 , 晚安 , 不好 。
we can go , jambo , guten abend , bonsoir , but we can also ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh .	我們可以去 , oooh , ooh , oooh , oooh , oooh , ooh , oooooh , oooooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , oooooooooooh ,
that is the call that chimpanzees make before they go to sleep in the evening .	那就是黑猩猩在晚上睡覺時會做的事 。
you hear it going from one side of the valley to the other , from one group of nests to the next .	你聽到它從一群巢穴到另一端 , 從一群巢穴到另一邊 。
and i want to pick up with my talk this evening from where zeray left off yesterday .	今天我要跟大家談談這個晚上 , 晚上 , 來自昨天的演講 。
he was talking about this amazing , threeyearold australopithecine child , selam .	他在談的是這個驚奇的三歲小孩 , 伊斯蘭教徒 。
and we've also been hearing about the history , the family tree , of mankind through dna genetic profiling .	我們也聽過了人類的歷史 , 家譜 , 人類 , 來自dna基因遺傳的歷史 。
and it was a paleontologist , the late louis leakey , who actually set me on the path for studying chimpanzees .	這是一位古生物學家 , 羅斯•萊特 , 他在研究黑猩猩的路上 。
and it was pretty extraordinary , way back then .	在那之後 , 很不尋常的 。
it's kind of commonplace now , but his argument was because he'd been searching for the fossilized remains of early humans in africa .	這很普遍 , 但他的論點是 , 因為他一直在尋找非洲人類的早期人類 。
and you can tell an awful lot about what those beings looked like from the fossils , from the shape of the muscle attachments , something about the way they lived from the various artifacts found with them .	你們可以說出很多關於那些從化石從化石上看到的東西 , 來自化石的形狀 , 來自化石的形狀 , 來自化石的形狀 , 來自化石的形狀 。
but what about how they behaved ? that's what he wanted to know .	但他們怎麼做呢 ? 這就是他想要知道的 。
and of course , behavior doesn't fossilize .	當然 , 行為不會化化 。
he argued and it's now a fairly common theory that if we found behavior patterns similar or the same in our closest living relatives , the great apes , and humans today , then maybe those behaviors were present in the apelike , humanlike ancestor some seven million years ago .	他現在認為 , 很常見的理論是 , 如果我們找到行為模式 , 或在我們親近親近親近親戚的祖先 , 很常見的理論 , 如果我們找到行為模式 , 或在我們親近親近親近親戚的人類 , 大約七百萬年前 。
and therefore , perhaps we had brought those characteristics with us from that ancient , ancient past .	因此 , 也許我們從古老、古老、古老、古老、古老、古老、古老、古老 。
well , if you look in textbooks today that deal with human evolution , you very often find people speculating about how early humans may have behaved , based on the behavior of chimpanzees .	嗯 , 如果你看現今的教科書 , 人類演化的行為 , 你通常會發現人類演化的行為 , 根據黑猩猩的行為 。
they are more like us than any other living creature , and we've heard about that during this ted conference .	牠們比其他生物還多 , 我們在ted會議中聽過這個ted會議 。
so it remains for me to comment on the ways in which chimpanzees are so like us , in certain aspects of their behavior .	所以 , 為了我要評論 , 黑猩猩的行為是如此的樣子 , 我們也在某些方面的行為 。
every chimpanzee has his or her own personality .	每個黑猩猩都有自己的個人性 。
of course , i gave them names . they can live to be 60 years or more , although we think most of them probably don't make it to 60 in the wild .	當然 , 我給他們名字 , 他們可以活到60歲 , 儘管我們認為大部分的人可能不會讓它60歲以下 。
mr . wurzel . the female has her first baby when she's 11 or 12 .	史黛絲.威爾 , 當她第一次寶寶的時候 , 母母是1或12歲的 。
thereafter , she has one baby only every five or six years , a long period of childhood dependency when the child is nursing , sleeping with the mother at night , and riding on her back .	此外 , 每五或六年間 , 每五或六年就有一個嬰兒 , 只有每五或六年的時間 , 很長一段時間 , 就是孩子在晚上睡覺 , 媽媽在晚上睡著 , 媽媽在晚上睡著她 。
and we believe that this long period of childhood is important for chimpanzees , just as it is for us , in relation to learning .	我們相信 , 對於黑猩猩來說 , 對於黑猩猩來說 , 這很長期對黑猩猩來說是很重要的 , 因為我們也在學習 。
as the brain becomes ever more complex during evolution in different forms of animals , so we find that learning plays an ever more important role in an individual's life history .	隨著大腦變得更加複雜 , 在不同形式的動物身上 , 我們發現學習扮演在不同的形式動物中扮演重要的角色 。
and young chimpanzees spend a lot of time watching what their elders do .	年輕的黑猩猩花很多時間觀察牠們的生長 。
we know now that they're capable of imitating behaviors that they see .	我們現在知道牠們可以模仿行為的行為 。
and we believe that it's in this way that the different toolusing behaviors that have now been seen in all the different chimpanzee populations studied in africa how these are passed from one generation to the next , through observation , imitation and practice , so that we can describe these toolusing behaviors as primitive culture .	我們相信 , 通過觀察、模仿和練習 , 我們相信 , 這種方式在不同種類的行為中 , 都是從一個世代到下一個世代 , 通過觀察、限制 , 和練習 , 讓我們能夠描述這些行為 , 作為原始文化 。
chimpanzees don't have a spoken language . we've talked about that .	黑猩猩沒有言語 。 我們談過這件事 。
they do have a very rich repertoire of postures and gestures , many of which are similar , or even identical , to ours and formed in the same context . greeting chimpanzees embracing .	牠們有非常豐富的生存和姿勢 , 許多相似之處 , 甚至是相似的 , 甚至在相同的情況下 , 在同一個情況下 , 牠們有著非常豐富的韌性和姿勢 。
they also kiss , hold hands , pat one another on the back .	它們也吻合 , 雙手 , 把手放在背上 。
and they swagger and they throw rocks .	他們會搖滾 , 搖搖搖滾 。
in chimpanzee society , we find many , many examples of compassion , precursors to love and true altruism .	在黑猩猩社會中 , 我們找到許多相同感的例子 , 去愛和真正的利他主義 。
unfortunately , they , like us , have a dark side to their nature .	不幸的是 , 牠們就像我們一樣 , 牠們有黑暗的面向 。
they're capable of extreme brutality , even a kind of primitive war .	牠們是非常殘酷的 , 甚至是一種原始的戰爭 。
and these really aggressive behaviors , for the most part , are directed against individuals of the neighboring social group .	而這些真正的行為 , 大部分的部分 , 都是對鄰居社會群體的行為造成的影響 。
they are very territorially aggressive .	牠們非常非常精彩 。
chimpanzees , i believe , more than any other living creature , have helped us to understand that , after all , there is no sharp line between humans and the rest of the animal kingdom .	黑猩猩 , 我相信 , 比任何其他生物都能幫助我們了解 , 人類和其他動物王國之間就沒有鯊魚 。
it's a very blurry line , and it's getting more blurry all the time as we make even more observations .	這是一個非常模糊的路線 , 隨著我們做更多觀察 , 就會變得越來越模糊 。
the study that i began in 1960 is still continuing to this day .	我從1960年開始的研究 , 一直持續到今天 。
and these chimpanzees , living their complex social lives in the wild , have helped more than anything else to make us realize we are part of , and not separated from , the amazing animals with whom we share the planet .	這些黑猩猩 , 牠們的複雜社群生活在野外 , 讓我們了解到我們是沒有分離的 , 很奇妙的動物 , 和我們共有的動物 。
so it's pretty sad to find that chimpanzees , like so many other creatures around the world , are losing their habitats .	所以 , 要發現黑猩猩 , 就像世界上許多其他生物一樣 , 都會失去棲息地 。
this is just one photograph from the air , and it shows you the forested highlands of gombe .	這張照片是從空氣中拍攝的 , 它展示了森林的高地 。
and it was when i flew over the whole area , about 16 years ago , and realized that outside the park , this forest , which in 1960 had stretched almost unbroken along the eastern shore of lake tanganyika , which is where the tiny , 30squaremile gombe national park lies , that a question came to my mind .	我在1960年的時候 , 發現在公園的東岸 , 當時我在公園之外 , 很不幸地 , 在1960年 , 幾乎被破壞了 , 整個區域 , 大約16年前 , 那時我在東邊的海岸邊 , 發現在公園裡 , 這裡的土地是很大的 , 一個問題來到我腦海裡 。
" how can we even try to save these famous chimpanzees , when the people living around the national park are struggling to survive ? "	「 我們要如何拯救這些著名的黑猩猩 , 當人們住在國家公園裡 , 那些有著生存下來的黑猩猩 ? 」
more people are living there than the land could possibly support .	更多的人住在土地上 , 可能是支持的 。
the numbers increased by refugees pouring in from burundi and over the lake from congo .	數量增加了來自土地的數量增加 , 來自於巴地的數量增加 , 來自土地的數量 。
and very poor people they couldn't afford to buy food from elsewhere .	非常貧窮的人他們也無法負擔得起買食物
this led to a program , which we call tacare .	這導致了一個計畫 , 我們稱之為 「 tacare 」 。
it's a very holistic way of improving the lives of the people living in the villages around the park .	這是一種非常合理的方式 , 可以改善生活在公園裡的人的生活 。
it started small with 12 villages . it's now in 24 .	它從12個村莊開始小 , 現在是24歲 。
there isn't time to go into it , but it's including things like tree nurseries , methods of farming most suitable to this now very degraded , almost desertlike land up in these mountains .	沒有時間去進去 , 但它包含了像樹木護士一樣 , 幾乎沙漠的土地都在這些山脈上 。
ways of controlling , preventing soil erosion .	控制 , 防止土壤消失 。
ways of reclaiming overused farmland , so that within two years they can again be productive .	重建土地的農土地 , 再次是生產力的兩年內 。
working to help the villagers obtain fresh water from wells .	為了幫助村民 , 能協助村民取得水源 。
perhaps build some schoolrooms .	也許建造一些學校 。
most important of all , i believe , is working with small groups of women , providing them with opportunities for microcredit loans .	最重要的是 , 我相信 , 與小群婦女合作 , 提供他們機會 , 給微貸款 。
and we've got , as is the case around the world , about 95 percent of all loans returned .	而我們在全世界的情況下 , 大約95%的貸款都被退休了 。
empowering women , working with education , providing scholarships for girls so they can finish secondary school , in the clear understanding that , all around the world , as women's education improves , family size drops .	賦予婦女教育 , 提供獎學金給女孩們 , 讓女性教育改善 , 家庭大小滴滴 。
we provide information about family planning and about hiv/aids .	我們提供關於家庭計畫和愛滋病的資訊 。
and as a result of this program , something's happening for conservation .	這項計畫的結果 , 是保育的結果 。
what's happening for conservation is that the farmers living in these 24 villages , instead of looking on us as a bunch of white people coming to study a whole bunch of monkeys and by the way , many of the staff are now tanzanian but when we began the tacare program , it was a tanzanian team going into the villages .	保育的農夫是住在這24個村莊裡的農民 , 而不是看著我們當我們開始加入村落時 , 人們會去研究一堆猴子 , 而不是在我們旁邊 , 看著我們 , 成為村落裡的農夫 , 我們現在坦尚尼亞人來研究一群猴子 。
it was a tanzanian team talking to the villagers , asking what they were interested in .	這是坦尚尼亞的團隊和村民們談話 , 問他們對什麼感興趣 。
were they interested in conservation ? absolutely not .	他們對保育感興趣嗎 ? 不是嗎 ?
they were interested in health ; they were interested in education .	他們對健康有興趣 , 他們對教育有興趣 。
and as time went on , and as their situation began to improve , they began to understand ever more about the need for conservation .	隨著時間進步 , 他們開始了解更多關於保育的需求 。
they began to understand that as the upper levels of the hills were denuded of trees , so you've got this terrible soil erosion and mudslides .	他們開始了解到山丘的高度是樹木的高層 , 所以你有了很糟糕的土壤和泥土 。
today , we are developing what we call the greater gombe ecosystem .	現今 , 我們正在開發出我們所謂的 「 更大的生態系統 」 。
this is an area way outside the national park , stretching out into all these very degraded lands .	這是在國家公園的地位 , 把各個國家公園放大 , 延伸到所有這些非常嚴重的土地 。
and as these villages have a better standard of life , they are actually agreeing to put between 10 percent and 20 percent of their land in the highlands aside , so that once again , as the trees grow back , the chimpanzees will have leafy corridors through which they can travel to interact as they must for genetic viability with other remnant groups outside the national park .	隨著這些村落有更好的標準 , 他們真的同意將在公園裡的百分之二十的土地上增加了10%的土地 , 再次 , 當這些村落有更好的標準 , 牠們可以旅行 , 來交互相互作用 , 來交互相互作用 , 以至於牠們在公園裡有更好的棲息地 。
so tacare is a success .	所以tacare是成功 。
we're replicating it in other parts of africa , around other wilderness areas which are faced with extreme population pressure .	我們還在非洲其他地方 , 其他的地區 , 在非洲的其他地方 , 其它的地區 , 受到極端人口壓力的影響 。
the problems in africa , however , as we've been discussing for the whole of these first couple of days of ted , are major problems .	然而 , 在非洲 , 我們一直在討論的 , 是主要的問題 。
there is a great deal of poverty .	這裡有很大的貧窮 。
and when you get large numbers of people living in land that is not that fertile , particularly when you cut down trees , and you leave the soil open to the wind for erosion , as desperate populations cut down more and more trees , so that they can try and grow food for themselves and their families , what's going to happen ? something's got to give .	而當你砍掉樹木時 , 大部分的人都住在土壤裡 , 特別是當你砍掉樹木 , 你就離開土壤 , 開放了樹木 , 所以他們可以試著為自己和家人提供食物 , 特別是你砍掉樹木 , 所以他們可以試著為自己和家人提供食物 。
and the other problems in not only africa , but the rest of the developing world and , indeed , everywhere what are we doing to our planet ?	另外一個問題不僅是非洲 , 而是發展中國家的其他問題 , 還在我們在地球上做什麼 ?
you know , the famous scientist , e . o . wilson said that if every person on this planet attains the standard of living of the average european or american , we need three new planets .	各位知道 , 科學家 , 艾倫•威爾森說 , 如果在這個星球上 , 任何人都在這個星球上 , 我們需要三個新行星 。
today , they are saying four . but we don't have them . we've got one .	今天 , 他們會說四個 。 但我們沒有他們 。 我們有一個 。
and what's happened ? i mean , the question here is , here we are , arguably the most intelligent being that's ever walked planet earth , with this extraordinary brain , capable of the kind of technology that is so well illustrated by these ted conferences , and yet we're destroying the only home we have .	發生了什麼事 ? 我的意思是 , 在這裡 , 我們是 , 世界上最聰明的人 , 被這些ted會議所採取的行動 , 並且我們也被這些ted會議所引發 , 並且我們還不想被這些ted會議員所採取 , 並且我們還在此時被這些ted會議所引發 。
the indigenous people around the world , before they made a major decision , used to sit around and ask themselves , " how does this decision affect our people seven generations ahead ? "	世界各地的原住民 , 在他們做了一個主要的決定之前 , 問自己: 「 這決定如何影響我們七代前代的人 ? 」
today , major decisions and i'm not particularly talking about africa here , but the developed world major decisions involving millions of dollars , and millions of people , are often based on , " how will this affect the next shareholders' meeting ? "	今天 , 主要的決策 , 並不是特別談論非洲 , 而是開發中國家主要的決策 , 包括數百萬人 , 通常是基於: 「 會如何影響下一股股東的會議 ? 」
and these decisions affect africa .	這些決策影響非洲 。
as i began traveling around africa talking about the problems faced by chimpanzees and their vanishing forests , i realized more and more how so many of africa's problems could be laid at the door of previous colonial exploitation .	當我開始旅行非洲各地 , 談到這些問題 , 我了解到許多非洲的問題 , 如我所知 , 許多非洲的問題 , 可能是來自黑猩猩和他們消失的森林 , 我意識到更多 , 很多非洲的問題 , 都可以在非洲的前殖民階層開始旅行 。
so i began traveling outside africa , talking in europe , talking in the united states , going to asia .	所以我開始旅行非洲 , 在歐洲 , 談話 , 在美國 , 去亞洲 。
and everywhere there were these terrible problems .	到處都是這些可怕的問題 。
and you know the kind i'm talking about . i'm talking about pollution .	你們知道我在談的是污染 。
the air that we breathe that often poisons us .	我們呼吸的空氣通常會毒害我們 。
the earth is poisoning our foods .	地球是毒害我們的食物 。
the water water is perhaps one of the most crucial issues that we're going to face in this century and everywhere water is being polluted by agricultural , industrial and household chemicals that still are being sprayed around the world , seemingly with the inability to profit from past experience .	水水水可能是最關鍵的議題之一 , 我們在這個世紀中所看到的 , 包括農業、工業和家庭的化學物質 , 仍然在世界各地都被污染了 , 不論是農業和家庭的化學物質 , 都被污染了 , 來自農業、工業和家庭的化學物質 , 仍然被污染了 。
the mangroves are being cut down ; the effects of things like the tsunami get worse .	紅樹林被砍掉 , 像海嘯的效應變得更糟 。
we've talked about the soil erosion .	我們談過土壤問題 。
we have the reckless burning of fossil fuels along with other greenhouse gasses , so called , leading to climate change .	我們還有其他溫室氣體排放的燃料 , 如同氣候變遷 。
finally , all around the world , people have begun to believe that there is something going on very wrong with our climate .	最後 , 在世界各地 , 大家都開始相信 , 我們的氣候狀況很糟糕 。
all around the world climates are mixed up .	世界各地的氣候都混合起來 。
and it's the poor people who are affected worse .	貧窮的人會變得更糟 。
it's africa that already is affected .	非洲已經受到影響 。
in many parts of subsaharan africa , the droughts are so much worse .	在撒哈拉以南非洲 , 乾旱變得更糟 。
and when the rain does come , it so often leads to flooding and added distress , and the cycle of poverty and hunger and disease .	當雨水降雨時 , 通常會導致洪水和水流、飢餓和疾病的循環 。
and the numbers of people living in an area that the land cannot support , who are too poor to buy food , who can't move away because the whole land is degraded .	居住在一個地區的人口數量 , 居住的地方 , 不是因為整個土地都被降低 , 沒辦法消失 。
and so you get desertification creeping , creeping , creeping as the last of the trees are cut down .	所以你會看到沙漠化 , 停下來 , 最後一棵樹木被砍掉 。
and this kind of thing is not just in africa . it's all over the world .	這種東西不僅僅是非洲 , 而是世界各地 。
so it wasn't surprising to me that as i was traveling around the world i met so many young people who seemed to have lost hope .	所以 , 讓我感到驚訝的是 , 當我在世界各地旅行時 , 我遇到許多年輕人似乎失去希望 。
we seem to have lost wisdom , the wisdom of the indigenous people .	我們似乎失去了智慧 , 原住民的智慧 。
i asked a question . " why ? "	我問了一個問題: 「 為什麼 ? 」

"	這些年輕人 , 當我和他們談話時 , 基本上就是他們對他們說 , 或同情、憤怒 , 和他們說 , 「 我們覺得你已經妥協了 , 不論我們在哪裡 , 或同一件事 , 我們感覺到自己 , 因為我們覺得你已經對抗了我們的未來 , 也沒有我們能做的事 。 」

but basically , we have programs now from preschool right through university , with more and more adults starting their own roots and shoots groups .	但基本上 , 我們有計畫從幼稚園到大學 , 越來越多成人開始自己的根源和槍枝 。
and every group chooses , between them , three different kinds of project to make this a better world , recognizing that all these different problems are interconnected and impinge on each other .	每個團體選擇 , 三個不同的不同問題 , 彼此之間互相連結 , 和彼此之間互相聯繫 。

and woven throughout all of this is a message of learning to live in peace and harmony within ourselves , in our families , in our communities , between nations , between cultures , between religions and between us and the natural world .	所有這一切都是學習的訊息 , 在我們的家庭中 , 在我們的社區 , 在我們的家庭 , 在我們的社區 , 在我們的家庭 , 在我們的社區 , 在我們的家庭 , 在我們的社區中 , 在我們的社區 , 國家 , 文化之間 , 宗教與我們之間之間的關係 。

artist dianna cohen shares some tough truths about plastic pollution in the ocean and in our lives and some thoughts on how to free ourselves from the plastic gyre .	藝術家中的塑膠污染在海洋中 , 和我們的生活中有一些不可思議的事實 , 關於塑膠污染的真相 , 以及我們的生活中 , 有些關於塑膠污染的問題 。
consumerism , global issues , green , mission blue , oceans , plastic	消費主義、全球議題、綠色、藍色、海洋、塑膠 。
dianna cohen: tough truths about plastic pollution	狄安娜•柯林:對塑膠污染的真相 。
i'm a visual artist , and i'm also one of the cofounders of the plastic pollution coalition .	我是個視覺藝術家 , 我也是一種塑膠污染的共同創作者 。
i've been working with plastic bags , which i cut up and sew back together as my primary material for my artwork for the last 20 years .	我一直和塑膠袋一起工作 , 我剪掉和塑膠袋 , 過去二十年來 , 我一直在用塑膠袋 。
i turn them into two and threedimensional pieces and sculptures and installations .	我把它們轉換成二、三維的雕塑和裝置 。
upon working with the plastic , after about the first eight years , some of my work started to fissure and break down into smaller little bits of plastic .	過去八年來 , 我的工作開始分裂成小小的塑膠 。
and i thought , " great .	我心想: 「 很好 。
it's ephemeral just like us . "	像我們一樣 , 像我們一樣 。 」
upon educating myself a little further about plastics , i actually realized this was a bad thing .	更進一步 , 我意識到這是個壞事 。
it's a bad thing that plastic breaks down into smaller little bits , because it's always still plastic .	這是一個壞事 , 塑膠會分裂成更小的部分 , 因為它總是仍然塑膠 。
and what we're finding is that a lot of it is in the marine environment .	我們發現 , 在海洋環境中 , 許多人都在海洋環境中 。
i then , in the last few years , learned about the pacific garbage patch and the gyre .	接著 , 在過去幾年 , 我了解到太平洋垃圾和蓋茲 。
and my initial reaction and i think this is a lot of people's first reaction to learning about it is , " oh my god !	我的第一個反應是 , 我想這是很多人的第一反應 , 就是: 「 我的天啊 !
we've got to go out there and clean this thing up . "	我們必須去那裡和清理乾淨 。 」
so i actually developed a proposal to go out with a cargo ship and two decommissioned fishing trawlers , a crane , a chipping machine and a coldmolding machine .	所以 , 我真的開發了一個提議 , 要用一台車牌 , 一台拖車機 , 一台拖車機 , 一台拖車機 , 一台拖車機 , 一台拖車機 。
and my intention was to go out to the gyre , raise awareness about this issue and begin to pick up the plastic , chip it into little bits and cold mold it into bricks that could potentially be used as building materials in underdeveloped communities .	我的意見是 , 開始拿起塑膠 , 把塑膠切割成磚塊 , 把塑膠切成碎片 , 把塑膠變成磚塊 , 把它變成磚塊 , 可以被用來建造材料在被用來建造材料 。
i began talking with people who actually had been out to the gyre and were studying the plastic problem in the marine environment and upon doing so , i realized actually that cleaning it up would be a very small drop in the bucket relative to how much is being generated every day around the world , and that actually i needed to back up and look at the bigger picture .	我開始和人們談談 , 實際上 , 我在海岸的塑膠上 , 去研究塑膠問題 , 那時 , 我意識到 , 實際上 , 要回去查看更大的圖片 , 比如今日 , 世界各地的塑膠問題都很小 , 這樣 , 我才會發現 , 實際上 , 要回頭看更大的圖片 。
and the bigger picture is: we need to find a way to turn off the faucet .	更大的照片是:我們需要找到一種方法來轉移 。
we need to cut the spigot of singleuse and disposable plastics , which are entering the marine environment every day on a global scale .	我們需要切除單純和可塑膠的塑膠 , 每天都在全球性的塑膠中 。
so in looking at that , i also realized that i was really angry .	所以 , 看看這一點 , 我也發現我很生氣 。
i wasn't just concerned about plastic that you're trying to imagine out in the middle of the pacific ocean of which i have learned there are now 11 gyres , potentially , of plastic in five major oceans in the world .	我並不擔心塑膠 , 可能是塑膠在我所知道的塑膠上 , 可能是塑膠在世界上五個大海洋中 。
it's not just that gyre of plastic that i'm concerned about it's the gyre of plastic in the supermarket .	不僅僅是塑膠的塑膠 , 我很擔心它是塑膠的塑膠 。
i'd go to the supermarket and all of my food is packaged in plastic .	我會去超市 , 所有的食物都包裝在塑膠裡 。
all of my beverages are packaged in plastic , even at the health food market .	我所有的平均都包裝在塑膠裡 , 甚至是健康食物市場 。
i'm also concerned about the plastic in the refrigerator , and i'm concerned about the plastic and the toxins that leach from plastic into us and into our bodies .	我也關注了塑膠和毒素從塑膠和毒素從塑膠變成我們的身體
so i came together with a group of other people who were all looking at this issue , and we created the plastic pollution coalition .	所以我和一群其他的人一起研究這個問題 , 我們創造了塑膠污染聯盟 。
we have many initiatives that we're working on , but some of them are very basic .	我們有許多倡議我們正在努力 , 但有些是非常基本的 。
one is: if 80 to 90 percent of what we're finding in the ocean of the marine debris that we're finding in the ocean is plastic , then why don't we call it what it is .	第一:如果我們在海洋中找到的海洋中有8090%是塑膠 , 那麼為什麼我們不稱它為 「 海洋 」 。
recycling everybody kind of ends their books about being sustainable and greening with the idea of recycling .	回收所有人的書 , 都能持續和綠化 , 回收這一切 。
you put something in a bin and you don't have to think about it again .	你把東西放進一塊麵包裡 , 你就不需要再思考一次 。
what is the reality of that ?	究竟是什麼 ?
in the united states , less than seven percent of our plastics are recycled .	在美國 , 不到7%的塑膠被回收 。
and if you really look into it , particularly when it comes to plastic bottles , most of it is only downcycled , or incinerated , or shipped to china .	如果你真的仔細看 , 特別是當它變成塑膠瓶時 , 大部分只會被丟棄 , 或運送到中國 。
it is downcycled and turned into lesser things , while a glass bottle can be a glass bottle again or can be used again a plastic bottle can never be a plastic bottle again .	它被循環 , 塑膠瓶可以再次再一次塑膠瓶子 , 再一次塑膠瓶也不能再被塑膠瓶蓋了 。
so this is a big issue for us .	這對我們來說是個大問題 。
another thing that we're looking at and asking people to think about is we've added a fourth r onto the front of the " reduce , reuse , recycle , " three r's , and that is refuse .	另一件我們在想的事情 , 就是拒絕 , 請大家想想我們已經把第四個面向前面: 「 減少、回收、回收 」 、 「 減重 」 、 「 回收 」 、 「 回收 」 。
whenever possible , refuse singleuse and disposable plastics .	盡可能地 , 拒絕的塑膠 , 廢棄塑膠 。
alternatives exist ; some of them are very oldschool .	替代方案是很老的 。

phyllis rodriguez and aicha elwafi have a powerful friendship born of unthinkable loss . rodriguez' son was killed in the world trade center attacks on september 11 , 2001 ; elwafi's son zacarias moussaoui was convicted of a role in those attacks and is serving a life sentence . in hoping to find peace , these two moms have come to understand and respect one another .	菲爾波菲•羅德里格茲和安德里茲•羅德里格茲在阿爾瓦菲的國際貿易中心攻擊中被殺死了 , 這兩位媽媽都來找和平 , 愛爾華•羅德里格茲和安德里克斯•羅德里格茲也在世貿易中心攻擊中 , 直到2001年9月11日 , 這兩位媽媽都來找和平 , 和平 , 這兩隻媽媽都來找和平 , 這兩隻媽媽是為了尋找和平 。

and when i saw it and yet , through the shock , the terrible shock , and the terrible explosion in our lives , literally , we were not vengeful .	當我看到它時 , 可怕的爆炸 , 在我們的生活中 , 很糟糕的爆炸 , 很糟糕的爆炸 , 很糟糕的爆炸 , 在我們的生活中 , 很糟糕的爆炸 。

before lifesaver , the best hand filters were only capable of filtering down to about 200 nanometers .	在生活品之前 , 最好的手濾器只能在大約200奈米的水面下降到200奈米 。

so a 200nanometer bacteria is going to get through a 200nanometer hole .	所以 , 一個200奈米的細菌會通過200奈米的細菌 。
the smallest virus , on the other hand , is about 25 nanometers .	最小的病毒 , 另一方面是大約25奈米 。
so that's definitely going to get through those 200 nanometer holes .	所以 , 這絕對是從200奈米的洞中得到的 。
lifesaver pores are 15 nanometers .	生活品質是15奈米 。
so nothing is getting through .	所以 , 一切都沒有發生 。

she picks the water up from there , desalinates it , for free , transports it over there , and dumps it onto the mountains , rivers , and streams .	她從那裡拿起水 , 把水從那裡 , 送到山上、河流、河流 , 及溪流 。

there's a poem written by a very famous english poet at the end of the 19th century .	在十九世紀末 , 詩人寫了一首詩 。

but what housman understood , and you hear it in the symphonies of nielsen too , was that the long , hot , silvan summers of stability of the 19th century were coming to a close , and that we were about to move into one of those terrifying periods of history when power changes .	可是 , 烏托爾斯人也知道 , 嗯 , 嗯 , 在尼爾森的聖經中 , 十九世紀的西班牙人是很長期的 , 很熱的 , 西班牙文字的年輕人 , 很長期 , 熱衷於西班牙文字 , 很久以來 , 熱情 , 來自尼爾森的年輕人 。
and these are always periods , ladies and gentlemen , accompanied by turbulence , and all too often by blood .	各位先生女士 , 女士們先生們 , 全都經常血液 。
and my message for you is that i believe we are condemned , if you like , to live at just one of those moments in history when the gimbals upon which the established order of power is beginning to change and the new look of the world , the new powers that exist in the world , are beginning to take form .	而我的信息是 , 如果你喜歡 , 生活在這個世界的新勢力的新勢力 , 世界的新勢力 , 已經開始形成 。
and these are and we see it very clearly today nearly always highly turbulent times , highly difficult times , and all too often very bloody times .	我們現在看到的 , 通常是非常嚴重的時期 , 通常是非常嚴重的時期 , 通常是非常嚴重的時期 。
by the way , it happens about once every century .	順便一提 , 每世紀都會發生 。
you might argue that the last time it happened and that's what housman felt coming and what churchill felt too was that when power passed from the old nations , the old powers of europe , across the atlantic to the new emerging power of the united states of america the beginning of the american century .	你可能會說 , 過去發生了 , 當權力來自舊的國家 , 歐洲的大西洋 , 美國的新興起力量 , 美國的新新興力 , 在美國的新興起 。
and of course , into the vacuum where the tooold european powers used to be were played the two bloody catastrophes of the last century the one in the first part and the one in the second part: the two great world wars .	當然 , 在那一刻 , 歐洲的權力被用來扮演了兩場大戰場的災難 , 最後一世紀 , 第二部分是兩場大戰 。

but let's talk about the shifts of power that are occurring to the world .	但讓我們來談談改變權力的轉變 。
and what is happening today is , in one sense , frightening because it's never happened before .	今天發生的情況是 , 一個令人害怕的原因 , 因為從來沒有發生過 。
we have seen lateral shifts of power the power of greece passed to rome and the power shifts that occurred during the european civilizations but we are seeing something slightly different .	我們在歐洲文明的權力轉變中看到了一些不同的事情 , 但在歐洲文明中 , 我們看到了一些不同的東西 。
for power is not just moving laterally from nation to nation .	權力不僅僅是來自國內的國家 。
it's also moving vertically .	它也在移動垂直 。
what's happening today is that the power that was encased , held to accountability , held to the rule of law , within the institution of the nation state has now migrated in very large measure onto the global stage .	現今 , 發生的權力是被強迫的權力 , 被監禁的權力 , 被監禁的權力 , 被監禁的權力 , 被監禁 , 國國的權力已經遷移到全球階段 。
the globalization of power we talk about the globalization of markets , but actually it's the globalization of real power .	我們談論全球化的全球化 , 但事實上這是全球化的全球化 。
and where , at the nation state level that power is held to accountability subject to the rule of law , on the international stage it is not .	在國際舞台上 , 國際舞台上 , 權力不足以規定法律的國際階段 。
the international stage and the global stage where power now resides: the power of the internet , the power of the satellite broadcasters , the power of the money changers this vast moneygoround that circulates now 32 times the amount of money necessary for the trade it's supposed to be there to finance the money changers , if you like , the financial speculators that have brought us all to our knees quite recently , the power of the multinational corporations now developing budgets often bigger than mediumsized countries .	國際舞台和國際舞台的權力 , 國際舞台和全球階段 , 現在的權力 , 如今 , 國際舞台和國際舞台的權力 , 大多國際舞台和全球性階段的力量 , 如今 , 國際舞台和國際舞台的權力 , 數量多國際舞台和全球階段的權力 , 實際上 , 國際舞台和全球性階段的力量 , 如今 , 國際舞台和國際舞台的權力 , 大多國際舞台和全球階段的權力 , 實際上 , 國際舞台和全球性階段的力量 , 如今 , 國際舞台和國際舞台的權力 , 將我們所有人的財政部門推廣到我們的膝蓋 , 現在 , 國際舞台和全球階段的力量 , 像是金融的推動器 , 將我們所有人的權力轉換成金錢的力量 。
these live in a global space which is largely unregulated , not subject to the rule of law , and in which people may act free of constraint .	這些生活在一個全球的空間中 , 不規定法律的規律 , 有些人可能會自由限制 。
now that suits the powerful up to a moment .	現在 , 這套裝置能強大到一瞬間 。
it's always suitable for those who have the most power to operate in spaces without constraint , but the lesson of history is that , sooner or later , unregulated space space not subject to the rule of law becomes populated , not just by the things you wanted international trade , the internet , etc . but also by the things you don't want international criminality , international terrorism .	總是為了那些擁有最強權的人 , 不管你想要國際貿易、網路 , 等等 , 不管你不想要國際貿易、網際網路等等 , 還有 , 你不想國際貿易、網際網路等等 , 等等 , 你不想國際貿易、網路等等 。
the revelation of 9/11 is that even if you are the most powerful nation on earth , nevertheless , those who inhabit that space can attack you even in your most iconic of cities one bright september morning .	9/11事件的結果是 , 即使你是地球上最有權力的國家 , 甚至是最有力的國家 , 即使你是地球上最有力的國家 , 即使你是地球上最有力的國家 , 即使你是地球上最有權力的國家 , 即使你是地球上最有力的國家 。
it's said that something like 60 percent of the four million dollars that was taken to fund 9/11 actually passed through the institutions of the twin towers which 9/11 destroyed .	據說 , 9/11事件發生的事件 , 9/11事件被摧毀了 , 9/11摧毀了 。
you see , our enemies also use this space the space of mass travel , the internet , satellite broadcasters to be able to get around their poison , which is about destroying our systems and our ways .	你看 , 我們的敵人也用這個空間 , 網路、衛星廣播 , 甚至可以用這個空間 , 網絡、衛星廣播 , 可以讓他們知道 , 我們的敵人也用這個空間 。
sooner or later , sooner or later , the rule of history is that where power goes governance must follow .	不久之後 , 歷史的規則是 , 權力管理必須遵守 。
and if it is therefore the case , as i believe it is , that one of the phenomenon of our time is the globalization of power , then it follows that one of the challenges of our time is to bring governance to the global space .	如果我相信它是這樣 , 那麼 , 接下來我們所面對的挑戰之一就是全球化的力量 , 同時也就是全球化的力量 。
and i believe that the decades ahead of us now will be to a greater or lesser extent turbulent the more or less we are able to achieve that aim: to bring governance to the global space .	我相信 , 十年前 , 我們將會成為一個更大或更少的人 , 能夠達成目標:要把治理帶到全球太空 。
now notice , i'm not talking about government .	注意到 , 我不是在談論政府 。
i'm not talking about setting up some global democratic institution .	我不是在談論一些全球民主制度
my own view , by the way , ladies and gentlemen , is that this is unlikely to be done by spawning more u . n . institutions .	順道一提 , 各位先生女士們 , 各位先生們 , 女士們先生們 , 女士們先生們 , 這不太可能發生在聯合國機構 。
if we didn't have the u . n . , we'd have to invent it .	如果我們沒有聯合國 , 我們就必須發明它 。
the world needs an international forum .	世界需要一個國際的爭議 。
it needs a means by which you can legitimize international action .	它需要一個意義 , 就是你可以合法化國際行動 。
but when it comes to governance of the global space , my guess is this won't happen through the creation of more u . n . institutions .	但 , 對於全球太空而言 , 我的猜是 , 這不會發生在聯合國和國內機構 。
it will actually happen by the powerful coming together and making treatybased systems , treatybased agreements , to govern that global space .	它會發生在強大的過程中 , 來解決基礎的系統、保護基礎系統、對基礎的協定 , 來解決基礎的系統 , 來解決基礎的系統 。
and if you look , you can see them happening , already beginning to emerge .	如果你看 , 你可以看到它們正在發生 , 已經開始出現了 。
the world trade organization: treatybased organization , entirely treatybased , and yet , powerful enough to hold even the most powerful , the united states , to account if necessary .	世界貿易組織:治療基礎組織 , 完全依據基礎組織 , 但 , 強大足夠強大 , 足以保持最強大的國家 。
kyoto: the beginnings of struggling to create a treatybased organization .	kyoto:開始掙扎創造一個治療的基礎組織 。
the g20: we know now that we have to put together an institution which is capable of bringing governance to that financial space for financial speculation .	g20:現在我們知道 , 我們需要把一個機構轉變成財務空間 , 來資助財務空間 。
and that's what the g20 is , a treatybased institution .	這就是g20的基礎機構 。
now there's a problem there , and we'll come back to it in a minute , which is that if you bring the most powerful together to make the rules in treatybased institutions , to fill that governance space , then what happens to the weak who are left out ?	現在 , 有一個問題 , 那就是 , 如果我們把最強大的力量結合起來 , 把最強大的力量結合起來 , 來填補管理空間 , 那麼 , 會發生什麼事呢 ?
and that's a big problem , and we'll return to it in just a second .	這是個很大的問題 , 我們會再次回到它 。
so there's my first message , that if you are to pass through these turbulent times more or less turbulently , then our success in doing that will in large measure depend on our capacity to bring sensible governance to the global space .	所以 , 我的第一個訊息是 , 如果你通過這些緊急事件 , 或更不穩定 , 我們的成功 , 會在大量的狀態下 , 通過這些動亂 , 或更不穩定 , 我們的成功在大量的依賴我們的能力 , 讓世界各地的安全感應 。
and watch that beginning to happen .	看看那開始發生 。
my second point is , and i know i don't have to talk to an audience like this about such a thing , but power is not just shifting vertically , it's also shifting horizontally .	我的第二個重點是 , 我知道我不需要跟聽眾談談這個議題 , 但權力不僅僅是轉移 , 它也會轉變平面 。
you might argue that the story , the history of civilizations , has been civilizations gathered around seas with the first ones around the mediterranean , the more recent ones in the ascendents of western power around the atlantic .	你可能會說 , 文明的歷史 , 文明的歷史 , 文明的歷史 , 文明的歷史 , 文明的歷史 , 文明的歷史 , 文明的歷史 , 文明的歷史 , 文明在西方國家的歷史上 , 已經被公民化的歷史文明所包圍在海中 。
well it seems to me that we're now seeing a fundamental shift of power , broadly speaking , away from nations gathered around the atlantic [seaboard] to the nations gathered around the pacific rim .	對我來說 , 我們現在看到的是基本的轉變 , 讓國家聚集在太平洋的河岸上 , 遠離國會聚集到太平洋岸邊 。
now that begins with economic power , but that's the way it always begins .	從經濟權力開始 , 但它總是開始 。
you already begin to see the development of foreign policies , the augmentation of military budgets occurring in the other growing powers in the world .	你已經開始看到外國政策的發展 , 軍事預算的發展 , 在世界各地的發展 。
i think actually this is not so much a shift from the west to the east ; something different is happening .	我認為這不是從西方移到東部的轉移 , 有些不同的事情發生了 。
my guess is , for what it's worth , is that the united states will remain the most powerful nation on earth for the next 10 years , 15 , but the context in which she holds her power has now radically altered ; it has radically changed .	我的猜猜是 , 美國將會保持在地球上最強大的國家 , 十五年 , 但它的存在 , 已經徹底改變了 。
we are coming out of 50 years , most unusual years , of history in which we have had a totally monopolar world , in which every compass needle for or against has to be referenced by its position to washington a world bestrode by a single colossus .	我們在五十年內 , 最不尋常的 , 在我們所處的環境中 , 最不尋常的時刻 , 世界各地的氣候變遷 , 都必須被它的基礎設施到華盛頓特區 , 以至於全球最不尋常的歷史 。
but that's not a usual case in history .	但在歷史上 , 這並不常見 。
in fact , what's now emerging is the much more normal case of history .	事實上 , 現在的新興是歷史上最常見的情況 。
you're beginning to see the emergence of a multipolar world .	你開始看到一個多點世界的新興 。
up until now , the united states has been the dominant feature of our world .	直到現在 , 美國已經成為我們世界的主要特徵 。
they will remain the most powerful nation , but they will be the most powerful nation in an increasingly multipolar world .	他們會保持最強大的國家 , 但他們會成為世界上最強大國家的國家 , 同時也是世界上最強大的國家 。
and you begin to see the alternative centers of power building up in china , of course , though my own guess is that china's ascent to greatness is not smooth .	然後你開始看到在中國的替代方案 , 當然 , 我的猜測是中國的平均高度是不平均的 。

you see india , you see brazil .	你可以看到印度 , 巴西 。
you see increasingly that the world now looks actually , for us europeans , much more like europe in the 19th century .	各位可以看到 , 越來越多的歐洲人在十九世紀就在19世紀 。
europe in the 19th century: a great british foreign secretary , lord canning , used to describe it as the " european concert of powers . "	在19世紀 , 一個偉大的英國外國秘密 , 被用來描述它是 「 歐洲的民主國家 」 。
there was a balance , a fivesided balance .	有一個平衡 , 一個平衡 , 五維平衡 。
britain always played to the balance .	英國總是在平衡 。
if paris got together with berlin , britain got together with vienna and rome to provide a counterbalance .	如果巴黎與柏林合作 , 英國和羅馬合作 , 來提供一個不平衡 。
now notice , in a period which is dominated by a monopolar world , you have fixed alliances nato , the warsaw pact .	注意到 , 在這個日子裡 , 由一個單獨的世界 , 你已經修復了伊斯蘭國 , 世界各地 , 你已經修復了伊斯蘭國 。
a fixed polarity of power means fixed alliances .	一個固定的權力的權力意味著修復 。
but a multiple polarity of power means shifting and changing alliances .	但 , 一個多重的權力代表轉變和改變 。
and that's the world we're coming into , in which we will increasingly see that our alliances are not fixed .	這就是我們正在進入的世界 , 我們會越來越明顯地看到我們的盟友並不固定 。
canning , the great british foreign secretary once said , " britain has a common interest , but no common allies . "	英國外國秘密會說: 「 英國外國秘密曾說過: 「 英國外國秘密會說: 「 英國外國秘密會說: 「 英國外國秘密會說: 「 英國外國秘密會說: 「 英國外國秘密

note , that when we went into libya , it was not good enough for the west to do it alone ; we had to bring others in .	注意到 , 當我們進入libya時 , 沒有足夠的資金才能獨自完成 ; 我們必須把其他人帶進去 。
we had to bring , in this case , the arab league in .	我們必須帶出這個案例 , 阿拉伯聯盟 。
my guess is iraq and afghanistan are the last times when the west has tried to do it themselves , and we haven't succeeded .	我的猜是伊拉克和阿富汗是過去一次當西方試圖去做自己 , 我們也沒有成功 。
my guess is that we're reaching the beginning of the end of 400 years i say 400 years because it's the end of the ottoman empire of the hegemony of western power , western institutions and western values .	我的猜測是 , 西方國家的四百年來 , 西方國家的力量、西方力量、西方力量、西方力量、西方力量、西方力量、西方力量、西方力量、西方力量、西方力量、西方力量、西方力量、西方力量、西方力量、西方力量、西方力量、西方力量 。
you know , up until now , if the west got its act together , it could propose and dispose in every corner of the world .	你知道 , 直到現在 , 若西方世界各地的角落 , 都可以提出和分歧 。
but that's no longer true .	但這不再是真正的 。
take the last financial crisis after the second world war .	以最後的金融危機為例 , 第二次世界大戰結束 。
the west got together the bretton woods institution , world bank , international monetary fund the problem solved .	西方世界銀行 , 國際貨幣基金會解決問題 。

let me make a prediction for you , which is probably even more startling .	讓我為各位介紹一個預測 , 這可能更令人振奮 。
i suspect we are now reaching the end of 400 years when western power was enough .	我懷疑我們現在已經到了四百年來 , 西方力量已經夠了 。
people say to me , " the chinese , of course , they'll never get themselves involved in peacemaking , multilateral peacemaking around the world . "	人們對我說: 「 中國人 , 當然 , 他們永遠不會自從世界各地和平在一起 。 」

how many chinese troops are serving under the blue beret , serving under the blue flag , serving under the u . n . command in the world today ?	有多少中國軍隊在藍色背景下 , 保留在藍色的海岸上 , 保護在藍色的海岸 , 在世界各地 ?

of course they are , they are a mercantilist nation .	當然 , 他們是一名非政府主義的國家 。

increasingly , we are going to have to do business with people with whom we do not share values , but with whom , for the moment , we share common interests .	漸漸地 , 我們要和大家合作 , 不是分享共同利益 , 而是與我們分享共同利益的人 。
