today in our modern world , because of the internet , because of the kinds of things people have been talking about here , everything is connected to everything .	現今 , 在現代世界中 , 因為網路 , 因為人們所談到的 , 一切都與一切有關 。
we are now interdependent .	我們現在是獨立的 。
we are now interlocked , as nations , as individuals , in a way which has never been the case before , never been the case before .	我們現在被鎖定為國家 , 身為一個國家 , 身為一個人 , 以前從來沒有這樣做過 , 以前從來沒有這樣做過 。
the interrelationship of nations , well it's always existed .	國家的國際關係 , 一直存在 。
diplomacy is about managing the interrelationship of nations .	外交官是指出國際關係 。
but now we are intimately locked together .	但現在我們很親密地被鎖在一起 。
you get swine flu in mexico , it's a problem for charles de gaulle airport 24 hours later .	你在墨西哥灣流入墨西哥 , 問題是查爾斯在墨西哥航空運動24小時後的原因 。
lehman brothers goes down , the whole lot collapses .	萊哈曼兄弟倒下 , 整個大崩潰 。
there are fires in the steppes of russia , food riots in africa .	在俄羅斯 , 俄國的暴風 , 暴露在非洲 。
we are all now deeply , deeply , deeply interconnected .	我們現在都深深、深深地深深、深深地深深地深深 。
and what that means is the idea of a nation state acting alone , not connected with others , not working with others , is no longer a viable proposition .	這意味著 , 國家的理念是國家獨立的 , 而非與他人合作 , 而非與他人合作 , 而非與其他人合作 , 而非與他人合作 。
because the actions of a nation state are neither confined to itself , nor is it sufficient for the nation state itself to control its own territory , because the effects outside the nation state are now beginning to affect what happens inside them .	因為 , 國內國家的權力不足以控制它自己的領土 , 因為美國國家的影響會發生在國內的情況下 , 還不足以控制它自己的領土 。
i was a young soldier in the last of the small empire wars of britain .	我是一位年輕士兵 , 在英國的年輕士兵 。
at that time , the defense of my country was about one thing and one thing only: how strong was our army , how strong was our air force , how strong was our navy and how strong were our allies .	在那時候 , 我國家的軍隊有多強 , 我們的軍隊有多強 , 我們的軍隊有多強 , 我們的軍隊有多強 , 我們的軍隊有多強 , 我們的軍隊有多強 。
that was when the enemy was outside the walls .	那時敵人是外面的敵人
now the enemy is inside the walls .	敵人在牆壁裡 。
now if i want to talk about the defense of my country , i have to speak to the minister of health because pandemic disease is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of agriculture because food security is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of industry because the fragility of our hitech infrastructure is now a point of attack for our enemies as we see from cyber warfare i have to speak to the minister of home affairs because who has entered my country , who lives in that terraced house in that inner city has a direct effect on what happens in my country as we in london saw in the 7/7 bombings .	現在 , 如果我要談談國內政府的安全性 , 我必須和政府談談 , 因為流行病對我的國家造成嚴重的影響 , 我必須和國內的官員談談 , 因為流行病對我的國家造成嚴重的影響 , 如我們所見到的 , 國內的防衛 , 我必須和國內的官員談談 , 因為流行病對我國家的影響 , 如我們所見 , 來自網路戰爭 , 我得和國務部長談談 , 因為流行病對我國家的影響 , 如我們所見 , 來自網路戰爭 , 我得和國務部長談談 , 因為流行病對我國家的影響 , 如我們所見的 , 在國內 , 我們的公共場所所造成的衝擊 , 已經進入了我的國家 。
it's no longer the case that the security of a country is simply a matter for its soldiers and its ministry of defense .	它不再是美國國家的安全 , 只是為了讓軍人和國防部長的安全 。
it's its capacity to lock together its institutions .	它的能力可以鎖在一起它的制度 。
and this tells you something very important .	這告訴你一件很重要的事 。
it tells you that , in fact , our governments , vertically constructed , constructed on the economic model of the industrial revolution vertical hierarchy , specialization of tasks , command structures have got the wrong structures completely .	它告訴各位 , 實際上 , 我們的政府 , 建立在工業革命的經濟模型上 , 建構在工業革命的經濟模式上 , 建構出了錯誤的結構 。
you in business know that the paradigm structure of our time , ladies and gentlemen , is the network .	你在商業界知道我們時代的典型結構 , 各位先生女士 , 就是網路 。
it's your capacity to network that matters , both within your governments and externally .	你的網絡很重要 , 包括你的政府和外部 。
so here is ashdown's third law .	這是第三條法律 。
by the way , don't ask me about ashdown's first law and second law because i haven't invented those yet ; it always sounds better if there's a third law , doesn't it ?	順道一提 , 如果有第三條法律 , 不要問我之前的第一個法律 , 不是嗎 ?
ashdown's third law is that in the modern age , where everything is connected to everything , the most important thing about what you can do is what you can do with others .	第三條法則是 , 在現代時代 , 所有東西都連結在一起 , 最重要的事情是你能和其他人做的事 。
the most important bit about your structure whether you're a government , whether you're an army regiment , whether you're a business is your docking points , your interconnectors , your capacity to network with others .	最重要的是 , 你的組織 , 不論你是企業 , 不管你是軍隊 , 不論你是企業 , 你的關係 , 你的網絡 , 和其他人的關係 。
you understand that in industry ; governments don't .	你了解在產業中 , 政府沒有 。
but now one final thing .	但 , 最後一件事 。
if it is the case , ladies and gentlemen and it is that we are now locked together in a way that has never been quite the same before , then it's also the case that we share a destiny with each other .	假如各位 , 女士們先生們 , 這也是我們與彼此相同的案件 。
suddenly and for the very first time , collective defense , the thing that has dominated us as the concept of securing our nations , is no longer enough .	突然間 , 在第一次、集體防禦的情況下 , 我們已經把我們視為一個概念 , 來保護我們的國家 , 不再夠 。
it used to be the case that if my tribe was more powerful than their tribe , i was safe ; if my country was more powerful than their country , i was safe ; my alliance , like nato , was more powerful than their alliance , i was safe .	以前 , 我是安全的 , 如果我的國家比他們的國家更強大 , 我安全 , 我是安全的 ; 如果我的國家比他們的國家更強大 , 我安全 , 我是安全的 。
it is no longer the case .	它不再是如此 。
the advent of the interconnectedness and of the weapons of mass destruction means that , increasingly , i share a destiny with my enemy .	相互聯繫和武器大規模毀滅的原因是 , 我與敵人之間的關係 。
when i was a diplomat negotiating the disarmament treaties with the soviet union in geneva in the 1970s , we succeeded because we understood we shared a destiny with them .	當我在1970年代 , 與蘇聯聯邦調查局合作時 , 我們成功了 , 因為我們明白我們和蘇聯聯合國的隔離 , 是因為我們了解我們與他們共享的 。
collective security is not enough .	集體安全並不足夠 。
peace has come to northern ireland because both sides realized that the zerosum game couldn't work .	和平來到北愛爾蘭 , 因為兩邊都知道 , 零和遊戲無法運作 。
they shared a destiny with their enemies .	他們與敵人分享了命運 。
one of the great barriers to peace in the middle east is that both sides , both israel and , i think , the palestinians , do not understand that they share a collective destiny .	在中東地區 , 最棒的障礙和平 , 就是兩邊 , 和平 , 都是以色列 , 我想 , 巴勒斯坦人 , 不了解他們共享集體的命運 。
and so suddenly , ladies and gentlemen , what has been the proposition of visionaries and poets down the ages becomes something we have to take seriously as a matter of public policy .	突然間 , 女士們先生們 , 女士們先生們 , 女士們先生們 , 女士們先生們 , 女士們正是公共政策的主張 。
i started with a poem , i'll end with one .	我從一首詩開始 , 我會結束 。
the great poem of john donne's .	約翰•唐納的一首詩
" send not for whom the bell tolls . "	「 不要把貝殼賣出來 。 」
the poem is called " no man is an island . "	這首詩叫做 " 沒有人是一個島嶼 "
and it goes: " every man's death affected me , for i am involved in mankind , send not to ask for whom the bell tolls , it tolls for thee . "	這句話說: 「 每個人的死亡都會影響我 , 不論是誰 , 都會影響我 , 不論是誰是誰 , 還是要做 。 」
for john donne , a recommendation of morality .	約翰•尼恩 , 是道德的建議 。
for us , i think , part of the equation for our survival .	對我們來說 , 我認為 , 我們生存的一部分 。
to find the path to long life and health , dan buettner and team study the world's " blue zones , " communities whose elders live with vim and vigor to recordsetting age . at tedxtc , he shares the 9 common diet and lifestyle habits that keep them spry past age 100 .	若要找到一條路徑 , 長壽命、健康、丹佛頓和世界的 「 藍色區塊 」 , 他們會一直在tedxttner和團隊研究世界 「 藍色區塊 」 , 他們的生長壽命和健康 , 丹•布萊特和我一起研究世界藍色區塊: 「 藍色區塊 」 社群 , 長壽命和世界的 「 藍色區塊 」 , 共有9個共同飲食和生活方式 , 讓他們在tedxtt中生長壽命 。
biology , culture , exploration , food , health , life , science	生物學、文化、探索、食物、健康、生命 。
dan buettner: how to live to be 100+	丹•布萊特:如何活到100+ 。
something called the danish twin study established that only about 10 percent of how long the average person lives , within certain biological limits , is dictated by our genes .	一個叫做丹伯文字的研究 , 只有大約10%的人生活在某些生物限制中 , 被我們的基因取代了 。
the other 90 percent is dictated by our lifestyle .	另外百分之九十的人都是生活方式
so the premise of blue zones: if we can find the optimal lifestyle of longevity we can come up with a de facto formula for longevity .	所以藍色區塊的最佳生活方式就是:如果我們能找到最佳的壽命 , 就能找到最佳的壽命長壽 。
but if you ask the average american what the optimal formula of longevity is , they probably couldn't tell you .	但如果你問美國人平均壽命的最佳形式 , 他們可能無法告訴你 。
they've probably heard of the south beach diet , or the atkins diet .	他們可能聽過南海灘飲食 , 或是皮膚飲食 。
you have the usda food pyramid .	你有食物金字塔 。
there is what oprah tells us .	歐普拉告訴我們 。
there is what doctor oz tells us .	醫生奧茲告訴我們 。
the fact of the matter is there is a lot of confusion around what really helps us live longer better .	重點是 , 有許多困惑 , 能讓我們活得更好 。
should you be running marathons or doing yoga ?	你應該跑馬拉松或做瑜伽嗎 ?
should you eat organic meats or should you be eating tofu ?	應該吃有機肉 , 或應該吃有機肉嗎 ?
when it comes to supplements , should you be taking them ?	到到供應時 , 應該要拿它們嗎 ?
how about these hormones or resveratrol ?	這些荷爾蒙又如何呢 ?
and does purpose play into it ?	是否有目的的目的 ?
spirituality ? and how about how we socialize ?	精神性嗎 ? 我們如何社會化呢 ?
well , our approach to finding longevity was to team up with national geographic , and the national institute on aging , to find the four demographically confirmed areas that are geographically defined .	我們的方法是與國家地理學院合作 , 找到了四個人口統計的區域 , 來找出四個人口統計 , 來找出四個人口統計的地理位置 。
and then bring a team of experts in there to methodically go through exactly what these people do , to distill down the crosscultural distillation .	接著 , 把一群專家帶到一個專家 , 把他們做的事 , 轉變為人們所做的事 , 將跨越文化的分解 。
and at the end of this i'm going to tell you what that distillation is .	在結束後 , 我要告訴各位 , 這是什麼樣的 。
but first i'd like to debunk some common myths when it comes to longevity .	但首先 , 我想要破壞一些常見的迷思 , 來到長壽之外 。
and the first myth is if you try really hard you can live to be 100 .	第一個迷思是 , 如果你試著真的很難活到100歲 ,
the problem is , only about one out of 5 , 000 people in america live to be 100 .	問題是 , 僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅有5000人美國居住在100個 。
your chances are very low .	你的機會非常低 。
even though it's the fastest growing demographic in america , it's hard to reach 100 .	即使是美國最快的人口統計數字 , 很難達到100分之一 。
the problem is that we're not programmed for longevity .	問題是 , 我們並沒有程式長壽 。
we are programmed for something called procreative success .	我們被稱為 「 成功的案例 」 。
i love that word .	我喜歡這個詞 。
it reminds me of my college days .	它提醒了我大學的日子 。
biologists term procreative success to mean the age where you have children and then another generation , the age when your children have children .	生物學家成功地說: 「 年齡 , 當你的孩子有孩子時 , 你的孩子就有孩子 。
after that the effect of evolution completely dissipates .	經過演化的效果之後 , 演化完全消失了 。
if you're a mammal , if you're a rat or an elephant , or a human , in between , it's the same story .	如果你是哺乳類動物 , 如果你是哺乳類動物 , 或大象 , 或人類 , 相同的故事 。
so to make it to age 100 , you not only have to have had a very good lifestyle , you also have to have won the genetic lottery .	所以 , 要讓它到100歲時 , 你不僅需要有好的生活方式 , 你也必須取得基因學 。
the second myth is , there are treatments that can help slow , reverse , or even stop aging .	第二個迷思是 , 有治療可以幫助緩慢、反轉 , 或甚至停止衰老 。
when you think of it , there is 99 things that can age us .	當你想到它時 , 會有99個可以讓我們做的事 。
deprive your brain of oxygen for just a few minutes , those brain cells die , they never come back .	把你的腦細胞消耗掉了幾分鐘 , 這些腦細胞死亡 , 它們永遠不會回來 。
play tennis too hard , on your knees , ruin your cartilage , the cartilage never comes back .	玩網球很硬 , 你膝蓋上 , 軟骨也無法回來 。
our arteries can clog . our brains can gunk up with plaque , and we can get alzheimer's .	我們的大腦可以發出口號 , 我們的腦袋可以穿上去 , 我們的腦袋可以穿上去 , 我們的腦袋可以穿梭 。
there is just too many things to go wrong .	有太多事情要走錯了 。
our bodies have 35 trillion cells , trillion with a " t . " we're talking national debt numbers here .	我們的身體有35兆個細胞 , 和 「 t 」 , 我們在談論國家債務 。
those cells turn themselves over once every eight years .	這些細胞每八年就開始一次 。
and every time they turn themselves over there is some damage . and that damage builds up .	每當他們把自己丟到某些損害中 , 損害就會破壞 。
and it builds up exponentially .	它建構出了指數 。
it's a little bit like the days when we all had beatles albums or eagles albums and we'd make a copy of that on a cassette tape , and let our friends copy that cassette tape , and pretty soon , with successive generations that tape sounds like garbage .	有點像是垃圾時 , 我們都在唱歌唱片 , 然後讓我們的朋友複製了一套很快的代碼 , 像是garbage的代碼 。
well , the same things happen to our cells .	同樣的事發生在我們的細胞身上 。
that's why a 65yearold person is aging at a rate of about 125 times faster than a 12yearold person .	這就是為什麼一個65歲的人 , 比一個12歲的老人更快 。
so , if there is nothing you can do to slow your aging or stop your aging , what am i doing here ?	所以 , 如果沒有什麼能讓你衰老、停止老化 , 我在做什麼 ?
well , the fact of the matter is the best science tells us that the capacity of the human body , my body , your body , is about 90 years , a little bit more for women .	嗯 , 事實是最好的科學告訴我們 , 人類身體的能力 , 我的身體 , 你的身體 , 大概90年 , 還多一點一點 。
but life expectancy in this country is only 78 .	但在這個國家的預期壽命只有78 。
so somewhere along the line , we're leaving about 12 good years on the table .	所以 , 在這條線上 , 我們留下了12個好年 。
these are years that we could get .	這些年來我們能做到的 。
and research shows that they would be years largely free of chronic disease , heart disease , cancer and diabetes .	研究顯示 , 大部分的慢性疾病、心臟病、癌症和糖尿病患者都差不多 。
we think the best way to get these missing years is to look at the cultures around the world that are actually experiencing them , areas where people are living to age 100 at rates up to 10 times greater than we are , areas where the life expectancy is an extra dozen years , the rate of middle age mortality is a fraction of what it is in this country .	我們認為最好的辦法讓這些失敗的數年來 , 世上最好的方法就是去看看全世界的文化 , 人口數年來的文化 , 比我們所在的地區 , 中年人口的壽命多年 , 中年人口數年的人口數年 , 年齡死亡率高達10倍 。
we found our first blue zone about 125 miles off the coast of italy , on the island of sardinia .	我們找到了第一條藍色區域 , 大約在2005英里的地方 , 在義大利的海岸 , 在義大利的海岸 , 在義大利的海岸 。
and not the entire island , the island is about 1 . 4 million people , but only up in the highlands , an area called the nuoro province .	不是整個島嶼 , 島嶼只有1400萬人 , 但只有在高地上 , 島嶼是約1400萬人 。
and here we have this area where men live the longest , about 10 times more centenarians than we have here in america .	在這裡 , 我們有這個區域 , 住在最長的地區 , 比美國人還多 , 百分之七十 。
and this is a place where people not only reach age 100 , they do so with extraordinary vigor .	這裡的人們不僅僅到達100歲 , 他們也做得很好 。
places where 102 year olds still ride their bike to work , chop wood , and can beat a guy 60 years younger than them .	在那裡 , 有102歲的老年人騎腳踏車去工作 , 樹木 , 可以比他們更年輕 。
their history actually goes back to about the time of christ .	他們的歷史實際上回到了基督教的時代 。
it's actually a bronze age culture that's been isolated .	其實是一片古老的文化 , 被隔離 。
because the land is so infertile , they largely are shepherds , which occasions regular , lowintensity physical activity .	因為土地的土地非常嚴重 , 大部份是牧羊 , 主要是牧羊 , 大量的身體活動 。
their diet is mostly plantbased , accentuated with foods that they can carry into the fields .	他們的飲食主要是以植物為基礎 , 以食物為主題 。
they came up with an unleavened whole wheat bread called carta musica made out of durum wheat , a type of cheese made from grassfed animals so the cheese is high in omega3 fatty acids instead of omega6 fatty acids from cornfed animals , and a type of wine that has three times the level of polyphenols than any known wine in the world .	牠們出去了 , 一個叫做卡塔音樂的麵包 , 由草食動物組成的 , 而一種葡萄酒 , 比世界上任何一種葡萄酒還多 , 比任何知道葡萄酒的種類更高 , 比任何知道葡萄酒的三倍 , 這種葡萄酒有三倍 。
but the real secret i think lies more in the way that they organize their society .	但真正的秘密 , 就是他們組織社會的秘密 。
and one of the most salient elements of the sardinian society is how they treat older people .	薩丁尼亞社會中最嚴重的一部分就是他們如何治療老年人 。
you ever notice here in america , social equity seems to peak at about age 24 ?	你們有注意到 , 在美國 , 社會平等大概是24歲嗎 ?
just look at the advertisements .	看看廣告 。
here in sardinia , the older you get the more equity you have , the more wisdom you're celebrated for .	在薩丁尼亞 , 愈來愈多的智慧 , 你就會得到更多的智慧 。
you go into the bars in sardinia , instead of seeing the sports illustrated swimsuit calendar , you see the centenarian of the month calendar .	你在沙丁尼亞看到一個月曆 , 而不是看到月曆的百分之九點 。
this , as it turns out , is not only good for your aging parents to keep them close to the family it imparts about four to six years of extra life expectancy research shows it's also good for the children of those families , who have lower rates of mortality and lower rates of disease .	事實證明 , 對孩子們來說 , 這不僅是對孩子們的父母 , 他們的壽命比較低 , 比起死亡率和低率疾病的死亡率高達四到六年 。
that's called the grandmother effect .	這叫做祖母效應 。
we found our second blue zone on the other side of the planet , about 800 miles south of tokyo , on the archipelago of okinawa .	我們發現了第二個藍色區塊在地球的另一邊 , 大約800英哩的南方 , 達西亞波 。
okinawa is actually 161 small islands .	okinawa其實是161個小島 。
and in the northern part of the main island , this is ground zero for world longevity .	而在主要島嶼的北部 , 這是地球的二氧化碳 。
this is a place where the oldest living female population is found .	這裡是最古老的居住女性族群 。
it's a place where people have the longest disabilityfree life expectancy in the world .	這是一個地方 , 人們在世界上最長的壽命不足 。
they have what we want .	他們擁有我們想要的 。
they live a long time , and tend to die in their sleep , very quickly , and often , i can tell you , after sex .	他們活了很久 , 很快就會死亡 , 很快地 , 我可以告訴你們 , 在性別之後 。
they live about seven good years longer than the average american .	他們比平均壽命更長 。
five times as many centenarians as we have in america .	美國有五倍 。
one fifth the rate of colon and breast cancer , big killers here in america .	其中一個第五分之一是乳癌 , 美國最大的殺人 。
and one sixth the rate of cardiovascular disease .	心血管疾病的四分之一 。
and the fact that this culture has yielded these numbers suggests strongly they have something to teach us .	這種文化已經有了這些數字建議 , 讓他們可以教導我們 。
what do they do ?	他們會怎麼做 ?
once again , a plantbased diet , full of vegetables with lots of color in them .	再一次 , 植物的飲食含有許多顏色 。
and they eat about eight times as much tofu as americans do .	他們吃了大約八倍 , 像美國人一樣 。
more significant than what they eat is how they eat it .	更重要的是 , 他們吃東西是怎麼吃的 。
they have all kinds of little strategies to keep from overeating , which , as you know , is a big problem here in america .	他們有各式各樣的策略 , 來避免 , 如你所知 , 這是美國最大的問題 。
a few of the strategies we observed: they eat off of smaller plates , so they tend to eat fewer calories at every sitting .	我們觀察的其中一些策略是:他們吃掉較小的盤子 , 所以他們會吃少數的卡路里 。
instead of serving family style , where you can sort of mindlessly eat as you're talking , they serve at the counter , put the food away , and then bring it to the table .	不是服務家庭風格 , 而是把食物帶到桌子上 , 把食物放到桌上 , 然後把食物帶到桌上 。
they also have a 3 , 000yearold adage , which i think is the greatest sort of diet suggestion ever invented .	他們也有三千歲的年齡 , 我認為這是最偉大的飲食建議 。
it was invented by confucius .	它是由於混亂而發明 。
and that diet is known as the hara , hatchi , bu diet .	這個飲食是哈拉、哈拉、哈拉、哈拉、霍亂 。
it's simply a little saying these people say before their meal to remind them to stop eating when their stomach is [80] percent full .	這只是一個小說 , 人們說在他們吃飯時 , 要提醒他們不要吃掉他們的胃 , 只剩下百分之八十的人 。
it takes about a half hour for that full feeling to travel from your belly to your brain .	它花了半小時 , 才能從你的腦袋到你的腦袋 。
and by remembering to stop at 80 percent it helps keep you from doing that very thing .	只要記住停止80% , 就能幫助你繼續做這件事 。
but , like sardinia , okinawa has a few social constructs that we can associate with longevity .	但 , 比如薩丁亞 , okinia , okinawa有一些社會建構 , 讓我們能與長壽的聯繫 。
we know that isolation kills .	我們知道孤立是殺人 。
fifteen years ago , the average american had three good friends .	五年前 , 平均美國有三個好朋友 。
we're down to one and half right now .	我們現在就到達一半 。
if you were lucky enough to be born in okinawa , you were born into a system where you automatically have a half a dozen friends with whom you travel through life .	如果你很幸運 , 生在哈拉瓦 , 你出生在你的生命中 , 你出生在一個系統中 , 你出生在五十多個朋友中 , 你出生在一個系統中 , 你出生在一個系統中 , 你出生在一個系統中 , 你出生在你的人生中 。
they call it a moai . and if you're in a moai you're expected to share the bounty if you encounter luck , and if things go bad , child gets sick , parent dies , you always have somebody who has your back .	他們稱之為moai , 如果你在一個月球上 , 你總是有一些人有你的背後 。
this particular moai , these five ladies have been together for 97 years .	這個特定的莫札 , 這些五位女士已經一起九十七年了 。
their average age is 102 .	他們的平均年齡是102 。
typically in america we've divided our adult life up into two sections .	通常在美國 , 我們把我們的成人分成兩部分 。
there is our work life , where we're productive .	我們的工作生活 , 我們有生產力 。
and then one day , boom , we retire .	有一天 , 我們退休 。
and typically that has meant retiring to the easy chair , or going down to arizona to play golf .	基本上 , 它的意思是要退縮到亞利桑那州的高爾夫球場 。
in the okinawan language there is not even a word for retirement .	在布拉瓦語中 , 沒有一個字可以退休 。
instead there is one word that imbues your entire life , and that word is " ikigai . "	相反地 , 這個字是 「 基加西 」 。
and , roughly translated , it means " the reason for which you wake up in the morning . "	粗糙地翻譯 , 意思是 「 你早上醒來的原因 。 」
for this 102yearold karate master , his ikigai was carrying forth this martial art .	對這個102歲的大師而言 , 他kigaikigaikigaikigaikigaikigaikigaikigaikigaikigaikigaikigaikigaikigaikigaikiga
for this hundredyearold fisherman it was continuing to catch fish for his family three times a week .	對這個百歲的漁民來說 , 牠持續捕魚 , 每週要捕魚三次 。
and this is a question . the national institute on aging actually gave us a questionnaire to give these centenarians .	這是個問題 , 美國國家的研究人員會提出一個問題 , 給了我們一個問卷 , 給予這些百分之九的人 。
and one of the questions , they were very culturally astute , the people who put the questionnaire .	其中一個問題是 , 他們很常常 , 他們是非常文化的 , 人們會問他們 。
one of the questions was , " what is your ikigai ? "	其中一個問題是: 「 你的ikigai是什麼 ? 」
they instantly knew why they woke up in the morning .	他們很早就知道為什麼在早上起床 。
for this 102 year old woman , her ikigai was simply her greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	對於這個102歲的女性 , 她的伊基吉只是她的偉大的祖父 。
two girls separated in age by 101 and a half years .	兩位女孩分離在101年半年 。
and i asked her what it felt like to hold a greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	我問她 , 覺得自己會覺得什麼樣子 , 像是一個曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾祖父的祖父 。
and she put her head back and she said , " it feels like leaping into heaven . "	她把她的頭放回來 , 她說: 「 感覺像是跳進天堂 。 」
i thought that was a wonderful thought .	我覺得那是個很棒的想法 。
my editor at geographic wanted me to find america's blue zone .	我在地理學的編輯要我去找美國的藍色區域 。
and for a while we looked on the prairies of minnesota , where actually there is a very high proportion of centenarians .	一旦我們去看了尼蘇達州 , 那裡有非常高的百分之七十 。
but that's because all the young people left .	但那是因為所有的年輕人 。
so , we turned to the data again .	所以 , 我們把資料再加上了 。
and we found america's longestlived population among the seventhday adventists concentrated in and around loma linda , california .	我們找到美國最長壽的人口之一 , 住在洛瑪琳達加州 , 加州 。
adventists are conservative methodists .	傳統主義者是保守派的 。
they celebrate their sabbath from sunset on friday till sunset on saturday .	他們慶祝他們在星期六日落在星期五日落的日落 。
a " 24hour sanctuary in time , " they call it .	《24小時的監獄》 , 他們稱之為 。
and they follow five little habits that conveys to them extraordinary longevity , comparatively speaking .	他們遵循了五個習慣 , 讓他們很長壽 , 相反的 , 比較談話 。
in america here , life expectancy for the average woman is 80 .	在美國 , 平均女性的預期壽命是80歲 。
but for an adventist woman , their life expectancy is 89 .	但 , 身為一位女性 , 他們的壽命是89歲 。
and the difference is even more pronounced among men , who are expected to live about 11 years longer than their american counterparts .	差異更大 , 比起美國人的預期壽命更長了11年 。
now , this is a study that followed about 70 , 000 people for 30 years .	現在 , 這是一項研究 , 大約有七萬人在三十年內 。
sterling study . and i think it supremely illustrates the premise of this blue zone project .	嚴謹的研究 , 我認為它很明確地說明了這個藍色區塊計畫的前景 。
this is a heterogeneous community .	這是個很大的社區 。
it's white , black , hispanic , asian .	它是白人、黑人、亞洲人 。
the only thing that they have in common are a set of very small lifestyle habits that they follow ritualistically for most of their lives .	他們唯一的共通點是一組非常小的生活習慣 , 讓他們遵循儀式的習慣 , 通常是一組非常小的生活習慣 。
they take their diet directly from the bible .	他們直接從聖經中得到食物 。
genesis: chapter one , verse [29] , where god talks about legumes and seeds , and on one more stanza about green plants , ostensibly missing is meat .	基因學家:章魚 , 上帝說了一些綠色植物 , 三分之二的 , 絕種是肉類 。
they take this sanctuary in time very serious .	他們在時間非常嚴肅地進行這個聖經 。
for 24 hours every week , no matter how busy they are , how stressed out they are at work , where the kids need to be driven , they stop everything and they focus on their god , their social network , and then , hardwired right in the religion , are nature walks .	每週24小時 , 不論他們有多忙 , 他們會停止一切 , 專注於他們的社會網絡 , 然後在宗教上 , 大自然行走 。
and the power of this is not that it's done occasionally , the power is it's done every week for a lifetime .	這種力量的力量是 , 每週都要花一生的時間 , 權力就已經完成了 。
none of it's hard . none of it costs money .	沒有什麼是困難的 , 沒有錢 。
adventists also tend to hang out with other adventists .	阿德維主義者也傾向於其他的抗議者 。
so , if you go to an adventist's party you don't see people swilling jim beam or rolling a joint .	所以 , 如果你去一個阿德派的派對 , 你看不見人們穿著jimbeam或rollingjimbeam 。
instead they're talking about their next nature walk , exchanging recipes , and yes , they pray .	相反地 , 他們說的是他們的下一個自然界線 , 是的 , 是的 , 禱告 。
but they influence each other in profound and measurable ways .	但它們對彼此的影響 , 更加深遠且可測量的方式 。
this is a culture that has yielded ellsworth whareham .	這是一種文化 , 讓ellswhareharehareham 。
ellsworth whareham is 97 years old .	ellswharehareharehareharehareham97歲
he's a multimillionaire , yet when a contractor wanted 6 , 000 dollars to build a privacy fence , he said , " for that kind of money i'll do it myself . "	他是多百萬富翁 , 但當收入者想要6 , 000美元打造隱私權利時 , 他說: 「 這樣我就可以做我自己 。 」
so for the next three days he was out shoveling cement , and hauling poles around .	所以 , 在接下來的三天內 , 他就穿著水泥 , 穿著水泥 。
and predictably , perhaps , on the fourth day he ended up in the operating room .	可預測的是 , 也許 , 在第四天他終止到手術室 。
but not as the guy on the table ; the guy doing openheart surgery .	但不是在桌上的人 , 開心手術的人 。
at 97 he still does 20 openheart surgeries every month .	在97歲時 , 每個月都有20個開頭手術 。
ed rawlings , 103 years old now , an active cowboy , starts his morning with a swim .	老鼠 , 十三歲的老鼠 , 一個游泳的早上游泳 。
and on weekends he likes to put on the boards , throw up rooster tails .	在週末 , 他喜歡把板塊丟下去 , 丟下樓梯 。
her grandson actually lives in the twin cities here .	她的孫子住在雙胞胎城市裡 。
she starts her day with lifting weights .	她從那天起起 , 開始了重量 。
she rides her bicycle .	她騎腳踏車 。
and then she gets in her rootbeer colored 1994 cadillac seville , and tears down the san bernardino freeway , where she still volunteers for seven different organizations .	接著 , 她在聖貝納諾爾•維爾的路上留下了七個不同的組織 , 在那裡她還是志願者為七個不同的組織 。
i've been on 19 hardcore expeditions .	我已經在19個艱難的旅程中 。
i'm probably the only person you'll ever meet who rode his bicycle across the sahara desert without sunscreen .	我可能是唯一你會遇見他騎腳踏車的人 , 坐在沙漠沒有陽光的地方 。
but i'll tell you , there is no adventure more harrowing than riding shotgun with marge deton .	但是我要告訴各位 , 沒有冒險的風險比起火星大樓還沒冒險 。
" a stranger is a friend i haven't met yet ! " she'd say to me .	「 陌生人是個朋友 , 我還沒見過 。 」 她跟我說 。
so , what are the common denominators in these three cultures ?	所以 , 三種文化中的共同點是什麼 ?
what are the things that they all do ?	什麼是他們所做的事 ?
and we managed to boil it down to nine .	然後我們把它放到九點 。
in fact we've done two more blue zone expeditions since this and these common denominators hold true .	事實上 , 我們做了兩項更藍色的區域 , 由這些常見的調節 , 和這些共同的點子保證 。
and the first one , and i'm about to utter a heresy here , none of them exercise , at least the way we think of exercise .	首先 , 我要把這段影片放在這裡 , 不論是誰 , 至少我們認為運動的方式 。
instead , they set up their lives so that they are constantly nudged into physical activity .	相反地 , 他們建立了自己的生命 , 所以他們不斷地成長 , 成為實體活動 。
these 100yearold okinawan women are getting up and down off the ground , they sit on the floor , 30 or 40 times a day .	這些一百歲的女生在地上坐下 , 她們坐在地板上 , 每天三、四十歲 。
sardinians live in vertical houses , up and down the stairs .	薩丁尼亞人住在垂直的房子 , 樓梯上樓梯 。
every trip to the store , or to church or to a friend's house occasions a walk .	每次旅行 , 或教堂或教堂 , 或去教堂 , 或去教堂 , 或去教堂或去教堂 。
they don't have any conveniences .	他們沒有任何方便 。
there is not a button to push to do yard work or house work .	沒有一個按鈕 , 去做房子工作或房子 。
if they want to mix up a cake , they're doing it by hand .	如果他們想要混合蛋糕 , 牠們就會用手做 。
that burns calories just as much as going on the treadmill does .	這種燃燒的卡路里就如同在跑步機上一樣 。
when they do do intentional physical activity , it's the things they enjoy . they tend to walk , the only proven way to stave off cognitive decline , and they all tend to have a garden .	當他們做實體活動時 , 他們會傾向於走路 , 唯一的證明方式是要走路 , 唯一的證明方式是要走路 , 唯一的證明方式是要走路 , 唯一能證明路徑 , 就是他們享受的目標 。 他們往往走路 。
they know how to set up their life in the right way so they have the right outlook .	他們知道如何在正確的狀態下生活 , 所以他們有權利的權利 。
each of these cultures take time to downshift .	每種文化都需要時間轉變 。
the sardinians pray . the seventhday adventists pray .	薩丁尼亞人祈禱 , 七天的禱告 。
the okinawans have this ancestor veneration .	okinawans有這個祖先的祖先 。
but when you're in a hurry or stressed out , that triggers something called the inflammatory response , which is associated with everything from alzheimer's disease to cardiovascular disease .	但當你在心血管疾病時 , 會觸發出一種稱為 「 炎反應 」 的反應 , 和所有來自阿茲海默症相關的疾病有關 。
when you slow down for 15 minutes a day you turn that inflammatory state into a more antiinflammatory state .	當你慢下來十五分鐘 , 就會變成更加抗炎的狀態 。
they have vocabulary for sense of purpose , ikigai , like the okinawans .	他們有用詞彙的意義 , 比如說 , 吉尼亞瓦語 。
you know the two most dangerous years in your life are the year you're born , because of infant mortality , and the year you retire .	你知道你人生中最危險的一年 , 是因為嬰兒死亡率 , 年復一年 。
these people know their sense of purpose , and they activate in their life , that's worth about seven years of extra life expectancy .	這些人知道他們的人生 , 值得約七年的時間 。
there's no longevity diet .	沒有長壽的飲食 。
instead , these people drink a little bit every day , not a hard sell to the american population .	相反地 , 這些人每天都喝了一點 , 不是賣給美國人口 。
they tend to eat a plantbased diet .	他們會吃植物的飲食 。
doesn't mean they don't eat meat , but lots of beans and nuts .	不代表他們不吃肉 , 而是很多豆類和甜甜圈 。
and they have strategies to keep from overeating , little things that nudge them away from the table at the right time .	他們有策略 , 把它們從桌子上移動 , 讓它們從桌子上移動 。
and then the foundation of all this is how they connect .	接下來的基礎是他們如何聯繫 。
they put their families first , take care of their children and their aging parents .	他們把他們的家人拿來 , 照顧孩子和老年人 。
they all tend to belong to a faithbased community , which is worth between four and 14 extra years of life expectancy if you do it four times a month .	他們都屬於一個信仰的社群 , 每個月有四分之二十四次 , 預期壽命 。
and the biggest thing here is they also belong to the right tribe .	最重要的是 , 他們也屬於對部落 。
they were either born into or they proactively surrounded themselves with the right people .	他們不是生生 , 或他們正常被賦予自己 , 和右邊的人一樣 。
we know from the framingham studies , that if your three best friends are obese there is a 50 percent better chance that you'll be overweight .	我們從fm研究中學到 , 如果你三位最好的朋友肥胖 , 假設你的三個最好的朋友都肥胖了 , 那你就會更好 。
so , if you hang out with unhealthy people , that's going to have a measurable impact over time .	所以 , 如果你和不健康的人交談 , 那將會有很大的影響力 。
instead , if your friend's idea of recreation is physical activity , bowling , or playing hockey , biking or gardening , if your friends drink a little , but not too much , and they eat right , and they're engaged , and they're trusting and trustworthy , that is going to have the biggest impact over time .	相反的 , 如果你的朋友喝了一小東西 , 或花園 , 或花園 , 或你的朋友喝酒 , 或花園 , 如果你的朋友喝了一點點 , 但不是太多 , 他們會吃 , 而他們會有很大的影響力 。
diets don't work . no diet in the history of the world has ever worked for more than two percent of the population .	飲食不在歷史上 , 世界各地的人口數量超過百分之二 。
exercise programs usually start in january ; they're usually done by october .	練習常常在一月開始 , 通常是十月 。
when it comes to longevity there is no short term fix in a pill or anything else .	長久以來 , 沒有短期的藥品或其他東西 。
but when you think about it , your friends are longterm adventures , and therefore , perhaps the most significant thing you can do to add more years to your life , and life to your years . thank you very much .	但當你思考一下 , 你的朋友是長期的冒險 , 可能是你人生中最重要的事情 , 幾年來 , 謝謝你 。 謝謝 。
ink that conducts electricity ; a window that turns from clear to opaque at the flip of a switch ; a jelly that makes music . all this stuff exists , and catarina mota says: it's time to play with it . mota leads us on a tour of surprising and cool new materials , and suggests that the way we'll figure out what they're good for is to experiment , tinker and have fun .	要用這東西來製造音樂 , 卡塔里娜•莫塔里娜莫塔里納莫塔說: 「 要做的是 , 去做實驗 , 玩具 , 玩樂 。 一切都存在 。 卡塔里娜•莫塔里娜莫塔里納莫塔里納莫塔里納莫塔里納莫塔里納莫塔里納莫塔里納motarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarina
creativity , design , technology	創造力、設計、科技 。
catarina mota: play with smart materials	catarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarina:
i have a friend in portugal whose grandfather built a vehicle out of a bicycle and a washing machine so he could transport his family .	我有個朋友在葡萄牙的祖父 , 用腳踏車和洗衣機來運送他的家人 。
he did it because he couldn't afford a car , but also because he knew how to build one .	他這麼做是因為他知道如何建造一個 。
there was a time when we understood how things worked and how they were made , so we could build and repair them , or at the very least make informed decisions about what to buy .	有一段時間 , 我們了解事情如何運作 , 以及它們如何運作 , 所以我們可以建造、修復它們 , 或至少能做出改善的決定要買什麼 。
many of these doityourself practices were lost in the second half of the 20th century .	在20世紀 , 許多人工人在20世紀就失去了 。
but now , the maker community and the opensource model are bringing this kind of knowledge about how things work and what they're made of back into our lives , and i believe we need to take them to the next level , to the components things are made of .	但現在 , 創作家族群和開放原始碼模型正在帶領這些知識 , 關於它們如何運作 , 以及它們在我們的生活中如何運作 , 而我相信我們需要把它們帶到下一個層面 , 來到下一個層面 , 要把它們帶到下一個層面 , 來說明它們是如何運作的 。
for the most part , we still know what traditional materials like paper and textiles are made of and how they are produced .	大部分部分 , 我們仍然知道傳統材料像是紙、紡織物 , 以及它們如何生產 。
but now we have these amazing , futuristic composites plastics that change shape , paints that conduct electricity , pigments that change color , fabrics that light up .	但現在我們有了這些令人驚訝的成果 , 製造電力的塑膠 , 顏色的塑膠 , 會改變顏色 , 會改變形狀 , 會改變顏色 , 製造出電力 。
let me show you some examples .	讓我舉個例子 。
so conductive ink allows us to paint circuits instead of using the traditional printed circuit boards or wires .	所以導電路板可以用傳統印刷電路或電路板或電路板 。
in the case of this little example i'm holding , we used it to create a touch sensor that reacts to my skin by turning on this little light .	在這個小小的例子中 , 我們用它來製造一個觸碰感應器 , 用它來製造觸感器 , 用它來製造觸感器 , 用它來製造觸感器 , 用它來製造觸感器 , 用它來製造觸感器 , 用它來製造觸感器 。
conductive ink has been used by artists , but recent developments indicate that we will soon be able to use it in laser printers and pens .	傳統的藝術家最近開發出了它 , 但最近的開發指出 , 我們很快就能夠用在雷射印表機和筆中 。
and this is a sheet of acrylic infused with colorless lightdiffusing particles .	這是一隻腳趾 , 用無色的光芒吸引粒子 。
what this means is that , while regular acrylic only diffuses light around the edges , this one illuminates across the entire surface when i turn on the lights around it .	這代表的是 , 光線穿過整個表面時 , 我會把光照在邊緣 , 只會在邊緣圍繞著它 。
two of the known applications for this material include interior design and multitouch systems .	這種材料包含了內部設計和多觸控系統 。
and thermochromic pigments change color at a given temperature .	紫外線的溫度會改變顏色 。
so i'm going to place this on a hot plate that is set to a temperature only slightly higher than ambient and you can see what happens .	所以 , 我要把這個放在溫度上 , 放在一個溫度上 , 比你能看到的情況更高 。
so one of the principle applications for this material is , amongst other things , in baby bottles , so it indicates when the contents are cool enough to drink .	其中一個原則是 , 在嬰兒瓶中 , 其中一個原則是 , 在嬰兒瓶子裡 , 所以它可以用來喝酒 。
so these are just a few of what are commonly known as smart materials .	這些只是一些常常被稱為智慧型材料的原因 。
in a few years , they will be in many of the objects and technologies we use on a daily basis .	幾年內 , 它們會在許多我們使用的物品和科技上使用的物品和技術 。
we may not yet have the flying cars science fiction promised us , but we can have walls that change color depending on temperature , keyboards that roll up , and windows that become opaque at the flick of a switch .	我們可能還沒有飛行汽車科幻小說 , 但我們可以有牆壁 , 改變顏色的溫度、鍵盤、鍵盤 , 並且窗戶會轉變為光線 。
so i'm a social scientist by training , so why am i here today talking about smart materials ?	所以 , 我是個社會科學家 , 因為我今天要來談智慧材料呢 ?
well first of all , because i am a maker .	首先 , 因為我是個製造家 。
i'm curious about how things work and how they are made , but also because i believe we should have a deeper understanding of the components that make up our world , and right now , we don't know enough about these hightech composites our future will be made of .	我很好奇他們如何運作 , 以及它們如何運作 , 但我也相信我們應該有更深入的了解 , 創造出我們的世界 , 而現在 , 我們並不知道這些高科技的組合物是如何製造出來的 。
smart materials are hard to obtain in small quantities .	智慧材料在小量子裡很難取得 。
there's barely any information available on how to use them , and very little is said about how they are produced .	幾乎沒有任何資訊可以使用它們 , 很少是說他們如何生產 。
so for now , they exist mostly in this realm of trade secrets and patents only universities and corporations have access to .	所以 , 目前 , 大部分都是在貿易秘密和專利 , 只有大學和企業都能取得 。
so a little over three years ago , kirsty boyle and i started a project we called open materials .	三年前 , 我開始了一個專案計畫叫做開放材料
it's a website where we , and anyone else who wants to join us , share experiments , publish information , encourage others to contribute whenever they can , and aggregate resources such as research papers and tutorials by other makers like ourselves .	它是個網站 , 每個人想要加入我們 , 分享實驗 , 發佈資訊 , 鼓勵其他人想要加入我們 , 分享實驗 , 發佈資訊 , 鼓勵其他人想要加入我們 , 分享實驗 , 發佈資訊 , 鼓勵其他人想要加入我們 , 分享實驗 , 發佈資訊 , 鼓勵其他人想要加入我們 , 分享實驗 , 發佈資訊 , 鼓勵其他人想要加入我們 , 分享實驗 , 發佈資訊 , 鼓勵其他人
we would like it to become a large , collectively generated database of doityourself information on smart materials .	我們會把它變成大型集體的資料庫 , 用智慧材料來製造資料庫 。
but why should we care how smart materials work and what they are made of ?	但 , 為什麼我們要關心智慧材料是如何運作的 , 以及它們是怎麼辦到的 ?
first of all , because we can't shape what we don't understand , and what we don't understand and use ends up shaping us .	首先 , 因為我們無法形塑我們不了解的事物 , 以及我們無法形容我們不了解的東西 , 以及我們不了解的東西 。
the objects we use , the clothes we wear , the houses we live in , all have a profound impact on our behavior , health and quality of life .	我們所使用的物品、衣服、衣服、衣服 , 都在我們的行為、健康和生活品質上有很大的影響 。
so if we are to live in a world made of smart materials , we should know and understand them .	所以 , 如果我們要活在一個充滿智慧材料的世界 , 我們應該知道 , 了解它們 。
secondly , and just as important , innovation has always been fueled by tinkerers .	第二 , 更重要的是 , 創新一直都是由tinkerer所造成的 。
so many times , amateurs , not experts , have been the inventors and improvers of things ranging from mountain bikes to semiconductors , personal computers , airplanes .	很多時候 , 演員、個人電腦、飛機 , 都不是專家 , 而是從山腳踏車到半導體、個人電腦、飛機 。
the biggest challenge is that material science is complex and requires expensive equipment .	最大的挑戰是 , 材料科學是複雜且需要昂貴的設備 。
but that's not always the case .	但這並不總是如此 。
two scientists at university of illinois understood this when they published a paper on a simpler method for making conductive ink .	伊利諾州大學的兩位科學家 , 他們發表了一篇論文 , 用一個簡單的方法來製造導電墨水 。
jordan bunker , who had had no experience with chemistry until then , read this paper and reproduced the experiment at his maker space using only offtheshelf substances and tools .	jordanbunker , 他沒有經驗 , 直到那之後 , 閱讀這篇論文和工具 , 讓他做出了實驗 。
he used a toaster oven , and he even made his own vortex mixer , based on a tutorial by another scientist/maker .	他用了一個烤箱 , 甚至製造出自己的創作者 , 由另一位科學家/maker所創造的 。
jordan then published his results online , including all the things he had tried and didn't work , so others could study and reproduce it .	jordan在網路上發表了他的結果 , 包括所有他曾經嘗試過的事 , 沒有工作 , 所以其他人可以研究並繁殖它 。
so jordan's main form of innovation was to take an experiment created in a wellequipped lab at the university and recreate it in a garage in chicago using only cheap materials and tools he made himself .	所以jordan主要的創新方式就是把一個實驗放在芝加哥的一個實驗中 , 在一個實驗中 , 在芝加哥 , 拿一個實驗 , 創造出一個實驗 , 在芝加哥的一個實驗創造出一個實驗 , 在芝加哥的一個實驗創造了一個實驗 , 在芝加哥的一個實驗創造了一個實驗 。
and now that he published this work , others can pick up where he left and devise even simpler processes and improvements .	現在 , 他發表了這個作品 , 其他人可以挑選他出版的作品 , 其他人可以挑選他出版的作品 , 其他人可以挑選他出版的作品 , 其他可以選出他出版的作品 。
another example i'd like to mention her project's goal is to highlight the expressive qualities of materials while focusing on the creativity and skills of the builder .	另一個例子我要提倡她專注於創造力和技能的創造力和技能 。
electronics kits are very powerful in that they teach us how things work , but the constraints inherent in their design influence the way we learn .	電子裝置非常強大 , 教導我們如何運作 , 但它們的設計影響我們學習的方式 。
so hannah's approach , on the other hand , is to formulate a series of techniques for creating unusual objects that free us from predesigned constraints by teaching us about the materials themselves .	漢娜的另一方面 , 就是建立一個系列的技術 , 用來創造出不尋常的物品 , 來讓我們從前來的設計 , 來創造出不尋常的物品 , 來讓我們從前來的設計 , 來創造出不尋常的物品 。
so amongst hannah's many impressive experiments , this is one of my favorites .	在漢娜 , 這是我最喜歡的實驗之一 。
[ " paper speakers " ] what we're seeing here is just a piece of paper with some copper tape on it connected to an mp3 player and a magnet .	[《紙張》 , 我們看到的只是一張紙 , 上面有一塊紙 , 上面有一塊紙 , 上面有一塊紙 , 上面有一塊紙 , 上面有一塊紙 , 上面有一塊紙 , 上面有一塊紙 , 上面有一塊紙 , 上面有一些銅板 ,
so based on the research by marcelo coelho from mit , hannah created a series of paper speakers out of a wide range of materials from simple copper tape to conductive fabric and ink .	所以 , 由於麻省理工學院的研究 , 漢娜創造了一系列的論文 , 用簡單銅製成的材料 , 來製造一系列的紙 , 用簡單的銅板來製造出一系列的紙表 。
just like jordan and so many other makers , hannah published her recipes and allows anyone to copy and reproduce them .	就像約旦和其他作家一樣 , 漢娜出版了她的文章 , 讓任何人能複製並繁殖他們 。
but paper electronics is one of the most promising branches of material science in that it allows us to create cheaper and flexible electronics .	但紙電子是材料科學的其中之一 , 它讓我們能創造更便宜且有彈性電子的東西 。
so hannah's artisanal work , and the fact that she shared her findings , opens the doors to a series of new possibilities that are both aesthetically appealing and innovative .	所以漢娜的工藝作品 , 其實她分享她的發現 , 開放了一系列新的可能性 , 其中的一系列新可能性 , 都是美麗的、創新的 。
so the interesting thing about makers is that we create out of passion and curiosity , and we are not afraid to fail .	所以 , 我們創造出熱情和好奇心的好奇心 , 我們並不害怕失敗 。
we often tackle problems from unconventional angles , and , in the process , end up discovering alternatives or even better ways to do things .	我們常常處理問題從不傳統的角度來看 , 而在過程中 , 最終發現了替代方案或甚至更好的方法來做事情 。
so the more people experiment with materials , the more researchers are willing to share their research , and manufacturers their knowledge , the better chances we have to create technologies that truly serve us all .	所以 , 越來越多的研究人員願意分享他們的研究 , 並製造出自己的知識 , 更好的機會 , 就能創造出科技 , 能讓我們全都能做到 。
so i feel a bit as ted nelson must have when , in the early 1970s , he wrote , " you must understand computers now . "	所以我覺得有點像是tednelson在1970年代早期說的 , 他寫道: 「 你必須了解電腦 。 」
back then , computers were these large mainframes only scientists cared about , and no one dreamed of even having one at home .	那時 , 電腦是這些大型的主人 , 只有科學家在家裡 , 沒有人想過 。
so it's a little strange that i'm standing here and saying , " you must understand smart materials now . "	所以 , 這有點奇怪 , 我站在這裡說: 「 你必須明白智慧材料 。 」
just keep in mind that acquiring preemptive knowledge about emerging technologies is the best way to ensure that we have a say in the making of our future .	請記住 , 先知新興科技是最好的方法 , 來確保我們在未來的新興科技 。
when we drive , we get into a glass bubble , lock the doors and press the accelerator , relying on our eyes to guide us even though we can only see the few cars ahead of and behind us . but what if cars could share data with each other about their position and velocity , and use predictive models to calculate the safest routes for everyone on the road ? jennifer healey imagines a world without accidents .	當我們開車時 , 用預測模式來計算安全道路的安全路線 , 用預測模式來計算安全的路上每個人的安全軌道 。 但如果汽車可以分享資料 , 與它們的位置相互相處 。 但如果汽車可以與我們分享資料 , 用預測模型來計算最安全的路徑 , 讓每個人在路上 , 不是意外 。
jennifer healey: if cars could talk , accidents might be avoidable	jenniferhaley:如果汽車可以說話 , 意外可能是避免的 。
let's face it: driving is dangerous .	咱們來面對它:開車是危險的 。
it's one of the things that we don't like to think about , but the fact that religious icons and good luck charms show up on dashboards around the world betrays the fact that we know this to be true .	我們不喜歡去思考 , 但事實上 , 宗教信仰和好運查理會在世界各地的地板上展示了我們知道的事實 。
car accidents are the leading cause of death in people ages 16 to 19 in the united states leading cause of death and 75 percent of these accidents have nothing to do with drugs or alcohol .	車禍發生在美國導致死亡率的75%而死亡和75%這些意外不適用藥物或酒精
no one can say for sure , but i remember my first accident .	沒有人可以說 , 但我記得我第一次意外 。
i was a young driver out on the highway , and the car in front of me , i saw the brake lights go on .	我是一名年輕駕駛在高速公路上 , 車子在我面前 , 我看到布拉克的燈光 。
i'm like , " okay , all right , this guy is slowing down , i'll slow down too . "	我說: 「 好吧 , 這傢伙慢下來 , 我會慢下來 。 」
i step on the brake .	我踏上腳踏 。
but no , this guy isn't slowing down .	但不 , 這傢伙並沒有慢慢下來 。
this guy is stopping , dead stop , dead stop on the highway .	這傢伙正在停止 , 死停 , 停在高速公路上 。
it was just going 65 to zero ?	僅僅是65到0 ?
i slammed on the brakes .	我在布拉克上打擊 。
i felt the abs kick in , and the car is still going , and it's not going to stop , and i know it's not going to stop , and the air bag deploys , the car is totaled , and fortunately , no one was hurt .	我知道它會停下來 , 車子也不停 , 我知道它不會停下來 , 車子還會停下來 , 汽車也沒人會受傷 。
but i had no idea that car was stopping , and i think we can do a lot better than that .	但我不知道車子停下來了 , 我認為我們可以做得更好 。
i think we can transform the driving experience by letting our cars talk to each other .	我認為我們可以改變駕駛體驗 , 讓車子互相交流 。
i just want you to think a little bit about what the experience of driving is like now .	我只是希望你們稍稍了解駕駛的經驗 。
get into your car . close the door . you're in a glass bubble .	進入你的車 , 關上門 。 你在玻璃泡泡裡 。
you can't really directly sense the world around you .	你不能直接感受到你周圍的世界 。
you're in this extended body .	你在這個延伸的身體裡 。
you're tasked with navigating it down partiallyseen roadways , in and amongst other metal giants , at superhuman speeds .	你的任務是 , 在超human的速度上 , 在超人類的速度上 , 超人類速度是很快的 。
okay ? and all you have to guide you are your two eyes .	好嗎 ? 你需要指導你兩隻眼睛 。
okay , so that's all you have , eyes that weren't really designed for this task , but then people ask you to do things like , you want to make a lane change , what's the first thing they ask you do ?	好 , 所以 , 各位眼睛都沒有設計這個任務 , 但人們會問你做的事 , 你想要做些什麼 , 第一件事情是 , 你想要做些什麼 , 首先要做的事 。
take your eyes off the road . that's right .	把你的眼睛放在路上 , 這是對的 。
stop looking where you're going , turn , check your blind spot , and drive down the road without looking where you're going .	停止看你在哪裡 , 看看你在哪裡 , 看你要走路 , 看看你在哪裡 。
you and everyone else . this is the safe way to drive .	你們和其他人 , 這是安全的方法 。
why do we do this ? because we have to , we have to make a choice , do i look here or do i look here ?	為什麼我們要這樣做 ? 因為我們必須做 , 我們要做這個嗎 ? 因為我們必須做一個選擇 , 來看看這裡 , 看看嗎 ?
and usually we do a fantastic job picking and choosing what we attend to on the road .	通常我們會做很棒的工作 , 選擇我們在路上做些什麼 。
but occasionally we miss something .	但偶爾 , 我們錯過了 。
occasionally we sense something wrong or too late .	偶爾我們會感覺到錯誤或太遲了 。
in countless accidents , the driver says , " i didn't see it coming . "	無數個意外 , 駕駛說: 「 我沒有看到它 。 」
and i believe that . i believe that .	我相信 , 我相信 。
we can only watch so much .	我們只能看得太多 。
but the technology exists now that can help us improve that .	但科技現在可以協助我們改善它 。
in the future , with cars exchanging data with each other , we will be able to see not just three cars ahead and three cars behind , to the right and left , all at the same time , bird's eye view , we will actually be able to see into those cars .	在未來 , 我們將能夠看到這些車子 , 不只三輛車 , 及左邊 , 同時 , 鳥類的眼睛觀看 , 我們將會看到這些車子的前面和左邊 。
we will be able to see the velocity of the car in front of us , to see how fast that guy's going or stopping .	我們能看到在我們面前的車輛 , 看到車輛的速度很快 , 或停止 。
if that guy's going down to zero , i'll know .	如果那個傢伙要走下去0 , 我就會知道 。
and with computation and algorithms and predictive models , we will be able to see the future .	藉由計算、演算法和預測模型 , 我們就能看到未來 。
you may think that's impossible .	你可能會認為這是不可能的 。
how can you predict the future ? that's really hard .	你要如何預測未來 ? 這真的很困難 。
actually , no . with cars , it's not impossible .	其實 , 沒有車子 , 不是不可能的 。
cars are threedimensional objects that have a fixed position and velocity .	汽車是三維空間的物體 , 它有固定的位置 。
they travel down roads .	他們往路走路 。
often they travel on prepublished routes .	通常他們都在旅行的路上 。
it's really not that hard to make reasonable predictions about where a car's going to be in the near future .	對於汽車未來的預測來說 , 很難做出合理預測 。
even if , when you're in your car and some motorcyclist comes bshoom ! 85 miles an hour down , lanesplitting i know you've had this experience that guy didn't " just come out of nowhere . "	即使 , 當你在車上 , 摩托車和摩托車 , 摩托車騎士走了八十五英哩 , 一路走到街上 , 說: 「 剛剛從來沒有 。 」
that guy's been on the road probably for the last half hour .	這傢伙在路上一半小時內就在路上 。
right ? i mean , somebody's seen him .	對吧 ? 我的意思是 , 有人見過他 。
ten , 20 , 30 miles back , someone's seen that guy , and as soon as one car sees that guy and puts him on the map , he's on the map position , velocity , good estimate he'll continue going 85 miles an hour .	10、20、30英哩 , 有人看過這個人 , 他在地圖上 , 很高 , 很快 , 只要一輛車看到那個傢伙 , 他就在地圖上 , 很快就會持續85英哩 。
you'll know , because your car will know , because that other car will have whispered something in his ear , like , " by the way , five minutes , motorcyclist , watch out . "	你會知道 , 因為你的車會知道 , 因為你的車會知道 , 因為那輛車會在他的耳朵中 , 比如說: 「 五分鐘 , 摩托車 , 車車會知道 。 」
you can make reasonable predictions about how cars behave .	你可以做出合理的預測 , 關於汽車的行為 。
i mean , they're newtonian objects .	我的意思是 , 他們是牛頓的物體 。
that's very nice about them .	這對他們來說很棒 。
so how do we get there ?	所以 , 我們該怎麼辦到呢 ?
we can start with something as simple as sharing our position data between cars , just sharing gps .	我們可以從簡單的角度來看 , 只要分享gps , 就分享gps 。
if i have a gps and a camera in my car , i have a pretty precise idea of where i am and how fast i'm going .	如果我有gps和攝影機在我的車裡 , 我有一個很精準的點子 , 我有很精確的點子 , 我有很精確的點子 , 我有很精確的點子 , 我有很精確的點
with computer vision , i can estimate where the cars around me are , sort of , and where they're going .	用電腦視覺 , 我可以估計我周圍的車子 , 或他們會在哪裡 。
and same with the other cars .	和其他汽車一樣 。
they can have a precise idea of where they are , and sort of a vague idea of where the other cars are .	他們可以有一個精確的點子 , 另一輛車子的位置 。
what happens if two cars share that data , if they talk to each other ?	如果兩個車子分享資料 , 如果他們互相交談呢 ?
i can tell you exactly what happens .	我可以告訴你發生了什麼事 。
professor bob wang and his team have done computer simulations of what happens when fuzzy estimates combine , even in light traffic , when cars just share gps data , and we've moved this research out of the computer simulation and into robot test beds that have the actual sensors that are in cars now on these robots: stereo cameras , gps , and the twodimensional laser range finders that are common in backup systems .	教授和他的團隊完成了電腦模擬測驗的結果 , 例如 , 電腦模擬器 , 和他的團隊完成了電腦模擬的結果 , 例如 , 使用電腦模擬器 , 和他的團隊完成電腦模擬的結果 , 例如 , 電腦模擬器 , 和他的團隊完成了電腦模擬 , 甚至在車子上 , 會發生在電腦模擬的情況下 , 例如 , 攝影機、gps , 和電腦模擬器 , 都在電腦模擬中 , 加入機器人測試床上 , 會發生在電腦模擬的情況下 , 例如:鋼琴攝影機、gps和電腦模擬 。
we also attach a discrete shortrange communication radio , and the robots talk to each other .	我們也用了無線電的頻率 , 機器人對彼此說話 。
when these robots come at each other , they track each other's position precisely , and they can avoid each other .	當這些機器人互相交流時 , 牠們會追蹤彼此的位置 , 牠們可以避免彼此 。
we're now adding more and more robots into the mix , and we encountered some problems .	現在我們把更多的機器人加入到混合物中 , 我們遇到了一些問題 。
one of the problems , when you get too much chatter , it's hard to process all the packets , so you have to prioritize , and that's where the predictive model helps you .	其中一個問題是 , 當你太過時 , 很難處理所有的包包 , 所以你必須優先考慮 , 所以你必須優先考慮 。
if your robot cars are all tracking the predicted trajectories , you don't pay as much attention to those packets .	如果你的機器人汽車是追蹤預測軌跡的軌跡 , 你不只注意到這些包裝 。
you prioritize the one guy who seems to be going a little off course .	你優先把這個傢伙看起來有點不錯 。
that guy could be a problem .	這傢伙可能會是個問題 。
and you can predict the new trajectory .	你可以預測新軌道 。
so you don't only know that he's going off course , you know how .	所以你不只知道他是怎麼走的 , 你知道的 。
and you know which drivers you need to alert to get out of the way .	而你知道駕駛你需要什麼駕駛才能避免 。
and we wanted to do how can we best alert everyone ?	我們想做的是如何讓大家成為最好的一員 ?
how can these cars whisper , " you need to get out of the way ? "	這些車子怎麼會說: 「 你需要脫離路嗎 ? 」
well , it depends on two things: one , the ability of the car , and second the ability of the driver .	這取決於兩件事:一個 , 汽車的能力 , 汽車的能力 , 以及第二個駕駛的能力 。
if one guy has a really great car , but they're on their phone or , you know , doing something , they're not probably in the best position to react in an emergency .	如果一個人有很棒的車子 , 但他們在電話 , 或你知道 , 做一些事 , 他們不可能會在最好的位置上做點什麼 。
so we started a separate line of research doing driver state modeling .	所以 , 我們開始了一系列的研究執行模式 。
and now , using a series of three cameras , we can detect if a driver is looking forward , looking away , looking down , on the phone , or having a cup of coffee .	現在 , 使用一系列三台攝影機 , 我們能偵測到如果駕駛員在電話上 , 或喝杯咖啡 。
we can predict the accident and we can predict who , which cars , are in the best position to move out of the way to calculate the safest route for everyone .	我們可以預測意外 , 我們能預測 , 火車是最好的位置 , 可以預測出誰 , 車子是最好的位置 , 可以預測出乎意外的路徑 , 來計算安全的安全路徑 。
fundamentally , these technologies exist today .	基本上 , 這些技術存在今天 。
i think the biggest problem that we face is our own willingness to share our data .	我認為我們所面臨的最大問題是我們自己的願意分享我們的資料 。
i think it's a very disconcerting notion , this idea that our cars will be watching us , talking about us to other cars , that we'll be going down the road in a sea of gossip .	我認為這是一個很讓人沮喪的概念 , 這想法是我們的車子 , 我們會在海裡走路 , 去看我們和其他車子的看法 。
but i believe it can be done in a way that protects our privacy , just like right now , when i look at your car from the outside , i don't really know about you .	但我相信它可以用來保護我們的隱私 , 就像現在 , 當我看著你的車子時 , 我並不知道你 。
if i look at your license plate number , i don't really know who you are .	假如我查看你的裝置數字 , 我並不知道你是誰 。
i believe our cars can talk about us behind our backs .	我相信車子可以在我們的背後說話 。
and i think it's going to be a great thing .	我認為這將會是一件很棒的事 。
i want you to consider for a moment if you really don't want the distracted teenager behind you to know that you're braking , that you're coming to a dead stop .	我想請各位想像一下 , 如果你真的不希望你有一刻的青少年 , 要你知道你是勇敢的 , 你會死去 。
by sharing our data willingly , we can do what's best for everyone .	透過分享我們的數據 , 我們就能為每個人做最好的事 。
so let your car gossip about you .	所以 , 咱們來談談你 。
it's going to make the roads a lot safer .	它會讓道路更安全 。
x prize founder peter diamandis talks about how he helped stephen hawking fulfill his dream of going to space by flying together into the upper atmosphere and experiencing weightlessness at zero g .	xperpeterdiamandis談到他如何幫助史蒂芬•霍金 , 他協助史蒂芬•霍金斯說他如何協助史蒂芬•霍金 , 他協助史蒂芬•霍金 , 讓他能透過飛行 , 將太空飛到大氣中 , 並從中空中跳脫無重力 。
business , flight , science , short talk , space , technology , universe	商業、飛行、科學、短談、空間、科技、宇宙 。

well , the only way to experience zerog on earth is actually with parabolic flight , weightless flight .	嗯 , 地球上唯一一種方式是有著飛行 , 不用飛行、無重的飛行 。
you take an airplane , you fly over the top , you're weightless for 25 seconds .	你拿飛機 , 飛到頂端 , 你飛過25秒 。
come back down , you weigh twice as much .	回到下面 , 你重量兩倍 。

medical animator david bolinsky presents 3 minutes of stunning animation that show the bustling life inside a cell .	醫學家davidbolinsky表演了3分鐘的動畫 , 顯示在一個細胞內的生命 。

david bolinsky animates a cell	大衛•波林斯基y動畫了細胞 。
i'm a medical illustrator , and i come from a slightly different point of view .	我是醫學插畫家 , 我來自一個不同的觀點 。
i've been watching , since i grew up , the expressions of truth and beauty in the arts and truth and beauty in the sciences .	從我長大後 , 我一直在看 , 從我成長過程中 , 真美和美麗在科學中 , 真相和美麗 。
and while these are both wonderful things in their own right they both have very wonderful things going for them truth and beauty as ideals that can be looked at by the sciences and by math are almost like the ideal conjoined twins that a scientist would want to date .	雖然這些都是很美好的事物 , 因為科學和數學是很美好的 , 因為科學和數學幾乎像理想的青少年 , 科學家會想要約會約會 。

they are unique . they are useful sometimes , often a long time after the fact .	他們是獨特的 , 有時通常是很長的時間 。
and you can actually roll some of the pictures now , because i don't want to look at me on the screen .	你們現在可以從螢幕上看 , 因為我不想在螢幕上看我 。
truth and beauty are things that are often opaque to people who are not in the sciences .	真相和美麗是常常被忽略在科學中的人 。
they are things that describe beauty in a way that is often only accessible if you understand the language and the syntax of the person who studies the subject in which truth and beauty is expressed .	他們是用這種方式來描述美麗的事物 , 只要你了解語言和美感 , 就會被表達出來 。
if you look at the math , e=mc squared , if you look at the cosmological constant , where there's an anthropic ideal , where you see that life had to evolve from the numbers that describe the universe these are things that are really difficult to understand .	如果你看看數學 , 宇宙的原則 , 你可以看到生命必須從數字描述宇宙的角度來看 , 宇宙中有一種永恆的現象 , 你可以看到生命從數字描述到宇宙中 , 都是非常困難的 。
and what i've tried to do since i had my training as a medical illustrator since i was taught animation by my father , who was a sculptor and my visual mentor i wanted to figure out a way to help people understand truth and beauty in the biological sciences by using animation , by using pictures , by telling stories so that the things that are not necessarily evident to people can be brought forth , and can be taught , and can be understood .	自從我被教導時 , 我的視覺指導師 , 我想要找出一種方法來幫助人們了解真相和美麗 , 透過使用影像 , 透過使用影像 , 透過使用影像 , 透過使用圖像 , 透過使用圖像 , 來協助人們了解真相和美麗 , 透過使用圖像 , 透過使用圖像 , 來協助人們了解真相和美麗 , 透過使用圖像 , 來協助人們了解真相和美麗 , 透過使用圖像 , 以至於我可以被教導 , 透過動畫來幫助大家了解真相和美麗 。
students today are often immersed in an environment where what they learn is subjects that have truth and beauty embedded in them , but the way they're taught is compartmentalized and it's drawn down to the point where the truth and beauty are not always evident .	現今 , 學生們通常會在環境中學習 , 他們被教學的主題是有真相和美的 , 並不是總是證據的 。

and figure out how to do this in a way that was truthful in that it imparted what was going on , but not so truthful that the compact crowding in a cell would prevent the vista from happening .	要找出如何做到這一點 , 很明確地說 , 在這個情況下 , 會預防病毒發生的狀況 。
and so what i'm going to show you is a threeminute reader's digest version of the first aspect of this film that we produced . it's an ongoing project that's going to go another four or five years .	接下來我要給你們看的是我們製作的第一面鏡片 , 它是一個持續發展的四、五年 。
and i want you to look at this and see the paths that the cell manufactures these little walking machines , they're called kinesins that take these huge loads that would challenge an ant in relative size .	我希望你們看看這個 , 看到這些巨大的路徑 , 把這些巨大的道路帶到這些巨大的道路上 , 將這些巨大的路徑放進機器中 , 他們稱之為 「 kinesins 」 , 用這些巨大的路徑來處理這些巨大的路徑 。
run the movie , please .	拍電影 , 拜託 。
but these machines that power the inside of the cells are really quite amazing , and they really are the basis of all life because all of these machines interact with each other .	但這些機器在細胞內運作的能力是很棒的 , 它們其實是生命的基礎 , 因為所有這些機器都互相互相作用 。
they pass information to each other .	他們互相傳遞訊息 。
they cause different things to happen inside the cell .	它們會造成不同的事情發生在細胞內 。
and the cell will actually manufacture the parts that it needs on the fly , from information that's brought from the nucleus by molecules that read the genes .	細胞會製造出一部分 , 來自核子的分子 , 來自核子的資訊 , 由分子閱讀基因 。
no life , from the smallest life to everybody here , would be possible without these little micromachines .	沒有這些小小的生命 , 從最小的生命到每個人 , 都可能沒有這些小小的生命 。
in fact , it would really , in the absence of these machines , have made the attendance here , chris , really quite sparse .	事實上 , 在這些機器中 , 克里斯 , 真的很不可思議 。
this is the fedex delivery guy of the cell .	這是細胞的fedext細胞 。
this little guy is called the kinesin , and he pulls a sack that's full of brand new manufactured proteins to wherever it's needed in the cell whether it's to a membrane , whether it's to an organelle , whether it's to build something or repair something .	這個小傢伙叫做 " kinesin " , 他推出了一堆新的製造蛋白質 , 包含所有品牌新的製造蛋白質 , 不管是用來建造物體或修復東西 。
and each of us has about 100 , 000 of these things running around , right now , inside each one of your 100 trillion cells .	我們每個人大約有十萬個這些東西正在運作 , 現在 , 在你的一百兆個細胞中 。
so no matter how lazy you feel , you're not really intrinsically doing nothing .	所以不論你有多瘋狂 , 不管你有多瘋狂 , 你根本沒有做任何事 。
so what i want you to do when you go home is think about this , and think about how powerful our cells are .	所以 , 當我回到家時 , 思考一下 , 我們的大腦有多強大 。
and think about some of the things that we're learning about cellular mechanics .	想想看一些我們在學習細胞機械的方法 。
once we figure out all that's going on and believe me , we know almost a percent of what's going on once we figure out what's going on , we're really going to be able to have a lot of control over what we do with our health , with what we do with future generations , and how long we're going to live .	一旦我們意識到 , 我們將會有辦法控制我們所做的事和未來的世代 , 和未來的世代 , 和未來的世代 , 和未來一代 , 我們將會有多長的壽命 。
and hopefully we'll be able to use this to discover more truth , and more beauty .	希望我們能用這個發現更多的真相 , 更美好 。
but it's really quite amazing that these cells , these micromachines , are aware enough of what the cell needs that they do their bidding .	但真的很令人驚訝 , 這些細胞 , 這些細胞 , 這些細胞 , 需要這些細胞 , 這些細胞需要他們做些什麼 。
they work together . they make the cell do what it needs to do .	他們一起工作 , 他們一起工作 , 讓細胞做得做的事 。
and their working together helps our bodies huge entities that they will never see function properly .	他們一起合作 , 協助我們身體巨大的特質 , 來協助他們從來沒有見過功能 。
enjoy the rest of the show . thank you .	享受剩餘的節目 。 謝謝 。
becky blanton planned to live in her van for a year and see the country , but when depression set in and her freelance job ended , her camping trip turned into homelessness . in this intimate talk , she describes her experience of becoming one of america's working homeless .	貝琪•布蘭頓計劃在她的旅遊中去年 , 但當憂鬱症和她的婚姻在她的旅程結束時 , 她的經歷變成了美國無家可歸的年輕人 , 她的經歷變成了無家可歸 。
adventure , happiness , life , personal growth , poverty , social change , society , storytelling	冒險、快樂、人生、個人成長、貧窮、社會變革、社會改變、社會、故事 。
becky blanton: the year i was homeless	貝琪.布蘭頓:我無家可歸 。
i'm a writer and a journalist , and i'm also an insanely curious person , so in 22 years as a journalist , i've learned how to do a lot of new things .	我是個作家和記者 , 我知道如何做很多新的事物 。
and three years ago , one of the things i learned how to do was to become invisible .	三年前 , 我學到了一件事 , 就是要成為隱形 。
i became one of the working homeless .	我變成了無家可歸的人 。
i quit my job as a newspaper editor after my father died in february of that same year , and decided to travel .	我辭職了一年 , 決定要旅行 , 決定要旅行 。
his death hit me pretty hard .	他的死亡非常困難 。
and there were a lot of things that i wanted to feel and deal with while i was doing that .	我在做這些事時 , 有許多東西我想要感覺和處理 。
i've camped my whole life . and i decided that living in a van for a year to do this would be like one long camping trip .	我把整個人生都放進去 , 我決定住在一個旅行的旅行中 , 決定住在一個旅行的旅行中 。
so i packed my cat , my rottweiler and my camping gear into a 1975 chevy van , and drove off into the sunset , having fully failed to realize three critical things .	所以我打開了我的貓 , 我的輪椅 , 開了車 , 開了車子 , 開了車 , 開了1975年的車子 , 開了車 , 完全失敗了 , 發現了三個關鍵物件 。
one: that society equates living in a permanent structure , even a shack , with having value as a person .	第一:社會平均生活在永久的結構中 , 甚至是一堆 , 一個人的價值 。
two: i failed to realize how quickly the negative perceptions of other people can impact our reality , if we let it .	第二:我失敗了 , 了解到他人的負面感知如何影響我們的現實 , 如果我們讓他人能影響我們的現實 。
three: i failed to realize that homelessness is an attitude , not a lifestyle .	第三:我失敗了 , 發現無家可歸是態度 , 而不是生活方式 。
at first , living in the van was great .	第一 , 生活在火車上是很棒的 。
i showered in campgrounds . i ate out regularly .	我在校園裡開車 , 我很常常 。
and i had time to relax and to grieve .	我有時間放鬆和悲慟 。
but then the anger and the depression about my father's death set in .	但 , 憤怒和憂鬱 , 是我父親的死亡 。
my freelance job ended . and i had to get a fulltime job to pay the bills .	我的自由工作終止了 。 我必須得到一份全職的工作 , 來支付帳單 。
what had been a really mild spring turned into a miserably hot summer .	當時 , 一個非常熱的夏天會變成一個非常熱的夏天 。
and it became impossible to park anywhere without being very obvious that i had a cat and a dog with me , and it was really hot .	到公園裡 , 沒有很明顯的 , 我和一隻貓狗跟我一樣 , 那真是熱 。
the cat came and went through an open window in the van .	貓帶走了一座開窗的窗戶 。
the doggy went into doggy day care .	狗狗走進了白天照護 。
whenever i could , i used employee showers in office buildings and truck stops .	每當我在辦公室大樓和卡車停車時 , 卡車就會停下來 。
or i washed up in public rest rooms .	或者我在公共場合的房間 。
nighttime temperatures in the van rarely dropped below 80 degrees fahrenheit , making it difficult or impossible to sleep .	夜晚的溫度是華氏80度的溫度 , 讓它很難或無法睡覺 。
food rotted in the heat .	食物在熱中腐化 。
ice in my ice chest melted within hours , and it was pretty miserable .	我冰層的冰層上升了幾小時 , 看起來很悲慘 。
i couldn't afford to find an apartment , or couldn't afford an apartment that would allow me to have the rottweiler and the cat .	我無法負擔得起一個公寓 , 不能負擔得起公寓 , 不能負擔得起一個公寓 , 不然我可以讓我看到公寓 , 或不能負擔得起公寓 。
and i refused to give them up , so i stayed in the van .	我拒絕放棄他們 , 所以我留在火車上 。
and when the heat made me too sick to walk the 50 feet to the public restroom outside my van at night , i used a bucket and a trash bag as a toilet .	當熱讓我太生病時 , 我用了一桶垃圾袋 , 一桶燃料 , 用一桶垃圾桶 , 用一桶垃圾袋 。
when winter weather set in , the temperatures dropped below freezing . and they stayed there .	當冬天天氣下降 , 溫度下降下降 , 溫度下降了 , 溫度下降了 。
and i faced a whole new set of challenges .	我面對了一個全新的挑戰 。
i parked a different place every night so i would avoid being noticed and hassled by the police .	我每天晚上都會停下來 , 我會避免注意到 , 被警察攔截 。
i didn't always succeed .	我並不總是成功 。
but i felt out of control of my life .	但我感覺到我人生的控制 。
and i don't know when or how it happened , but the speed at which i went from being a talented writer and journalist to being a homeless woman , living in a van , took my breath away .	我不知道它怎麼發生 , 但是我從一個很有名的作家和記者變成一個無家可歸的年輕人 , 身為一個無家可歸的女人 , 生活在我的呼吸中 。
i hadn't changed . my i . q . hadn't dropped .	我沒有改變 。 我的智商 , 沒有改變 。
my talent , my integrity , my values , everything about me remained the same .	我的天賦、我的價值觀、我的價值觀 , 和我的價值 , 完全不一樣 。
but i had changed somehow .	但我已經改變了 。
i spiraled deeper and deeper into a depression .	我更深入憂鬱 。
and eventually someone referred me to a homeless health clinic .	最後有人把我送到一個無家可歸的健康診所 。
and i went . i hadn't bathed in three days .	我去了 。 我在三天內就沒有洗澡了 。
i was as smelly and as depressed as anyone in line .	我跟任何人一樣 , 憂鬱了 。
i just wasn't drunk or high .	我只是沒有喝醉或高興 。
and when several of the homeless men realized that , including a former university professor , they said , " you aren't homeless . why are you really here ? "	當幾位無家可歸的人意識到 , 包括一位前大學教授 , 他們說: 「 你不是無家可歸 , 你為什麼要在這裡 ? 」
other homeless people didn't see me as homeless , but i did .	其他無家可歸的人 , 我也沒見過我 。
then the professor listened to my story and he said , " you have a job . you have hope .	接著 , 教授聽我的故事 , 他說: 「 你有個工作 , 你有希望 。
the real homeless don't have hope . "	無家可歸的無家可歸 。 」
a reaction to the medication the clinic gave me for my depression left me suicidal . and i remember thinking , " if i killed myself , no one would notice . "	診所給了我的憂鬱症 , 造成了我的憂鬱症 。 我記得我心想: 「 如果我殺了我 , 我記得我在想: 「 如果我殺了我 , 我還記得我在想: 「 如果我殺了我 , 我還記得我心想 。 」
a friend told me , shortly after that , that she had heard that tim russert , a nationally renowned journalist , had been talking about me on national t . v .	一個朋友告訴我 , 沒多久 , 她聽說了timrussert , 一個全國性的記者 , 一直在談論我在國際電視台上 。
an essay i'd written about my father , the year before he died , was in tim's new book .	我寫了一篇文章 , 是在tim的新書中 。
and he was doing the talk show circuit . and he was talking about my writing .	當時他正在講我的寫作 。
and when i realized that tim russert , former moderator of " meet the press , " was talking about my writing , while i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , i started laughing .	當我意識到timrussert在walmartsertssertsertssertsertssertsertstimrussert時 , 我開始笑了 。
i started laughing because it got to the point where , was i a writer , or was i a homeless woman ?	我開始笑 , 因為它到達的地方 , 我是作家 , 或是我是一位作家 , 還是我是無家可歸的人 ?
so i went in the bookstore . and i found tim's book .	所以我去了書 , 我找到了tim的書 。
and i stood there . and i reread my essay .	我站在那裡 , 然後我把我的文字放進去 。
because i was a writer .	因為我是作家 。
i was a writer .	我是個作家 。
shortly after that i moved back to tennessee .	不久之後 , 我搬到密度 。
i alternated between living in a van and couch surfing with friends .	我住在一間旅館裡 , 與朋友一起生活 。
and i started writing again .	我又開始寫作 。
by the summer of the following year i was a working journalist .	接下來的夏天 , 我是記者 。
i was winning awards . i was living in my own apartment .	我贏得獎勵 , 我住在我自己的公寓 。
i was no longer homeless .	我不再無家可歸 。
and i was no longer invisible .	我不再隱形了 。
thousands of people work full and parttime jobs , and live in their cars .	成千上萬的人工作 , 生活在他們的車子裡 。
but society continues to stigmatize and criminalize living in your vehicle or on the streets .	但社會持續著犯罪犯罪犯 , 或街道上 。
so the homeless , the working homeless , primarily remain invisible .	所以 , 無家可歸 , 無家可歸 , 無家可歸 , 無家可歸 。
but if you ever meet one , engage them , encourage them , and offer them hope .	但如果你遇見一個人 , 鼓勵他們 , 鼓勵他們 , 鼓勵他們 , 鼓勵他們 , 鼓勵他們 , 鼓勵他們 , 鼓勵他們 。
the human spirit can overcome anything if it has hope .	人類的精神可以克服任何東西 , 如果它有希望 。
and i'm not here to be the poster girl for the homeless .	我不是在這裡 , 要成為那些無家可歸的女性 。
i'm not here to encourage you to give money to the next panhandler you meet .	我不是在這裡鼓勵你去鼓勵你去鼓勵你去給下一個panhandler 。
but i am here to tell you that , based on my experience , people are not where they live , where they sleep , or what their life situation is at any given time .	但我在這裡要告訴各位 , 基於我的經驗 , 人們不是他們生活在哪裡 , 或他們生活在哪裡 。
three years ago i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , and today i'm speaking at ted .	三年前 , 我住在一個沃爾瑪的火車場 , 今天我在ted演講 。
hope always , always finds a way . thank you .	希望總是找到一種方式 。 謝謝 。
at tedxchange , thailand's " mr . condom , " mechai viravaidya , walks us through the country's bold plan to raise its standard of living , starting in the 1970s . first step: population control . and that means a lot of frank , funny and very effective talk about condoms .	在tedxchange , tedxchange , thailandmr.stexchange , thailand " mr. " thailand " mr " thailand " thailand " , 第一次步驟:人口控制 。 這意味著 , 很多坦白 , 非常有效的談談保險套 。
culture , global issues , health , population , science	文化、全球議題、健康、人口、科學 。
mechai viravaidya: how mr . condom made thailand a better place	伊維拉維拉瓦迪亞:馬上 , 泰國是怎樣的 。
now , when i was a young man 40 years ago , the country was very , very poor with lots and lots and lots of people living in poverty .	在我年輕的時候 , 40年前 , 國家很貧窮 , 許多人生活在貧困中 。
we decided to do something about it , but we didn't begin with a welfare program or a poverty reduction program .	我們決定要做點什麼 , 但我們不從福利計畫或貧窮的計畫開始 。
but we began with a familyplanning program , following a very successful maternal child health activity , sets of activities .	但我們從一個家庭的計畫開始 , 有一個非常成功的兒童健康活動 , 活動 。
so basically , no one would accept family planning if their children didn't survive .	基本上 , 沒有人接受家庭計劃如果孩子沒有生存 。
so the first step: get to the children , get to the mothers , and then follow up with family planning .	所以 , 第一步:到孩子們 , 到孩子們 , 到媽媽 , 然後追隨家庭計劃 。
not just child mortality alone , you need also family planning .	不只是孩子的死亡率 , 你也需要家庭計劃 。
now let me take you back as to why we needed to do it .	現在 , 讓我帶各位回顧一下為什麼我們需要這麼做 。
in my country , that was the case in 1974 .	在我的國家 , 那是1974年的案例 。
seven children per family tremendous growth at 3 . 3 percent .	在3.3%的成長中 , 3.3% 。
there was just no future .	沒有未來 。
we needed to reduce the population growth rate .	我們需要減少人口成長率 。
so we said , " let's do it . "	所以我們說: 「 咱們來做吧 。 」
the women said , " we agree . we'll use pills , but we need a doctor to prescribe the pills , " and we had very , very few doctors .	婦女說: 「 我們會用藥丸 , 但我們需要醫生來做乳癌 。 我們會吃藥 。 」 我們很少醫生 。
we didn't take no as an answer ; we took no as a question .	我們不把問題當作一個問題 。
we went to the nurses and the midwives , who were also women , and did a fantastic job at explaining how to use the pill .	我們去了護士和蜘蛛 , 也是女性 , 做了一個很棒的工作 , 來解釋如何用藥劑 。
that was wonderful , but it covered only 20 percent of the country .	這很棒 , 但它只佔了20%的國家 。
what do we do for the other 80 percent leave them alone and say , " well , they're not medical personnel . "	我們對其他80%的人說: 「 嗯 , 他們不是醫療人員 。 」
no , we decided to do a bit more .	不 , 我們決定再做一點 。
so we went to the ordinary people that you saw .	所以 , 我們去了你看到的一般人 。
actually , below that yellow sign i wish they hadn't wiped that , because there was " cocacola " there .	其實 , 在那黃色的標誌裡 , 我希望他們沒有太過 , 因為有 「 可口可樂 」 。
we were so much bigger than cocacola in those days .	在那天 , 我們比可口可樂還多 。
and no difference , the people they chose were the people we chose .	沒有差異 , 他們選擇的人就是我們選擇的人 。
they were wellknown in the community , they knew that customers were always right , and they were terrific , and they practiced their family planning themselves .	在社區中 , 他們知道客戶通常是對的 , 他們知道客戶總是對的 , 他們很擅長 , 他們很擅長 , 他們很擅長 , 他們很擅長 , 他們很擅長 , 他們很擅長 , 他們很擅長 , 他們很擅長 。
so they could supply pills and condoms throughout the country , in every village of the country .	所以他們可以供應藥丸和保險套在全國各地的村莊
so there we are . we went to the people who were seen as the cause of the problem to be the solution .	所以 , 我們走到那些被視為解決方案的人 。
wherever there were people and you can see boats with the women , selling things here's the floating market selling bananas and crabs and also contraceptives wherever you find people , you'll find contraceptives in thailand .	不論你在哪裡去找誰 , 你會發現在泰國 , 賣香蕉、螃蟹、販賣香蕉、螃蟹 , 還有避孕法 , 你就會發現在泰國的販賣品 。
and then we decided , why not get to religion because in the philippines , the catholic church was pretty strong , and thai people were buddhist .	接著 , 我們決定 , 為什麼不去宗教 , 因為在菲律賓 , 天教教堂非常強壯 , 以及泰國人是佛教徒 。
we went to them and they said , " look , could you help us ? "	我們去找他們 , 說: 「 看 , 你能幫我們嗎 ? 」
i'm there the one in blue , not the yellow holding a bowl of holy water for the monk to sprinkle holy water on pills and condoms for the sanctity of the family .	我是藍色的 , 不是黃色的 , 黃色的房子裡有一塊水 , 用在藥丸和保險套上 , 讓大家吃飯 。
and this picture was sent throughout the country .	這張照片被送到整個國家 。
so some of the monks in the villages were doing the same thing themselves .	所以 , 村落裡的一些猴子也做同樣的事 。
and the women were saying , " no wonder we have no sideeffects .	女人會說: 「 不知道我們有沒有副作用 。
it's been blessed . "	很幸運 。 」
that was their perception .	那是他們的感知 。
and then we went to teachers .	接著 , 我們去教師 。

because poor people are business people who lack business skills and access to credit .	因為窮人是商業缺乏商業的商業技能和取得信仰的人 。
those are the things to be provided by the business community .	這些是商業社區所提供的 。
we're trying to turn them into barefoot entrepreneurs , little business people .	我們試著把它們轉變成基礎創業家 , 小型企業家 。
the only way out of poverty is through business enterprise .	貧窮的唯一方法就是透過企業企業 。
so , that was done .	所以 , 那就完成了 。
the money goes from the company into the village via treeplanting .	錢從公司到村莊的村莊 。
it's not a free gift .	這不是自由禮物 。
they plant the trees , and the money goes into their microcredit fund , which we call the village development bank .	他們把樹木拿到他們的微信箱裡 , 我們稱之為鄉村發展銀行 。
everybody joins in , and they feel they own the bank , because they have brought the money in .	每個人都加入 , 他們覺得自己是銀行 , 因為他們把錢花了 。
and before you can borrow the money , you need to be trained .	在你能借錢之前 , 你需要被訓練 。
and we believe if you want to help the poor , those who are living in poverty , access to credit must be a human right .	我們相信 , 如果你想要幫助窮人 , 那些住在貧窮的窮人 , 那些活在貧窮的人權中 , 才是人權的 。

here's what we call a " barefoot mba , " teaching people how to do business so that , when they borrow money , they'll succeed with the business .	這是我們稱之為 「 教導人們如何做企業 」 的課題 , 當他們借錢時 , 他們就會成功 。

your smartphone may feel like a friend but a true friend would give you a smile once in a while . at ted2013 , keller rinaudo demos romo , the smartphonepowered mini robot who can motor along with you on a walk , slide you a cup of coffee across the table , and react to you with programmable expressions .	你的智慧手機可能感覺像是朋友 , 但你會給你一杯咖啡 , 一杯咖啡 , 在ted2013年 , 泰德莫斯•羅莫 , 一個朋友 , 一個朋友 , 給你一杯咖啡 , 在ted2013年 , 泰德莫斯•羅莫斯 , 一個朋友 , 給你一杯咖啡 , 在ted2013年 , 泰德莫斯•羅莫斯 , 一個朋友 , 給你一個微笑 。
keller rinaudo: a mini robot powered by your phone	kellerrinaudo:一個mini機器人 , 來自你的手機 。
so just by a show of hands , how many of you all have a robot at home ?	舉例來說 , 有多少人在家裡有機器人 ?
not very many of you .	不是很多人 。
okay . and actually of those hands , if you don't include roomba how many of you have a robot at home ?	好吧 , 實際上 , 那些手 , 如果你不包含房子裡的機器人 , 你有多少人在家裡 ?
that's the problem that we're trying to solve at romotive that i and the other 20 nerds at romotive are obsessed with solving .	這就是我們在努力解決的問題 , 同時我和其他20位德羅摩托夫人在romott上工作 , 也是我和其他20位迷人在羅馬福特工作的 。
so we really want to build a robot that anyone can use , whether you're eight or 80 .	所以我們真的想要建造一個機器人 , 任何人都可以使用 , 無論你是八十歲 。
and as it turns out , that's a really hard problem , because you have to build a small , portable robot that's not only really affordable , but it has to be something that people actually want to take home and have around their kids .	結果發現 , 這是個非常困難的問題 , 因為你必須建造一個小型、可攜式的機器人 , 不僅僅是可行的機器人 , 而且它必須是一個非常困難的問題 。
this robot can't be creepy or uncanny .	這種機器人不能是奇怪或不可思議 。
he should be friendly and cute .	他應該是友善且可愛的 。
romo's a robot that uses a device you already know and love your iphone as his brain .	romo是一個機器人 , 用一種裝置你已經知道和愛你的iphone的機器人 。
and by leveraging the power of the iphone's processor , we can create a robot that is wifi enabled and computer visioncapable for 150 bucks , which is about one percent of what these kinds of robots have cost in the past .	藉由使用iphone處理器的力量 , 我們就能創造一個機器人 , 在過去 , 使用iphone處理器的能力 , 可以創造出一個機器人 , 大約有150美元 , 可以創造出一個機器人 , 可以創造一個機器人 , 可以在過去有150美元 。

so there are all of you through romo's eyes .	所以 , 在羅姆的眼睛中 , 你都看到了romo的眼睛 。

so he actually streams twoway audio and video between any two smart devices .	所以他實際上在兩個智慧裝置之間傳播了兩種智慧裝置 。
