mit researcher skylar tibbits works on selfassembly the idea that instead of building something , we can create materials that build themselves , much the way a strand of dna zips itself together . it's a big concept at early stages ; tibbits shows us three inthelab projects that hint at what a selfassembling future might look like .	麻省理工學院學院的研究人員在自我組裝的過程中 , 不是建造東西 , 我們可以創造材料 , 建造出自己 , 可以製造出一種自我組裝的模型 , 可以製造出一個自我組裝的樣子 , 比方說 , 我們可以創造材料 , 將它們自組裝置在自我組合的模型中 , 以至於自我組合的未來可能看起來像這樣 。
skylar tibbits: can we make things that make themselves ?	太陽能 , 可以讓自己做些東西嗎 ?
today i'd like to show you the future of the way we make things .	今天我想給大家看我們製作東西的方法 。
i believe that soon our buildings and machines will be selfassembling , replicating and repairing themselves .	我相信 , 很快的 , 我們的建築物和機器會自我組合、複製、修復自己 。
so i'm going to show you what i believe is the current state of manufacturing , and then compare that to some natural systems .	所以 , 我來告訴各位我相信目前的生產過程 , 和一些自然系統的運作方式相比 。
so in the current state of manufacturing , we have skyscrapers two and a half years [of assembly time] , 500 , 000 to a million parts , fairly complex , new , exciting technologies in steel , concrete , glass .	所以 , 在現有的技術上 , 我們有天花板 , 花了兩年半的時間 , 50萬到1000000000000000 , 000到一百萬個部分 , 非常複雜、令人興奮的技術 , 像是鋼鐵、水泥、玻璃 。
we have exciting machines that can take us into space five years [of assembly time] , 2 . 5 million parts .	我們有令人振奮的機器 , 可以帶我們進入太空五年內 , 等於2500萬個部分 。
but on the other side , if you look at the natural systems , we have proteins that have two million types , can fold in 10 , 000 nanoseconds , or dna with three billion base pairs we can replicate in roughly an hour .	但另一方面 , 如果你觀察自然系統 , 我們有兩百萬種類型的蛋白質 , 有兩百萬種類型 , 可以複製在大約一小時 。
so there's all of this complexity in our natural systems , but they're extremely efficient , far more efficient than anything we can build , far more complex than anything we can build .	所以 , 我們自然體系中有許多複雜的系統 , 但它們非常有效率 , 比任何我們能建造的更有效率 , 更有效率 , 比任何我們能建造的更有效率 。
they're far more efficient in terms of energy .	它們在能源方面更有效率 。
they hardly ever make mistakes .	他們很難犯錯 。
and they can repair themselves for longevity .	牠們可以修復自己長壽 。
so there's something super interesting about natural systems .	所以 , 自然體系中有很有趣的東西 。
and if we can translate that into our built environment , then there's some exciting potential for the way that we build things .	如果我們可以把它轉化為我們的建築環境 , 那就有一些令人興奮的潛力 , 以我們建造的方式 。
and i think the key to that is selfassembly .	我認為關鍵是自我組裝 。
so if we want to utilize selfassembly in our physical environment , i think there's four key factors .	所以 , 如果我們想要在我們的身體環境中運作 , 我認為有四個關鍵因素 。
the first is that we need to decode all of the complexity of what we want to build so our buildings and machines .	首先 , 我們需要解碼我們所需要的複雜性 , 來建造我們的建築物和機器 。
and we need to decode that into simple sequences basically the dna of how our buildings work .	我們需要解碼到簡單的序列 , 基本上是我們建築物的運作方式 。
then we need programmable parts that can take that sequence and use that to fold up , or reconfigure .	接著 , 我們需要程式的部分 , 可以採取那個序列 , 用它來摺疊或重複 。
we need some energy that's going to allow that to activate , allow our parts to be able to fold up from the program .	我們需要一些能量 , 讓它能夠從程式中解開 。
and we need some type of error correction redundancy to guarantee that we have successfully built what we want .	我們需要一些類型錯誤的反射線來保證我們成功地建立了我們所想要的 。
so i'm going to show you a number of projects that my colleagues and i at mit are working on to achieve this selfassembling future .	所以 , 我要給你們看一些我同事在麻省理工學院的工作 , 來達成這個自我組裝的未來 。
the first two are the macrobot and decibot .	第一個是mcrobot和decibot 。
so these projects are largescale reconfigurable robots 8 ft . , 12 ft . long proteins .	所以這些計劃是大規模的重建機器人 , 十二公尺高 , 十二英尺長蛋白質 。
they're embedded with mechanical electrical devices , sensors .	它們被用機械電裝置 , 感應器 。
you decode what you want to fold up into , into a sequence of angles so negative 120 , negative 120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , negative 120 something like that ; so a sequence of angles , or turns , and you send that sequence through the string .	你解碼你想要摺疊成一系列的角度、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、1
each unit takes its message so negative 120 it rotates to that , checks if it got there and then passes it to its neighbor .	每個單位都把它送到鄰近 , 只要它到那裡 , 就會傳送到它的鄰居 。
so these are the brilliant scientists , engineers , designers that worked on this project .	這些是傑出的科學家 , 工程師 , 設計師在這個專案計畫工作 。
and i think it really brings to light: is this really scalable ?	我認為這真的很可怕嗎 ?
i mean , thousands of dollars , lots of man hours made to make this eightfoot robot .	我的意思是 , 數千美元 , 數以千計的人 , 花了數千美元 , 花了很多小時製作這個8英尺的機器人 。
can we really scale this up ? can we really embed robotics into every part ?	我們能否實現它嗎 ? 可以把機器人放到每一個部分嗎 ?
the next one questions that and looks at passive nature , or passively trying to have reconfiguration programmability .	下一個問題是 , 或通過性地嘗試修復程式 。
but it goes a step further , and it tries to have actual computation .	但它更進一步 , 試圖實際計算 。
it basically embeds the most fundamental building block of computing , the digital logic gate , directly into your parts .	基本上 , 它基本上是建立了數位邏輯 , 直接進入你的部分 。
so this is a nand gate .	這是一個nandgate 。
you have one tetrahedron which is the gate that's going to do your computing , and you have two input tetrahedrons .	你有一支電鐵 , 你有兩個輸入的鐵路 。
one of them is the input from the user , as you're building your bricks .	其中之一是使用者的輸入 , 如同你在建造你的磚塊 。
the other one is from the previous brick that was placed .	另一個是從前面的磚塊 。
and then it gives you an output in 3d space .	然後它會給你一個輸入3d空間的空間 。
so what this means is that the user can start plugging in what they want the bricks to do .	所以這意味著 , 使用者可以開始在他們想要磚塊上做些什麼 。
it computes on what it was doing before and what you said you wanted it to do .	它計算了它在做什麼 , 你說你想要它做什麼 。
and now it starts moving in threedimensional space so up or down .	現在它開始在三維空間中移動 , 或下降 。
so on the lefthand side , [1 , 1] input equals 0 output , which goes down .	所以在左手邊 , 1.1 , 輸入1.1 , 輸入等於0輸入 , 結果是下降 。
on the righthand side , [0 , 0] input is a 1 output , which goes up .	在右手邊 , 0.0是1的輸入 , 輸出的結果是1的輸出 。
and so what that really means is that our structures now contain the blueprints of what we want to build .	所以這意味著 , 我們的結構現在包含了我們想要建造的藍圖 。
so they have all of the information embedded in them of what was constructed .	所以他們有所有的資訊都被建構出來 。
so that means that we can have some form of selfreplication .	這意味著我們可以有某種形式的自我複製 。
in this case i call it selfguided replication , because your structure contains the exact blueprints .	在這個案例中 , 我稱它為自我複製 , 因為你的結構包含了藍圖 。
if you have errors , you can replace a part .	如果你有錯誤 , 你可以取代一部分 。
all the local information is embedded to tell you how to fix it .	所有當地的資訊都被嵌入了 , 告訴你要如何修復它 。
so you could have something that climbs along and reads it and can output at one to one .	所以 , 你可以有一些東西可以爬上去 , 閱讀它 , 並且能輸入其中一個 。
it's directly embedded ; there's no external instructions .	它直接被嵌入 , 沒有外外的指令 。
so the last project i'll show is called biased chains , and it's probably the most exciting example that we have right now of passive selfassembly systems .	最後一個專案我稱之為 「 偏見鏈 」 , 它可能是最令人興奮的例子 , 就是我們現在所擁有的自動自組系統 。
so it takes the reconfigurability and programmability and makes it a completely passive system .	所以它需要重組和設計能力 , 讓它完全被動體系統 。
so basically you have a chain of elements .	基本上你有一塊元素 。
each element is completely identical , and they're biased .	每個元素都是完全相同的 , 它們偏見 。
so each chain , or each element , wants to turn right or left .	所以每個鏈 , 或左邊 , 都想要轉右或左邊 。
so as you assemble the chain , you're basically programming it .	所以當你組裝鏈 , 你基本上就是編寫程式 。
you're telling each unit if it should turn right or left .	你告訴每個單位 , 如果它應該轉右或左邊 。
so when you shake the chain , it then folds up into any configuration that you've programmed in so in this case , a spiral , or in this case , two cubes next to each other .	所以 , 當你搖晃鏈 , 就會折疊成任何你在這個案例中所編寫的程式 , 或這個案例 , 兩個立方體 。
so you can basically program any threedimensional shape or onedimensional , twodimensional up into this chain completely passively .	所以你可以基本上設計任何三維空間的形狀或維度 , 把它放在這個鏈上完全被動 。
so what does this tell us about the future ?	這告訴我們什麼呢 ?
i think that it's telling us that there's new possibilities for selfassembly , replication , repair in our physical structures , our buildings , machines .	我認為 , 它告訴我們 , 我們的建築物、機器 , 都有新的可能性 。
there's new programmability in these parts .	在這些部分中有新的程式 。
and from that you have new possibilities for computing .	從你有新的可能性來計算 。
we'll have spatial computing .	我們會有空間運算 。
imagine if our buildings , our bridges , machines , all of our bricks could actually compute .	想像一下 , 如果我們的建築、橋樑、機器 , 所有的磚塊都可以計算 。
that's amazing parallel and distributed computing power , new design possibilities .	這是很棒的計算能力 , 新的設計可能性 。
so it's exciting potential for this .	所以 , 這很令人興奮 。
so i think these projects i've showed here are just a tiny step towards this future , if we implement these new technologies for a new selfassembling world .	所以 , 我認為這些計畫已經展現出一個新的自我組裝世界 。
we've been to the moon , we've mapped the continents , we've even been to the deepest point in the ocean twice . what's left for the next generation to explore ? biologist and explorer nathan wolfe suggests this answer: almost everything . and we can start , he says , with the world of the unseeably small .	我們已經登陸月球 , 我們已經到達地球上最深的一刻 , 去探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索
biodiversity , exploration , microbiology , science	生物多樣性、探索、生物多樣性、探索、微生物學 。
nathan wolfe: what's left to explore ?	nathanwolfe:剩下的是什麼 ?
recently i visited beloit , wisconsin .	最近我去了布萊斯康斯康斯康斯康斯 。
and i was there to honor a great 20th century explorer , roy chapman andrews .	我很榮幸 , 二十世紀的探險家 , 羅莉•查普曼德雷斯 。
during his time at the american museum of natural history , andrews led a range of expeditions to uncharted regions , like here in the gobi desert .	在美國自然歷史博物館中 , 奧爾德雷特在美國自然歷史博物館內進行了許多探險 , 來到未知的區域 , 如同在座的沙漠 。
he was quite a figure .	他的確是很合理的 。
he was later , it's said , the basis of the indiana jones character .	後來 , 他說 , 印度的基礎是印第安納瓊斯的基礎 。
and when i was in beloit , wisconsin , i gave a public lecture to a group of middle school students .	當我在布魯威斯康斯康斯康辛 , 我給一群中學學生的一群中學學生 。
and i'm here to tell you , if there's anything more intimidating than talking here at ted , it'll be trying to hold the attention of a group of a thousand 12yearolds for a 45minute lecture .	我在這裡要告訴各位 , 如果這裡有比在ted演講中更感激的事情 , 會試著把注意力集成一千個12歲的孩子 , 一個45分鐘的演講 。
at the end of the lecture they asked a number of questions , but there was one that's really stuck with me since then .	在課程結束時 , 他們問了一些問題 , 但有一件事是從那之後開始的 。
there was a young girl who stood up , and she asked the question: " where should we explore ? "	有一位年輕的女孩站起來 , 她問了這個問題: 「 我們要去哪裡 ? 」
i think there's a sense that many of us have that the great age of exploration on earth is over , that for the next generation they're going to have to go to outer space or the deepest oceans in order to find something significant to explore .	我認為有許多人在地球上都知道 , 最深的海洋是為了尋找重要的探索 , 要去外太空或深海 。
but is that really the case ?	但那是真的嗎 ?
is there really nowhere significant for us to explore left here on earth ?	在地球上 , 我們是否有極大的意義去探索左邊地球 ?
it sort of made me think back to one of my favorite explorers in the history of biology .	這讓我覺得回到我最喜歡的探險家之一 。
this is an explorer of the unseen world , martinus beijerinck .	這是未知世界的探險家 , 馬丁斯•貝伊斯 。
so beijerinck set out to discover the cause of tobacco mosaic disease .	所以beijerinck發現了菸草疾病的原因 。
what he did is he took the infected juice from tobacco plants and he would filter it through smaller and smaller filters .	他所做的是 , 他把感染的汁液從菸草植物中拿出來 , 然後他會把感染的汁液從菸草植物中 , 更小的味道 。
and he reached the point where he felt that there must be something out there that was smaller than the smallest forms of life that were ever known bacteria , at the time .	他到達了這個點子 , 知道細菌的存在 , 比最小的生命中有所得知的細菌更小 。
he came up with a name for his mystery agent .	他提出了一個名字 , 名字是他的謎團 。
he called it the virus latin for " poison . "	他稱之為 「 毒藥 」 。
and in uncovering viruses , beijerinck really opened this entirely new world for us .	在未知病毒的病毒中 , 貝莉克真的打開了這個全新的世界 。
we now know that viruses make up the majority of the genetic information on our planet , more than the genetic information of all other forms of life combined .	我們現在知道病毒會把基因資訊傳遞到我們的星球上 , 遠超過其它生命組成的基因信息 。
and obviously there's been tremendous practical applications associated with this world things like the eradication of smallpox , the advent of a vaccine against cervical cancer , which we now know is mostly caused by human papillomavirus .	很顯然 , 這種世界有很大的實際應用 , 例如 , 避免疫苗的抗癌 , 我們現在知道最主要是由人類皮質病毒所造成的 。
and beijerinck's discovery , this was not something that occurred 500 years ago .	貝蒂克的發現 , 這並不是發生在500年前發生的事 。
it was a little over 100 years ago that beijerinck discovered viruses .	大約一百年前 , 蜜蜂鳥發現了病毒 。
so basically we had automobiles , but we were unaware of the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	基本上 , 我們有自動飛行器 , 但我們沒有意識到地球上所有基因資訊的形式 。
we now have these amazing tools to allow us to explore the unseen world things like deep sequencing , which allow us to do much more than just skim the surface and look at individual genomes from a particular species , but to look at entire metagenomes , the communities of teeming microorganisms in , on and around us and to document all of the genetic information in these species .	現在我們有了這些驚人的工具 , 讓我們能夠去探索未知的世界 , 像是深深的序列 , 讓我們能夠探索未知的世界 , 像是深深的序列 , 讓我們能夠探索未知的世界 , 來記錄所有基因遺傳信息 。
we can apply these techniques to things from soil to skin and everything in between .	我們可以應用這些技術 , 從土壤到皮膚和所有東西 。
in my organization we now do this on a regular basis to identify the causes of outbreaks that are unclear exactly what causes them .	在我的組織中 , 我們現在用一種規定的方式來判斷出疫情爆發的原因 , 不一定會造成它們 。
and just to give you a sense of how this works , imagine that we took a nasal swab from every single one of you .	為了讓大家了解這個作品如何運作 , 想像一下 , 想像一下 , 我們從每個人身上帶著一根氣味 。
and this is something we commonly do to look for respiratory viruses like influenza .	這是我們常常能去尋找呼吸器的病毒 , 像是流感病毒 。
the first thing we would see is a tremendous amount of genetic information .	首先 , 我們會看到的是巨大的基因資訊 。
and if we started looking into that genetic information , we'd see a number of usual suspects out there of course , a lot of human genetic information , but also bacterial and viral information , mostly from things that are completely harmless within your nose .	如果我們開始研究基因信息 , 我們會看到許多人的基因信息 , 大部分是來自於你鼻子裡完全無害的東西 。
but we'd also see something very , very surprising .	但我們也看到了一些非常令人驚訝的事 。
as we started to look at this information , we would see that about 20 percent of the genetic information in your nose doesn't match anything that we've ever seen before no plant , animal , fungus , virus or bacteria .	當我們開始觀察這些資訊時 , 我們會看到20%的基因信息 , 在你的鼻子裡 , 沒有植物、動物、真菌、病毒或細菌 。
basically we have no clue what this is .	基本上 , 我們不知道這是什麼 。
and for the small group of us who actually study this kind of data , a few of us have actually begun to call this information biological dark matter .	對於小組的研究 , 我們事實上研究這種數據 , 其中少數人已經開始稱之為 「 資訊生物暗物質 」 。
we know it's not anything that we've seen before ; it's sort of the equivalent of an uncharted continent right within our own genetic information .	我們知道它不是我們之前所見過的 , 它是完全不在我們自己的基因信息中所看到的 。
and there's a lot of it .	還有很多 。
if you think 20 percent of genetic information in your nose is a lot of biological dark matter , if we looked at your gut , up to 40 or 50 percent of that information is biological dark matter .	如果你認為20%的基因信息是生態暗物質 , 如果你在你的鼻子裡有40%或50%的基因資訊是生物暗物質 。
and even in the relatively sterile blood , around one to two percent of this information is dark matter can't be classified , can't be typed or matched with anything we've seen before .	即使在相對的血液中 , 大約有1%到2%的資訊是黑暗物質無法被分配或配合我們所見過的東西 。
at first we thought that perhaps this was artifact .	首先 , 我們以為可能是工藝品 。
these deep sequencing tools are relatively new .	這些深密的工具是相對的 。
but as they become more and more accurate , we've determined that this information is a form of life , or at least some of it is a form of life .	但隨著它們變得更精確 , 我們決定信息是生命的一種形式 , 或者至少是生命的一部分 。
and while the hypotheses for explaining the existence of biological dark matter are really only in their infancy , there's a very , very exciting possibility that exists: that buried in this life , in this genetic information , are signatures of as of yet unidentified life .	雖然假設解釋了生物暗物質的存在 , 存在於生命中 , 在這個基因信息中 , 存在的可能性存在 , 存在於生命中 , 在這個基因信息中 , 存在的可能性存在:埋藏在生命中 。
that as we explore these strings of a's , t's , c's and g's , we may uncover a completely new class of life that , like beijerinck , will fundamentally change the way that we think about the nature of biology .	當我們探索這些弦 , 像是beijerinck , 基本上改變了我們對生物學的看法 。
that perhaps will allow us to identify the cause of a cancer that afflicts us or identify the source of an outbreak that we aren't familiar with or perhaps create a new tool in molecular biology .	這或許會讓我們能夠辨識出我們對癌症的新工具 , 或辨別出我們所熟悉的新工具 , 或在分子生物學中找到一種新工具 。
i'm pleased to announce that , along with colleagues at stanford and caltech and ucsf , we're currently starting an initiative to explore biological dark matter for the existence of new forms of life .	我很高興能告訴大家 , 在史丹佛大學和加州史丹佛大學的同事 , 我們目前正在進行一項探索生物暗物質 , 來探索生物暗物質存在於新生命的存在 。
a little over a hundred years ago , people were unaware of viruses , the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	一百年前 , 人們不知病毒 , 生命的形式 , 形成了我們地球上大部分基因資訊的基因資訊 。
a hundred years from now , people may marvel that we were perhaps completely unaware of a new class of life that literally was right under our noses .	一百年後 , 人們可能會馬上發現我們可能完全不知道 , 人類的新階段 , 可能是完全不知我們所知的新階段 。
it's true , we may have charted all the continents on the planet and we may have discovered all the mammals that are out there , but that doesn't mean that there's nothing left to explore on earth .	真的 , 我們可能在地球上發現所有的哺乳類動物 , 我們可能發現了所有的哺乳動物 , 但這並不表示 , 地球上沒有任何東西 。
beijerinck and his kind provide an important lesson for the next generation of explorers people like that young girl from beloit , wisconsin .	威斯康斯康斯康斯康斯康斯康斯康斯康辛 , 他對下一代的探險家提供了重要的課程 , 像是年輕女孩 , 伊斯康斯康斯康斯康 。
and i think if we phrase that lesson , it's something like this: don't assume that what we currently think is out there is the full story .	我想如果我們把這句話說出來 , 就如這樣:不假設我們現在所認為的 , 就是它的存在 。
go after the dark matter in whatever field you choose to explore .	除非你選擇去探索的暗物質 。
there are unknowns all around us and they're just waiting to be discovered .	不知我們周遭的環境 , 等著被發現 。
legendary scientist david deutsch puts theoretical physics on the back burner to discuss a more urgent matter: the survival of our species . the first step toward solving global warming , he says , is to admit that we have a problem .	法律科學家大衛•狄克斯基博士會提出理論物理 , 他說 , 要承認我們有問題 , 要承認我們有問題 。
climate change , cosmos , culture , environment , global issues , physics , science , technology , universe	氣候變遷、科學、科技、宇宙 。
david deutsch on our place in the cosmos	大衛•迪德在宇宙中 , 在宇宙中 。
we've been told to go out on a limb and say something surprising .	我們被告知要走出來 , 說出令人意外的事 。
so i'll try and do that , but i want to start with two things that everyone already knows .	我會試著做這件事 , 但我想要從兩件事開始 , 大家都知道的 。
and the first one , in fact , is something that has been known for most of recorded history .	首先 , 事實上 , 大部分的記錄歷史都已知名 。
and that is that the planet earth , or the solar system , or our environment or whatever , is uniquely suited to sustain our evolution or creation , as it used to be thought and our present existence , and most important , our future survival .	那就是地球 , 或太陽系 , 或環境 , 不論我們在哪裡 , 都能維持我們的演化或創造力 , 以至於我們現在存在的存在 , 最重要的是 , 我們的未來生存 。
nowadays this idea has a dramatic name: spaceship earth .	現今這個想法有一個很戲劇性的名字:太空船地球 。
and the idea there is that outside the spaceship , the universe is implacably hostile , and inside is all we have , all we depend on .	而這個想法是 , 在太空船內 , 宇宙是無所不在的 , 宇宙是超級的 , 我們都仰賴 。
and we only get the one chance: if we mess up our spaceship , we've got nowhere else to go .	我們只得到一個機會:如果我們把太空船放進去 , 我們就沒辦法去了 。
now , the second thing that everyone already knows is that contrary to what was believed for most of human history , human beings are not , in fact , the hub of existence .	第二件 , 大家都知道的 , 其實是人類歷史上的人類歷史 , 人類史上沒有 , 實際上 , 人類史上是不存在的 。
as stephen hawking famously said , we're just a chemical scum on the surface of a typical planet that's in orbit around a typical star , which is on the outskirts of a typical galaxy , and so on .	如史蒂芬•霍金所說的 , 我們只是一個典型的星球 , 在一個典型的星球上 , 在一個典型的星球上 , 在一個典型的星球上 , 在一個典型的星球上 , 會在一個典型的星球上 。
now the first of those two things that everyone knows is kind of saying that we're at a very untypical place , uniquely suited and so on , and the second one is saying that we're at a typical place .	首先 , 大家知道的第一件是:我們在一個非常典型的地方 , 第二個說法是 , 我們在一個典型的狀態 。
and especially if you regard these two as deep truths to live by and to inform your life decisions , then they seem a little bit to conflict with each other .	尤其是如果你把這兩項深實的真相轉換為你生命的決策 , 那他們似乎會互相衝突 。
but that doesn't prevent them from both being completely false .	但這並不預防它們完全是錯誤的 。
and they are . so let me start with the second one: typical . well is this a typical place ? well , let's look around , you know , and look in a random direction , and we see a wall , and chemical scum and that's not typical of the universe at all .	第二個問題是:典型的 。 嗯 , 這是典型的 。 好吧 , 我們來看一下 , 一個典型的空間 , 一個典型的狀態 。 嗯 , 我們看到一座牆 , 一個典型的環境 , 一個典型的狀態 , 我們看到一座牆 , 化學物體 , 不是典型的 。
all you've got to do is go a few hundred miles in that same direction and look back , and you won't see any walls or chemical scum at all all you see is a blue planet . and if you go further than that , you'll see the sun , the solar system , and the stars and so on .	你只剩下一百英哩 , 直到你看到陽光、太陽、太陽、太陽、太陽、太陽、太陽、太陽、太陽、太陽、太陽、太陽、太陽、太陽 。
but that's still not typical of the universe , because stars come in galaxies .	但這仍然不是典型的宇宙 , 因為恆星在銀河系 。
and most places in the universe , a typical place in the universe , is nowhere near any galaxies .	在宇宙中 , 大部分地方在宇宙中 , 幾乎沒有任何銀河系 。
so let's go out further , till we're outside the galaxy , and look back , and yeah , there's the huge galaxy with spiral arms laid out in front of us .	再進一步 , 再進一步 , 向外星系 , 向外星系 , 看看 , 再來看看 , 是的 , 在我們面前有一個巨大的星系 。
and at this point we've come 100 , 000 light years from here .	在這個時候 , 我們已經有十萬個光年 。
but we're still nowhere near a typical place in the universe .	但我們仍然處於宇宙中一個典型的地方 。
to get to a typical place , you've got to go 1 , 000 times as far as that into intergalactic space .	要到達一個典型的地方 , 你必須有一千倍以外的空間 , 到達一個典型的地方 。
and so what does that look like ? typical .	這看起來是什麼樣子呢 ?
what does a typical place in the universe look like ?	宇宙中的典型是什麼樣子 ?
well , at enormous expense , ted has arranged a highresolution immersion virtual reality rendering of intergalactic space the view from intergalactic space .	嗯 , 很高解析度的虛擬實境 , 用了高解析度的虛擬實境空間 , 來分析虛擬實境的空間 。
so can we have the lights off , please , so we can see it ?	所以 , 我們可以有燈光 , 請 , 我們能看到它嗎 ?
well , not quite , not quite perfect you see , in intergalactic space intergalactic space is completely dark , pitch dark .	嗯 , 不太完美 , 你看到的空間是完全黑暗的 , 完全黑暗的 。
it's so dark that if you were to be looking at the nearest star to you , and that star were to explode as a supernova , and you were to be staring directly at it at the moment when its light reached you , you still wouldn't be able to see even a glimmer .	很黑暗的是 , 如果你在那顆星球上看最近的星星 , 你就會看到即使是一顆超新星 , 而那顆星球就會被視為超新星 , 而你就會被視為超新星 , 而那顆星星會被送到你 , 而那顆星星就會被視為超新星 , 而你就會被視為超新星 , 而你就會被視為超新星 。
that's how big and how dark the universe is .	這就是宇宙的多大和黑暗 。
and that's despite the fact that a supernova is so bright , so brilliant an event , that it would kill you stone dead at a range of several light years .	儘管如此 , 一個超新星很亮 , 很明亮 , 很明亮 , 很明亮 , 很明亮 , 很明亮 , 很明亮 , 所以 , 很明亮 , 這樣一來 , 才會殺死你在幾光年內爆炸的 。
and yet from intergalactic space , it's so far away you wouldn't even see it .	但從星際空間中 , 遠遠遠離你看不到 。
it's also very cold out there less than three degrees above absolute zero .	同時也非常寒冷 , 不到三度 , 絕對零 。
and it's very empty . the vacuum there is one million times less dense than the highest vacuum that our best technology on earth can currently create . so that's how different a typical place is from this place .	真空是如此 , 地球上最高的空氣有一百萬倍 , 比最高的空氣更高 , 我們最好的科技在地球上是如此 。 所以這是不同的典型的地方 。
and that is how untypical this place is .	這就是這個地方的樣子 。
so can we have the lights back on please ? thank you .	所以 , 我們可以有燈光嗎 ? 謝謝 。
now how do we know about an environment that's so far away , and so different , and so alien , from anything we're used to ?	現在我們如何知道一個環境是如此遙遠 , 外星人 , 和外星人 , 從我們所熟悉的環境呢 ?
well , the earth our environment , in the form of us is creating knowledge .	嗯 , 在我們的環境中 , 我們在創造知識 。
well , what does that mean ? well , look out even further than we've just been i mean from here , with a telescope and you'll see things that look like stars .	這意味著什麼呢 ? 嗯 , 比我們剛剛說的 , 我是指望遠鏡 , 而你會看到像星星一樣的東西 。
they're called " quasars . " quasars originally meant quasistellar object .	他們稱之為 「 四角洲 」 , 意思是 「 水龍 」 。
which means things that look a bit like stars . but they're not stars .	這意味著 , 看起來像星星一樣 , 但它們不是星星 。
and we know what they are . billions of years ago , and billions of light years away , the material at the center of a galaxy collapsed towards a supermassive black hole .	我們知道它們在幾十億年前、幾十億年前、幾十億年前、幾十億光年 , 星系中的物質在一個超大質量的黑洞 。
and then intense magnetic fields directed some of the energy of that gravitational collapse . and some of the matter , back out in the form of tremendous jets which illuminated lobes with the brilliance of i think it's a trillion suns .	接著 , 強烈的磁場會引發爆炸的能量 , 引力崩潰的能量 , 以及一些物質 , 以巨大的能量 , 重力崩塌的能量 , 甚至是一兆個太陽 。
now , the physics of the human brain could hardly be more unlike the physics of such a jet .	現在 , 人類大腦的物理學 , 不像噴射的物理一樣 。
we couldn't survive for an instant in it . language breaks down when trying to describe what it would be like in one of those jets .	我們無法存活下來 , 當嘗試描述它會發生什麼時 , 像是在噴射的那樣 。
it would be a bit like experiencing a supernova explosion , but at pointblank range and for millions of years at a time .	它會有點像是經歷超新星爆炸 , 但在一瞬間 , 數百萬年來 , 它會有點像經歷超新星爆炸 。
and yet , that jet happened in precisely such a way that billions of years later , on the other side of the universe , some bit of chemical scum could accurately describe , and model , and predict , and explain , above all there's your reference what was happening there , in reality .	然而 , 在宇宙的幾十億年後 , 在宇宙的另一邊 , 有些化學物體可以準確地描述、模型、預測 , 以及預測 , 並且預測 , 並且預測 , 並且預測 , 並且預測 , 並且預測 , 並且預測 , 並且預測 , 並且預測 , 並且預測 , 並且預測 , 並且預測 , 解釋一下 , 在宇宙的其他地方 , 有些化學物體可以準確地描述、模型、預測 。
the one physical system , the brain , contains an accurate working model of the other the quasar .	一個體體系統 , 大腦 , 包含了一個精確的模型 。
not just a superficial image of it , though it contains that as well , but an explanatory model , embodying the same mathematical relationships and the same causal structure .	不僅僅是一個超級的圖像 , 它包含了相同的數學關係和相同的數學關係和相同的數學關係 。
now that is knowledge . and if that weren't amazing enough , the faithfulness with which the one structure resembles the other is increasing with time . that is the growth of knowledge .	這就是知識的知識 。 如果你不夠驚人 , 不夠精彩的信仰 , 會隨著時間的成長 , 成為知識的基礎 。
so , the laws of physics have this special property .	所以 , 物理學的物理學有特別的特性 。
that physical objects , as unlike each other as they could possibly be , can nevertheless embody the same mathematical and causal structure and to do it more and more so over time .	這些物理物體物品 , 不像彼此相同的數學和蛋糕結構 , 可以很快地運作 , 相同的數學和蛋白質結構 , 讓它們能更加順暢 。
so we are a chemical scum that is different . this chemical scum has universality .	所以 , 我們是一個化學農場 , 化學的狀態是不同的 。 這化學的化量是不同的 。
its structure contains , with everincreasing precision , the structure of everything . this place , and not other places in the universe , is a hub which contains within itself the structural and causal essence of the whole of the rest of physical reality . and so , far from being insignificant , the fact that the laws of physics allow this , or even mandate that this can happen , is one of the most important things about the physical world .	它的結構和結合 , 包括了物理世界的所有東西 。 而非其它地方 , 其它的結構與其它的存在 , 實際上是物理世界的基礎 , 不論是哪個地方 , 都在宇宙中 , 實際上 , 物理定律和其它的基礎 , 不論是物理世界的任何地方 , 或甚至可以製造出它 , 它的結構和整體現實之間的差距非常重要 。
now how does the solar system and our environment , in the form of us acquire this special relationship with the rest of the universe ?	太陽系和我們的環境 , 我們如何與宇宙的相互作用 ?
well , one thing that's true about stephen hawking's remark i mean , it is true , but it's the wrong emphasis . one thing that's true about it is that it doesn't do it with any special physics . there's no special dispensation , no miracles involved . it does it simply with three things that we have here in abundance .	史蒂芬霍金所說的 , 是真的 , 但它是錯的 。 這是真的 , 但這是錯的 。 這是真正的 。 它是真正的 , 不論是錯的 , 只有三件事 , 就是我們所擁有的 , 沒有任何特殊的物理 , 沒有任何特殊的技術 。
one of them is matter , because the growth of knowledge is a form of information processing . information processing is computation , computation requires a computer there's no known way of making a computer without matter .	其中之一是 , 因為知識的增長是資訊處理的計算 , 計算的速度是資訊處理的計算 , 計算的速度是資訊處理計算 , 計算的速度是資訊處理計算的速度 , 不管是資訊處理的速度 。
we also need energy to make the computer , and most important , to make the media in effect onto which we record the knowledge that we discover .	我們也需要能量來製造電腦 , 最重要的是 , 讓媒體在影響我們所記錄的知識中所發現的知識 。
and then thirdly , less tangible , but just as essential for the openended creation of knowledge , of explanations , is evidence .	第三 , 更不容易理解 , 但 , 為了開放式知識的知識 , 簡單的解釋 , 是證據 。
now , our environment is inundated with evidence .	我們的環境充滿證據 。
we happen to get round to testing , let's say , newton's law of gravity about 300 years ago .	我們在進行測試時 , 牛頓的重力約300年前 。
but the evidence that we used to do that was falling down on every square meter of the earth for billions of years before that , and will continue to fall on for billions of years afterwards . and the same is true for all the other sciences .	但證據顯示我們過去數十億年來一直在地球上每平方公尺的數十億年 , 並且持續下降到地球的數十億年之久 , 同時也同樣地對其他科學的證據 。
as far as we know , evidence to discover the most fundamental truths of all the sciences is here just for the taking on our planet .	如我們所知 , 證據顯示 , 證據證明了科學的所有科學領域的真相 , 都是在地球上 。
our location is saturated with evidence , and also with matter and energy .	我們的位置是充滿證據的 , 同時也很重要和能量 。
out in intergalactic space , those three prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge are at their lowest possible supply .	在交際空間中 , 三種最低的可能供應商品 , 創造出了知識 。
as i said , it's empty ; it's cold ; and it's dark out there . or is it ?	如同我所說的 , 它是空的 ; 冷卻是冷 ; 它是空氣的 ; 它是冷的 , 它是空的嗎 ?
now actually , that's just another parochial misconception .	事實上 , 這只是另一種錯誤觀念 。
because imagine a cube out there in intergalactic space , the same size as our home , the solar system . now that cube is very empty by human standards , but that still means that it contains over a million tons of matter .	因為想像一個立方體在地平線上 , 相同的尺寸 , 正如我們家鄉的太陽系 , 這個方塊是人類標準的大小 , 但那仍然意味著它包含了一百萬噸的重量 。
and a million tons is enough to make , say , a selfcontained space station , on which there's a colony of scientists that are devoted to creating an openended stream of knowledge , and so on .	一百萬噸足夠 , 來創造出一個開放式的流傳知識 , 以此類推 。
now , it's way beyond present technology to even gather the hydrogen from intergalactic space and form it into other elements and so on .	現在 , 遠遠超越科技甚至能把氫氣從交叉空間轉換成其他元素 。
but the thing is , in a comprehensible universe , if something isn't forbidden by the laws of physics , then what could possibly prevent us from doing it , other than knowing how ?	但 , 問題是 , 在一個不可思議的宇宙中 , 如果沒有被物理定律所發生的一切 , 那麼 , 我們可以阻止我們做的事 , 不知如何 ?
in other words , it's a matter of knowledge , not resources .	換句話說 , 這是知識 , 不是資源 。
and the same well , if we could do that we'd automatically have an energy supply , because the transmutation would be a fusion reactor and evidence ?	同樣的 , 如果我們能自動駕駛 , 因為運輸會是核融合反應爐和證據 。
well , again , it's dark out there to human senses . but all you've got to do is take a telescope , even one of presentday design , look out and you'll see the same galaxies as we do from here .	嗯 , 再一次 , 黑暗對人類有意義 。 但是你要做的是用望遠鏡 , 甚至是日常設計 , 向外看 , 你會看到同一個銀河系 。
and with a more powerful telescope , you'll be able to see stars , and planets .	有了更大的望遠鏡 , 你就能看見星星和行星 。
in those galaxies , you'll be able to do astrophysics , and learn the laws of physics .	在這些銀河系中 , 你可以做天體物理學物理學法 。
and locally there you could build particle accelerators , and learn elementary particle physics , and chemistry , and so on .	在那裡 , 你可以建造粒子加速器 , 並且學習粒子物理學 , 和化學等等 。
probably the hardest science to do would be biology field trips because it would take several hundred million years to get to the nearest lifebearing planet and back .	或許最難的科學是生物學領域的旅程 , 因為它花了數億年才能到達地球上最難的地方 。
but i have to tell you and sorry , richard but i never did like biology field trips much , and i think we can just about make do with one every few hundred million years .	但是我必須告訴各位 , 抱歉 , 理查但我從來沒有做過像生物學領域的旅程 , 我認為我們只能在每幾億年就能做到 。
so in fact , intergalactic space does contain all the prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge . any such cube , anywhere in the universe , could become the same kind of hub that we are , if the knowledge of how to do so were present there .	所以事實上 , 星際空間包含了所有宇宙中的任何一個基礎 , 可以成為我們所謂的 「 知識 」 的空間 。 無論如何在宇宙中的任何地方 , 都可以成為我們所謂的 「 知識 」 。
so we're not in a uniquely hospitable place .	所以我們不是一個獨特的穩定的地方 。
if intergalactic space is capable of creating an openended stream of explanations , then so is almost every other environment . so is the earth . so is a polluted earth .	如果有空間可以創造出一個開放式的解釋 , 幾乎所有其他環境 。 所以 , 地球就是地球 。 所以 , 地球是地球 。 所以這是地球 。
and the limiting factor , there and here , is not resources , because they're plentiful , but knowledge , which is scarce .	這裡有限的因素 , 不是資源 , 因為它們是很有用的 , 也是很有限的 。
now this cosmic knowledgebased view may and i think ought to make us feel very special . but it should also make us feel vulnerable , because it means that without the specific knowledge that's needed to survive the ongoing challenges of the universe , we won't survive them .	這個宇宙的科學知識 , 我認為應該讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為這意味著 , 沒有任何特殊的知識 , 應該讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為這意味著 , 沒有任何特殊知識 , 可以讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為它意味著沒有任何特殊知識 , 可以讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為它意味著沒有任何特殊的知識 , 可以讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為它意味著 , 沒有任何特殊的知識 , 可以讓我們感到脆弱 。
all it takes is for a supernova to go off a few light years away , and we'll all be dead !	只剩下幾光年 , 我們都死了 !
martin rees has recently written a book about our vulnerability to all sorts of things , from astrophysics , to scientific experiments gone wrong , and most importantly to terrorism with weapons of mass destruction .	馬丁最近寫了一本書 , 關於我們脆弱的各種事物 , 來自天體物理學 , 科學實驗出錯了 , 最重要的是恐怖主義和武器大規模毀滅 。
and he thinks that civilization has only a 50 percent chance of surviving this century .	他認為文明只有50%的機會可以存活下來 。
i think he's going to talk about that later in the conference .	我想他會在會議上談到這場演講 。
now i don't think that probability is the right category to discuss this issue in .	我不認為這個問題是正確的分類 , 可以討論這個議題 。
but i do agree with him about this . we can survive , and we can fail to survive .	但我同意他說的 , 我們可以生存下來 , 我們可以生存下來 。
but it depends not on chance , but on whether we create the relevant knowledge in time .	但它依賴於機會 , 但 , 不論我們如何創造出相關的知識 。
the danger is not at all unprecedented . species go extinct all the time .	危險是無所不在的 。 物種絕對是絕對的 。
civilizations end . the overwhelming majority of all species and all civilizations that have ever existed are now history .	文明終結 , 所有物種和所有文明已經存在的歷史 。
and if we want to be the exception to that , then logically our only hope is to make use of the one feature that distinguishes our species , and our civilization , from all the others namely , our special relationship with the laws of physics , our ability to create new explanations , new knowledge to be a hub of existence .	若我們想成為一個特殊的關係 , 我們的文明與物理的關係 , 我們的能力創造出新的解釋 , 新的知識 , 一個特殊的關係 , 來創造新的解釋 , 新的知識 , 一個特殊的關係 。
so let me now apply this to a current controversy , not because i want to advocate any particular solution , but just to illustrate the kind of thing i mean .	現在 , 讓我來談談我的意思 , 不是因為我想要提倡任何特定的解決方案 , 只是為了說明我的意思 。
and the controversy is global warming .	爭議是全球暖化 。
now , i'm a physicist , but i'm not the right kind of physicist . in regard to global warming , i'm just a layman . and the rational thing for a layman to do is to take seriously the prevailing scientific theory . and according to that theory , it's already too late to avoid a disaster .	我是物理學家 , 但是我不是正確的物理學家 , 但我不是物理學家 , 我是個物理學家 , 但是我不是正確的物理學家 。 根據這個理論 , 它已經太遲了 , 來避免災難 。
because if it's true that our best option at the moment is to prevent co2 emissions with something like the kyoto protocol , with its constraints on economic activity and its enormous cost of hundreds of billions of dollars or whatever it is , then that is already a disaster by any reasonable measure .	因為如果我們最好的選項 , 就是要預防二氧化碳排放 , 像是金屬基金會 , 及其它的限制 , 要預防二氧化碳排放 , 例如在經濟活動上 , 最好的選項是要預防二氧化碳排放 , 例如在經濟活動的限制 , 以及它的限制在經濟活動上 , 最好的選項是要預防二氧化碳排放量 。
and the actions that are advocated are not even purported to solve the problem , merely to postpone it by a little . so it's already too late to avoid it , and it probably has been too late to avoid it ever since before anyone realized the danger .	投票者的行動還不足以避免它 , 可能已經太遲了 , 甚至無法避免它 , 它可能已經太遲了 , 無法避免它 , 它可能已經太遲了 , 避免它可能已經太遲了 , 可能已經太遲了 , 無法避免它 , 可能已經太遲了 , 甚至無法避免它 。 所以它已經太遲了 , 甚至無法避免它 。 所以它已經太遲了 。
it was probably already too late in the 1970s , when the best available scientific theory was telling us that industrial emissions were about to precipitate a new ice age in which billions would die .	在1970年代末期 , 最好的科學理論告訴我們 , 工業排放會造成新的冰冰年齡 , 數十億人會死亡 。
now the lesson of that seems clear to me , and i don't know why it isn't informing public debate .	這對我來說很明顯 , 我不知道為什麼它不是公眾辯論 。
it is that we can't always know . when we know of an impending disaster , and how to solve it at a cost less than the cost of the disaster itself , then there's not going to be much argument , really .	這是我們無法一直知道的 。 當我們知道一個災難的代價時 , 會如何解決它的成本 , 比起災難的代價還要低 , 卻不會有爭議 。
but no precautions , and no precautionary principle , can avoid problems that we do not yet foresee .	但沒有預防措施 , 沒有預防措施 , 沒有預防措施 , 我們還沒有預防措施 。
hence , we need a stance of problemfixing , not just problemavoidance .	所以 , 我們需要一個穩定的問題 , 不是只是解決問題 。
and it's true that an ounce of prevention equals a pound of cure , but that's only if we know what to prevent .	一旦我們知道預防措施的預防措施 , 預防是如此 。
if you've been punched on the nose , then the science of medicine does not consist of teaching you how to avoid punches .	如果你一直在鼻子上 , 科學醫學不會教導你如何避免懲罰 。
if medical science stopped seeking cures and concentrated on prevention only , then it would achieve very little of either .	如果醫學科學停止尋求治癒和專注在預防的情況下 , 那它就會變得非常少 。
the world is buzzing at the moment with plans to force reductions in gas emissions at all costs .	世界正在不斷地在氣體排放中 , 計畫要減少氣體排放量的排放量 。
it ought to be buzzing with plans to reduce the temperature , and with plans to live at the higher temperature and not at all costs , but efficiently and cheaply . and some such plans exist , things like swarms of mirrors in space to deflect the sunlight away , and encouraging aquatic organisms to eat more carbon dioxide .	應該要分析這些計畫 , 例如 , 把陽光照射到陽光下 , 更高溫度 , 沒有任何成本 , 但有效率又便宜 , 還有一些計畫 , 例如在空間中空氣的溫度 , 將陽光照射出來 , 讓陽光消失 , 讓陽光消失 , 讓陽光飛行 , 讓陽光飛行 , 讓陽光飛行 , 讓陽光飛行 , 讓陽光飛行 , 讓陽光飛行 , 讓陽光飛行 , 讓陽光飛行 , 讓陽光飛行 , 讓陽光飛行 , 讓陽光飛行 , 讓陽光飛行 , 讓陽光飛行 , 讓陽光飛行 , 讓陽光飛行 , 讓陽光飛行 , 讓陽光飛行 , 讓陽光飛行 , 讓陽光飛行 , 讓陽光飛行 , 讓陽光飛行 , 讓陽光飛行 , 讓陽光飛行 , 讓陽光飛行 , 讓陽光飛行 , 讓陽光飛行 , 讓陽光飛行 ,
at the moment , these things are fringe research .	此時此刻 , 這些東西都是fring研究 。
they're not central to the human effort to face this problem , or problems in general .	他們不是中央人類努力面對這個問題 , 或一般的問題 。
and with problems that we are not aware of yet , the ability to put right not the sheer good luck of avoiding indefinitely is our only hope , not just of solving problems , but of survival .	對於我們所未知的問題 , 不只能解決問題 , 而是生存 , 而是生存 。
so take two stone tablets , and carve on them .	所以 , 拿兩隻石頭 , 帶著兩隻石頭 。
on one of them , carve: " problems are soluble . "	其中一面 , 卡路: 「 問題是固定的 。 」
and on the other one carve: " problems are inevitable . "	另一方面 , 「 問題是不可避免的 。 」
how can a struggling country break out of poverty if it's trapped in a system of bad rules ? economist paul romer unveils a bold idea: " charter cities , " cityscale administrative zones governed by a coalition of nations .	要如何解決貧窮的問題 ? 經濟學家保羅爾•羅默默思想: 「 查爾斯•羅弗斯 」 一個 「 城市 」 的城市 , 經濟學家保羅爾•羅默所說: 「 查爾斯特市 」 , 城市是 「 大城市城市 」 , 經濟學家保羅•羅默所說的是 「 大城市 」 城市 , 經濟學家保羅•羅姆提出一個大膽的想法: 「 查爾斯特城市 」 。
business , culture , economics , global issues , politics	商業、文化、經濟、全球議題 , 政治 。
paul romer's radical idea: charter cities	保羅•羅馬的主題是:荷蘭城市 。
take a look at this picture .	看看這張照片 。
it poses a very fascinating puzzle for us .	這對我們來說是個非常迷人的謎題 。
these african students are doing their homework under streetlights at the airport in the capital city because they don't have any electricity at home .	這些非洲學生在家裡做作業 , 因為他們沒有任何電力在家裡 。
now , i haven't met these particular students , but i've met students like them .	我沒有遇過這些學生 , 但我遇到像他們這樣的學生 。
let's just pick one for example , the one in the green shirt .	咱們來舉個例子 , 綠色的衣服 。
let's give him a name , too: nelson .	我們給他一個名字:nelson 。
i'll bet nelson has a cellphone .	我將tnelson有手機 。
so here is the puzzle .	這是謎題 。
why is it that nelson has access to a cuttingedge technology , like the cellphone , but doesn't have access to a 100yearold technology for generating electric light in the home ?	為什麼 , 尼爾森可以接觸到一個一百歲的科技 , 可以在家裡發電燈 ?
now , in a word , the answer is " rules . "	在一個字中 , 答案是 「 規則 」 。
bad rules can prevent the kind of winwin solution that's available when people can bring new technologies in and make them available to someone like nelson .	糟糕的規則可以防止愛滋病的解決方案 , 讓人們可以預防愛爾森的情況 。
what kinds of rules ?	什麼樣的規則 ?
the electric company in this nation operates under a rule , which says that it has to sell electricity at a very low , subsidized price in fact , a price that is so low it loses money on every unit that it sells .	這個國家的電力公司在一個非常低的價格下降低了價格 , 價格很低 , 價格很低 , 價格很低 , 價格很低 , 價格很低 , 價格很低 , 價格很低 , 價格很低 , 價格很低 。
so it has neither the resources , nor the incentives , to hook up many other users .	所以 , 不管是資源 , 或獎勵 , 都能把許多其他使用者使用 。
the president wanted to change this rule .	總統想要改變這個規則 。
he's seen that it's possible to have a different set of rules , rules where businesses earn a small profit , so they have an incentive to sign up more customers .	他發現 , 有些規則 , 商業賺錢的價格很高 , 所以他們有一種不同的規則 , 規則 , 商業賺錢的價格很高 , 所以他們有獎勵來標示更多客戶 。
that's the kind of rules that the cellphone company that nelson purchases his telephony from operates under .	這是一種規則 , nelson購買他的手機公司 , nelson購買了他的電話公司 。
the president has seen how those rules worked well .	總統看到這些規則如何運作 。
so he tried to change the rules for pricing on electricity , but ran into a firestorm of protest from businesses and consumers who wanted to preserve the existing subsidized rates .	所以他試圖改變規則 , 用電力的規則 , 但從商業和消費者中 , 消費者想要保存保存的代價 。
so he was stuck with rules that prevented him from letting the winwin solution help his country .	所以 , 他堅持規則 , 讓他無法讓他贏得解決方案 , 來協助他的國家 。
and nelson is stuck studying under the streetlights .	nelson在街道上被困在街道上 。
the real challenge then , is to try to figure out how we can change rules .	真正的挑戰是 , 試圖找出我們如何改變規則 。
are there some rules we can develop for changing rules ?	我們是否有一些規則 , 來改變規則 ?
i want to argue that there is a general abstract insight that we can make practical , which is that , if we can give more choices to people , and more choices to leaders who , in many countries , are also people .	我想說的是 , 一個普遍的抽象概念 , 如果我們能讓更多的選擇給人民 , 更多的選擇 , 更多的選擇 , 和更多的國家 , 也是人民 。
but , it's useful to present the opposition between these two .	但 , 這兩者之間的反對 。
because the kind of choice you might want to give to a leader , a choice like giving the president the choice to raise prices on electricity , takes away a choice that people in the economy want .	因為你可能想要給領袖的選擇 , 比如給領袖的選擇 , 像是給領袖的選擇 , 像是給領袖的選擇 , 像是給領袖的選擇 , 像是給領袖的選擇 , 像是給領袖的選擇 , 像是給領袖的選擇 。
they want the choice to be able to continue consuming subsidized electric power .	他們想要選擇能夠繼續消費能源的電力 。
so if you give just to one side or the other , you'll have tension or friction .	所以 , 如果你只給一個方塊或摩擦 , 你就會有緊張或摩擦力 。
but if we can find ways to give more choices to both , that will give us a set of rules for changing rules that get us out of traps .	但如果我們能找到方法 , 來改變規則 , 會讓我們脫離陷阱 。
now , nelson also has access to the internet .	nelson也能取得網路 。
and he says that if you want to see the damaging effects of rules , the ways that rules can keep people in the dark , look at the pictures from nasa of the earth at night .	他說 , 如果你想看到大規模的破壞法則可以讓人們在黑暗中看到我們在黑暗中看到的影像 , 像是在黑暗的照片 , 看來自美國太空總署的照片 。
in particular check out asia .	特別檢查出亞洲
if you zoom in here , you can see north korea , in outline here , which is like a black hole compared to its neighbors .	如果你放大到這裡 , 你可以看到北韓 , 在這裡 , 看起來像黑洞相比它的鄰居 。
now , you won't be surprised to learn that the rules in north korea keep people there in the dark .	現在 , 你不會很驚訝 , 北韓的規則則會讓人們在黑暗中 。
but it is important to recognize that north korea and south korea started out with identical sets of rules in both the sense of laws and regulations , but also in the deeper senses of understandings , norms , culture , values and beliefs .	但 , 很重要的是 , 要知道北韓和南韓的法律和法律規則 , 都有法律和規範的規則 , 同時也更深入了解、文化、價值觀和信念 。
when they separated , they made choices that led to very divergent paths for their sets of rules .	當他們分離時 , 他們做出選擇 , 導致了非常多樣性的道路 。
so we can change we as humans can change the rules that we use to interact with each other , for better , or for worse .	所以 , 我們可以改變我們人類的規則 , 可以改變我們所使用的規則 , 更好、更好 , 或更糟 。
now let's look at another region , the caribbean .	現在我們來看看另一個區域 , 加勒比海 。
zoom in on haiti , in outline here .	在海地 , 在海地 , 在海地上網 。
haiti is also dark , compared to its neighbor here , the dominican republic , which has about the same number of residents .	海地也暗 , 相較於鄰居的鄰居 , 大量的居民 , 和鄰居共和國 。
both of these countries are dark compared to puerto rico , which has half as many residents as either haiti or the dominican republic .	這兩種國家都與青少年相比 , 如同居民、巴黎 , 甚至還有半數的居民 , 像是海地或多數民族 。
what haiti warns us is that rules can be bad because governments are weak .	海地警告 , 我們的規則是壞的 , 因為政府很弱 。
it's not just that the rules are bad because the government is too strong and oppressive , as in north korea .	不只規則是糟糕的 , 因為政府太強大、壓迫 , 在北韓 。
so that if we want to create environments with good rules , we can't just tear down .	所以 , 如果我們想要創造環境有好的規則 , 我們就不能只是淚水而已 。
we've got to find ways to build up , as well .	我們必須找到方法來建構 。
now , china dramatically demonstrates both the potential and the challenges of working with rules .	現在 , 中國顯然地展示了潛力與規則的潛力與規則 。
back in the beginning of the data presented in this chart , china was the world's hightechnology leader .	在這個圖表中 , 中國是世界高科技領袖 。
chinese had pioneered technologies like steel , printing , gunpowder .	中國人有先進的科技 , 像是鋼鐵、印刷、火車 。
but the chinese never adopted , at least in that period , effective rules for encouraging the spread of those ideas a profit motive that could have encouraged the spread .	但中國人從來沒有採用 , 至少 , 在那段期間 , 有效的規則 , 能鼓勵傳播這些想法的傳播 。
and they soon adopted rules which slowed down innovation and cut china off from the rest of the world .	他們很快的採取規則 , 慢慢下來創新 , 並把中國從世界各地移除 。
so as other countries in the world innovated , in the sense both of developing newer technologies , but also developing newer rules , the chinese were cut off from those advances .	所以 , 在其他國家 , 中國人都從這些進步發展出新的規則 , 中國人從這些進步中發展出新的規則 。
income there stayed stagnant , as it zoomed ahead in the rest of the world .	收入保持穩定 , 讓世界各地的保持穩定 。
this next chart looks at more recent data .	下一張圖表是最近的數據 。
it plots income , average income in china as a percentage of average income in the united states .	中國的平均收入是美國的平均收入的平均收入 。
in the '50s and '60s you can see that it was hovering at about three percent .	在50年代和60年代 , 你可以看到 , 大約有三分之三 。
but then in the late '70s something changed .	但在1970年代末期 , 改變了 。
growth took off in china . the chinese started catching up very quickly with the united states .	中國長大 , 中國開始捕捉到中國 , 中國開始很快地抓到美國 。
if you go back to the map at night , you can get a clue to the process that lead to the dramatic change in rules in china .	如果你回到地圖上 , 你就能得到一個線索 , 來到中國的大規模改變規則 。
the brightest spot in china , which you can see on the edge of the outline here , is hong kong .	中國最亮的點 , 你可以看到在上面的邊緣 , 就是香港 。
hong kong was a small bit of china that , for most of the 20th century , operated under a very different set of rules than the rest of mainland china rules that were copied from working market economies of the time , and administered by the british .	香港是個小小的中國規則 , 在20世紀 , 由英國的規則 , 由英國而來 , 中國的規則完全不同 。
in the 1950s , hong kong was a place where millions of people could go , from the mainland , to start in jobs like sewing shirts , making toys .	在1950年代 , 香港是個地方數百萬人可以從主角開始 , 像是縫衣衣、製作玩具 。
but , to get on a process of increasing income , increasing skills led to very rapid growth there .	但 , 要加入越來越多的進步 , 越來越多的技能能快速成長 。
hong kong was also the model which leaders like deng xiaoping could copy , when they decided to move all of the mainland towards the market model .	香港也是模型 , 當他們決定要搬到市場模式時 , 他們決定要移動所有大陸 , 到市場模式 。
but deng xiaoping instinctively understood the importance of offering choices to his people .	但 , 針對他人的重要性 , 要明白的重要性 , 會帶來選擇的重要性 。
so instead of forcing everyone in china to shift immediately to the market model , they proceeded by creating some special zones that could do , in a sense , what britain did: make the opportunity to go work with the market rules available to the people who wanted to opt in there .	所以 , 與市場規則相反 , 沒有任何人在中國轉移到市場規則 , 讓機會可以去市場規則 , 讓大家可以去做 , 去做市場規則 , 讓大家可以去工作 , 去市場規則 , 才能和市場規則交易 。
so they created four special economic zones around hong kong: zones where chinese could come and work , and cities grew up very rapidly there ; also zones where foreign firms could come in and make things .	所以 , 他們創造了四個特殊的經濟區塊 , 在那裡 , 中國人可以來到那裡 , 城市長大 , 很快地 , 都市長大 , 都市長大 , 都市長大 , 都市長大 。
one of the zones next to hong kong has a city called shenzhen .	香港的一個城市叫做nzhen 。
in that city there is a taiwanese firm that made the iphone that many of you have , and they made it with labor from chinese who moved there to shenzhen .	在這個城市裡 , 有一個塔iphone , 裡面有許多人的工廠 , 他們用勞動力 , 用勞動力 , 讓iphone和中國人一起工作 。
so after the four special zones , there were 14 coastal cites that were open in the same sense , and eventually demonstrated successes in these places that people could opt in to , that they flocked to because of the advantages they offered .	所以 , 在四個特殊區塊裡 , 那裡有14個海岸線 , 這些地方的人們可以採取行動 , 最終會成功 , 這些地方的人們可以採取行動 , 因為他們所擁有的優勢 。
demonstrated successes there led to a consensus for a move toward the market model for the entire economy .	展示成功的成功 , 讓整個經濟的成功 。
now the chinese example shows us several points .	中國的例子顯示了我們幾點 。
one is: preserve choices for people .	第一:保存選擇 。
two: operate on the right scale .	第二:操作正確的規模 。
if you try to change the rules in a village , you could do that , but a village would be too small to get the kinds of benefits you can get if you have millions of people all working under good rules .	如果你試著改變規則 , 你就能做到 , 但村落的村子太小了 , 你就能做到 , 但村子的村子太小了 , 你就能做到 , 但村子的村子太小了 , 你就能做到這一點 , 只要有數百萬人在良好的規則上工作 。
on the other hand , the nation is too big .	另一方面 , 國家太大了 。
if you try to change the rules in the nation , you can't give some people a chance to hold back , see how things turn out , and let others zoom ahead and try the new rules .	如果你試著改變規則 , 你不能給一些人一個機會來回顧 , 看看事情如何轉變 , 讓其他人有機會 , 再看看如何 , 讓其他的規則 。
but cities give you this opportunity to create new places , with new rules that people can opt in to .	但城市給你機會創造新的規則 , 讓人們可以選擇 。
and they're large enough to get all of the benefits that we can have when millions of us work together under good rules .	當數百萬人一起工作時 , 我們能得到所有益處 , 如同我們所能擁有的好處 。
so the proposal is that we conceive of something called a charter city .	因此 , 建議是我們所謂的 「 大城市 」 。
we start with a charter that specifies all the rules required to attract the people who we'll need to build the city .	我們從一系列的規則開始 , 規定所有規則都需要吸引人 , 才能吸引我們所需的城市 。
we'll need to attract the investors who will build out the infrastructure the power system , the roads , the port , the airport , the buildings .	我們需要吸引投資者 , 把投資者推出基礎建設電力系統、道路、機場、建築物 。
you'll need to attract firms , who will come hire the people who move there first .	你需要吸引公司 , 誰會來僱用那些搬到那裡的人 。
and you'll need to attract families , the residents who will come and live there permanently , raise their children , get an education for their children , and get their first job .	你會需要吸引家庭 , 居住家人 , 養育他們的孩子 , 取得他們的教育 , 讓他們的第一份工作 。
with that charter , people will move there .	有了這個章節 , 人們會搬到那裡 。
the city can be built .	城市可以建造 。
and we can scale this model .	我們可以擴展這個模型 。
we can go do it over and over again .	我們可以再一次地做一次 。
to make it work , we need good rules . we've already discussed that .	為了讓它運作 , 我們需要好的規則 。 我們已經討論了 。
those are captured in the charter .	這些都是被捕捉到的 。
we also need the choices for people .	我們也需要選擇給人們 。
that's really built into the model if we allow for the possibility of building cities on uninhabited land .	這實在是建造城市在未被建設的城市 。
you start from uninhabited territory .	你從未被居住的領土開始 。
people can come live under the new charter , but no one is forced to live under it .	人們可以生活在新圖表 , 但沒有人被迫活在下面 。
the final thing we need are choices for leaders .	最後我們需要的是選擇領導者 。
and , to achieve the kind of choices we want for leaders we need to allow for the potential for partnerships between nations: cases where nations work together , in effect , de facto , the way china and britain worked together to build , first a little enclave of the market model , and then scale it throughout china .	為了達成目標 , 我們想要領導者的需求 , 我們需要讓大家能參與國家之間的關係 , 例如 , 中國和英國一起合作 , 建立第一個小小的市場模型 , 並且在中國和英國之間合作 。
in a sense , britain , inadvertently , through its actions in hong kong , did more to reduce world poverty than all the aid programs that we've undertaken in the last century .	在某種意義上 , 英國很不可思議 , 英國 , 不幸地 , 透過它的行動 , 才能減少世界貧窮 , 比所有援助計畫都還要多 。
so if we allow for these kind of partnerships to replicate this again , we can get those kinds of benefits scaled throughout the world .	所以如果我們能讓這些合作夥伴再次重複 , 我們就能得到這些全球各地的益處 。
in some cases this will involve a delegation of responsibility , a delegation of control from one country to another to take over certain kinds of administrative responsibilities .	在某些情況下 , 該國有責任性 , 來自一個國家的負責任 , 由一個國家來取代某些案例 , 負責任 。
now , when i say that , some of you are starting to think , " well , is this just bringing back colonialism ? "	現在 , 當我說 , 你們有些人開始想: 「 嗯 , 這只是把殖民主義帶回殖民主義嗎 ? 」
it's not . but it's important to recognize that the kind of emotions that come up when we start to think about these things , can get in the way , can make us pull back , can shut down our ability , and our interest in trying to explore new ideas .	不是 , 但很重要的是 , 當我們開始思考這些東西時 , 可以把我們的能力帶回去 , 同時也能改變我們的能力 , 同時也能讓我們回顧 , 能讓我們退出 , 才能讓我們退出 , 去探索新的點子 。
why is this not like colonialism ?	為什麼這不是殖民主義 ?
the thing that was bad about colonialism , and the thing which is residually bad in some of our aid programs , is that it involved elements of coercion and condescension .	關於殖民主義的差異 , 和我們對殖民主義的差異很糟 , 其實我們還在一些援助計畫中 , 正是關於殖民主義的影響 , 且在我們的援助計畫中 , 很糟糕的是 , 它涉及了協調和執行 。
this model is all about choices , both for leaders and for the people who will live in these new places .	這個模式是所有的選擇 , 包括領袖 , 和那些住在這些新地方的人 。
and , choice is the antidote to coercion and condescension .	選擇是 , 選擇反對會議和混亂 。
so let's talk about how this could play out in practice .	咱們來談談如何在練習中扮演 。
let's take a particular leader , raul castro , who is the leader of cuba .	讓我們拿一個特定領袖 , 拉克斯特 , 他是古巴的領導者 。
it must have occurred to castro that he has the chance to do for cuba what deng xiaoping did for china , but he doesn't have a hong kong there on the island in cuba .	牠必須有機會去做古巴 , 為了中國 , 但他沒有一個香港 , 在那裡 , 牠有機會去做古巴 。
he does , though , have a little bit of light down in the south that has a very special status .	不過 , 在南方有一個非常特別的地位 。
there is a zone there , around guantanamo bay , where a treaty gives the united states administrative responsibility for a piece of land that's about twice the size of manhattan .	有一塊土地 , 有一塊土地大約是曼哈頓的兩倍大小 。
castro goes to the prime minister of canada and says , " look , the yankees have a terrible pr problem .	加拿大的總理 , 說: 「 看 , 金恩總理會說: 「 看 , 黃金會很糟糕 。
they want to get out .	他們想出去 。
why don't you , canada , take over ?	為什麼你不加拿大 , 加拿大 ?

they also totally get the idea that in some instances they can make more credible promises to longterm investors the kind of investors who will come build the port , build the roads , in a new city they can make more credible promises if they do it along with a partner nation .	他們也很清楚地知道 , 若他們能做出更有信任的承諾 , 就能讓更有信任的承諾 , 在一個新的城市中 , 他們能讓更有信任的承諾 , 能讓更多客戶的承諾 , 在一個新的城市中 , 讓他們能更有信任地承諾 。

well , throughout the world , if we look at the lights at night , the one thing that's misleading is that , visually , it looks like most of the world is already built out .	在世界各地 , 如果我們看看燈光在夜晚 , 它看起來像世界上大部分都已經建造出來了 。

and if these are cities governed by good rules , they can be cities where people are safe from crime , safe from disease and bad sanitation , where people have a chance to get a job .	如果這些城市被良好的規則所影響 , 他們可以成為城市 , 讓人們有機會去取得工作機會 , 取得工作 。

turns out singapore and hong kong are cities that made huge gains on the value of the land that they owned when they got started .	後來 , 新加坡和香港是城市 , 製造了巨大的穀物 , 讓它們能在當地的土地上產生巨大的價值 。
you could use the gains on the value of the land to pay for things like the police , the courts , but the school system and the health care system too , which make this a more attractive place to live , makes this a place where people have higher incomes which , incidentally , makes the land more valuable .	你可以用在土地上的錢 , 像是警察、法庭、學校系統 , 以及健康照護體制 , 讓這個地方變得更有吸引力 , 讓土地變得更有吸引力 , 讓土地變得更有吸引力 。
so the incentives for the people helping to construct this zone and build it , and set up the basic rules , go very much in the right direction .	所以鼓勵人們幫助建構這個區塊並建構這個區塊並建構這個區塊並建立這個區塊並建立這個區塊並建立這個區塊並建立這個區塊並建立這個區塊並建立這個區塊並建構這個區塊並建立基礎規則
