let me conclude with this picture .	讓我結論這張照片 。
the reason we can be so well off , even though there is so many people on earth , is because of the power of ideas .	我們之所以如此 , 儘管地球上有很多人 , 是因為有許多人的力量 。
we can share ideas with other people , and when they discover them , they share with us .	我們可以分享點子 , 和其他人分享點子 , 當他們發現他們 , 他們和我們分享 。
it's not like scarce objects , where sharing means we each get less .	它不像稀有的物品 , 分享的意思是 , 我們每一步都比較少了 。
when we share ideas we all get more .	當我們分享點子時 , 我們都能得到更多 。
when we think about ideas in that way , we usually think about technologies .	當我們想到這些想法時 , 我們通常會想到科技 。
but there is another class of ideas: the rules that govern how we interact with each other ; rules like , let's have a tax system that supports a research university that gives away certain kinds of knowledge for free .	但還有其他的規則:規則 , 我們有不同的規則 , 例如 , 我們有一系列的規則 , 來說明我們如何互動的規則 , 例如 , 我們有一個稅制系統 , 來協助一個研究大學 , 來提供某些知識免費 。
let's have a system where we have ownership of land that is registered in a government office , that people can pledge as collateral .	讓我們有一個系統 , 在政府辦公室裡 , 人們可以聚集在政府辦公室 。
if we can keep innovating on our space of rules , and particularly innovate in the sense of coming up with rules for changing rules , so we don't get stuck with bad rules , then we can keep moving progress forward and truly make the world a better place , so that people like nelson and his friends don't have to study any longer under the streetlights . thank you .	如果我們可以繼續進步 , 讓世界變得更好 , 這樣 , 像尼爾森和他的朋友不需要再多進步 , 讓世界變得更好 。 謝謝 。 謝謝 。
genomics pioneer craig venter takes a break from his epic roundtheworld expedition to talk about the millions of genes his team has discovered so far in its quest to map the ocean’s biodiversity .	基因學家先生多樣性 , 他的基因學家先生多樣性 , 他的基因學家先生多樣性 , 從他的團隊發現了 , 遠遠超過了數百萬個基因組成員 。
dna , biosphere , biotech , entrepreneur , genetics , invention , oceans , science , technology	dna、生物科技、生物學、發明、海洋、科學技術 。
craig venter on dna and the sea	在dna和海面上 ,
at the break , i was asked by several people about my comments about the aging debate .	一開始 , 我被問到一些人關於辯論的評論 。
and this will be my only comment on it .	這是我唯一的評論 。
and that is , i understand that optimists greatly outlive pessimists .	那就是 , 我知道樂觀主義者很悲觀主義者 。
what i'm going to tell you about in my 18 minutes is how we're about to switch from reading the genetic code to the first stages of beginning to write the code ourselves .	在我十八分鐘之內 , 我們要從讀基因編碼到第一階段 , 開始寫程式碼 。
it's only 10 years ago this month when we published the first sequence of a freeliving organism , that of haemophilus influenzae .	僅僅十年前 , 我們發表了第一段序列的免疫感染 , 叫做 「 流感疫苗 」 。
that took a genome project from 13 years down to four months .	從13年到4個月 , 完成了基因組計畫 。
we can now do that same genome project in the order of two to eight hours .	我們現在可以做同樣的基因組計畫 , 花了兩到八個小時 。
so in the last decade , a large number of genomes have been added: most human pathogens , a couple of plants , several insects and several mammals , including the human genome .	所以 , 在過去十年 , 大量的基因組成了人類的基因組 , 包括人類基因組 , 包括人類的基因組 。
genomics at this stage of the thinking from a little over 10 years ago was , by the end of this year , we might have between three and five genomes sequenced ; it's on the order of several hundred .	在這十年前的基因組定序 , 我們可能有三到五個基因組組序列 , 這是數百個基因組 。
we just got a grant from the gordon and betty moore foundation to sequence 130 genomes this year , as a side project from environmental organisms .	我們剛剛從gordon和betmardon和貝蒂莫爾基金會找到了這一年的一份基因組 , 它是環保生物的一部分 。
so the rate of reading the genetic code has changed .	所以 , 閱讀基因碼的速度已經改變了 。
but as we look , what's out there , we've barely scratched the surface on what is available on this planet .	但當我們看 , 究竟到底是什麼 , 我們在地球上沒有什麼東西 。
most people don't realize it , because they're invisible , but microbes make up about a half of the earth's biomass , whereas all animals only make up about one onethousandth of all the biomass .	大多數人並不了解它 , 因為它們是可見的 , 但微生物的數量只佔據地球生物物質的一半 。
and maybe it's something that people in oxford don't do very often , but if you ever make it to the sea , and you swallow a mouthful of seawater , keep in mind that each milliliter has about a million bacteria and on the order of 10 million viruses .	也許 , 牛津人並不常常這麼做 , 但如果你把海水帶到海水裡 , 每一百萬個細菌和一百萬個細菌 , 都有大約一百萬個細菌 , 一百萬個細菌 。
less than 5 , 000 microbial species have been characterized as of two years ago , and so we decided to do something about it .	超過5000種微生物物種已經被性格化了 , 所以我們決定要做點什麼 。
and we started the sorcerer ii expedition , where we were , as with great oceanographic expeditions , trying to sample the ocean every 200 miles .	然後我們開始採用大型的海洋攝影機 , 試圖將海洋景象放大 , 每200英里就要採用大量的海洋 。
we started in bermuda for our test project , then moved up to halifax , working down the u . s . east coast , the caribbean sea , the panama canal , through to the galapagos , then across the pacific , and we're in the process now of working our way across the indian ocean .	我們開始在加勒比海海岸 , 加勒比海 , 加勒比海 , 加勒比海 , 加勒比海 , 加勒比海 , 加勒比海 , 加勒比海 , 加勒比海 , 加勒比海 , 加勒比海 , 加勒比海 , 都在美國東岸 。
it's very tough duty ; we're doing this on a sailing vessel , in part to help excite young people about going into science .	這是非常艱難的 , 因為我們在一艘帆船上做 , 讓年輕人去探索科學 。
the experiments are incredibly simple .	實驗非常簡單 。
we just take seawater and we filter it , and we collect different size organisms on different filters , and then take their dna back to our lab in rockville , where we can sequence a hundred million letters of the genetic code every 24 hours .	我們只要把海水拿到我們的實驗室裡 , 將它們的dna放回我們的實驗室 , 在岩洞裡 , 我們就能收集不同的尺寸 , 每24小時就能收集不同的小生物 。
and with doing this , we've made some amazing discoveries .	這樣做 , 我們做了一些很棒的發現 。
for example , it was thought that the visual pigments that are in our eyes there was only one or two organisms in the environment that had these same pigments .	舉例來說 , 認為我們眼睛中的視覺色素 , 只有一個或兩個有機體在環境中有著相同的顏色 。
it turns out , almost every species in the upper parts of the ocean in warm parts of the world have these same photoreceptors , and use sunlight as the source of their energy and communication .	結果發現 , 幾乎所有物種都在海洋中 , 在海洋中 , 有著相同的光源 , 牠們的能量和溝通 。
from one site , from one barrel of seawater , we discovered 1 . 3 million new genes and as many as 50 , 000 new species .	從一桶海水裡 , 我們發現了130萬個新的基因 , 和五萬個新物種 。
we've extended this to the air now with a grant from the sloan foundation .	我們已經把這個從地底下的空氣拿出來了 。
we're measuring how many viruses and bacteria all of us are breathing in and out every day , particularly on airplanes or closed auditoriums .	我們測量了多少病毒和細菌 , 每天都有呼吸 , 特別是在飛機或閉上 。
we filter through some simple apparatuses ; we collect on the order of a billion microbes from just a day filtering on top of a building in new york city .	我們收集了一些簡單的應用程式 , 我們收集了數十億微生物 , 僅僅是紐約市的一棟大樓 。
and we're in the process of sequencing all that at the present time .	我們正處於這個階段的過程中 。
just on the data collection side , just where we are through the galapagos , we're finding that almost every 200 miles , we see tremendous diversity in the samples in the ocean .	僅僅在資料集中 , 我們在海洋中看到了巨大的多樣性 , 大約在200英里外 , 我們發現幾乎每200英里 。
some of these make logical sense , in terms of different temperature gradients .	在不同溫度的層面上 , 不同的溫度會降低 。
so this is a satellite photograph based on temperatures red being warm , blue being cold and we found there's a tremendous difference between the warm water samples and the cold water samples , in terms of abundant species .	這是一張衛星拍攝的照片 , 溫度是紅色的溫度紅色 , 溫度是紅色的 , 溫度是紅色的 , 溫度是紅色的 , 溫度是紅色的 , 溫度是紅色的 , 溫度是紅色的 , 溫度是紅色的 , 溫度是紅色的 。
the other thing that surprised us quite a bit is these photoreceptors detect different wavelengths of light , and we can predict that based on their amino acid sequence .	另外一件令人驚訝的是這些相片的微小光線可以預測根據它們的氨基酸序列來預測
and these vary tremendously from region to region .	從區域到區域 , 都很大 。
maybe not surprisingly , in the deep ocean , where it's mostly blue , the photoreceptors tend to see blue light .	或許不令人驚訝的是 , 在深海中 , 最藍光的部分是藍色光線 。
when there's a lot of chlorophyll around , they see a lot of green light .	當那裡有許多綠光時 , 它們會看到很多綠光 。
but they vary even more , possibly moving towards infrared and ultraviolet in the extremes .	但它們甚至更有可能在極端中移動到紅外線和紫外線 。
just to try and get an assessment of what our gene repertoire was , we assembled all the data including all of ours thus far from the expedition , which represents more than half of all the gene data on the planet and it totaled around 29 million genes .	為了要嘗試 , 了解我們的基因資料包含我們所有的資料 , 我們組合所有資料包含了全部的基因資料 , 包含了我們全部的基因資料 , 將所有資料包含在地球上 , 超過一半的基因資料 , 包含了超過一半的基因資料 。
and we tried to put these into gene families to see what these discoveries are: are we just discovering new members of known families , or are we discovering new families ?	我們試圖把這些發現新成員 , 看看這些發現的新成果 , 我們是否發現新成員的新成員 , 或是我們發現新的家庭 ?
and it turns out we have about 50 , 000 major gene families , but every new sample we take in the environment adds in a linear fashion to these new families .	結果發現 , 我們有大約五萬個主要的基因家庭 , 但是我們在每種新品種的樣本中 , 都在對這些新品種類的新家庭組合 。
so we're at the earliest stages of discovery about basic genes , components and life on this planet .	所以 , 我們在這個星球上最早期的階段 , 發現了基本的基因 , 和生命的基礎基因 。
when we look at the socalled evolutionary tree , we're up on the upper righthand corner with the animals .	當我們觀察所謂的演化樹 , 我們就在右手邊的角落 。
of those roughly 29 million genes , we only have around 24 , 000 in our genome .	大約290萬個基因組中 , 我們只有2億個基因組 。
and if you take all animals together , we probably share less than 30 , 000 and probably maybe a dozen or more thousand different gene families .	如果你把所有的動物聚在一起 , 我們可能有超過三萬個 , 可能是一千個不同的基因家庭 。
i view that these genes are now not only the design components of evolution .	我認為這些基因不僅是演化的設計元素 。
and we think in a genecentric view maybe going back to richard dawkins' ideas than in a genomecentric view , which are different constructs of these gene components .	我們認為 , 在基因組合中 , 這種基因組合的不同結構 , 會造成這些基因組合 。
synthetic dna , the ability to synthesize dna , has changed at sort of the same pace that dna sequencing has over the last decade or two , and is getting very rapid and very cheap .	合成dna組成dna序列 , 在過去的十年或兩年間 , 基因組成dna序列的速度非常便宜 。
our first thought about synthetic genomics came when we sequenced the second genome back in 1995 , and that from mycoplasma genitalium .	我們首先想到合成基因組 , 在1995年 , 基因組學會出現在1995年 , 當時是基因組學 。
and we have really nice tshirts that say , you know , " i heart my genitalium . "	我們有很棒的t恤 , 說: 「 我心我的生殖器 。 」
this is actually just a microorganism .	這其實只是一個微生物 。
but it has roughly 500 genes .	但它大約有500個基因 。
haemophilus had 1 , 800 genes .	漢菲爾斯有1800個基因 。
and we simply asked the question , if one species needs 800 , another 500 , is there a smaller set of genes that might comprise a minimal operating system ?	我們只問這個問題 , 如果一個物種需要800 , 500 , 另一個500 , 另一個500 , 另一個500 , 另一個500 , 另一個500 , 一個比較小的基因會產生最小的基因嗎 ?
so we started doing transposon mutagenesis .	所以 , 我們開始做轉變的突破 。
transposons are just small pieces of dna that randomly insert in the genetic code .	翻譯只是小小的dna , 在基因編碼中被遺傳密碼 。
and if they insert in the middle of the gene , they disrupt its function .	如果他們在基因中分裂 , 它們會破壞它的功能 。
so we made a map of all the genes that could take transposon insertions and we called those " nonessential genes . "	所以我們做了一幅地圖 , 把所有基因的基因放進去 , 我們稱之為 「 不健康的基因 」 。
but it turns out the environment is very critical for this , and you can only define an essential or nonessential gene based on exactly what's in the environment .	但結果發現 , 環境是非常關鍵的 , 你只能定義一個基本或不健康的基因 , 只能定義一個基本或不健康的基因 。
we also tried to take a more directly intellectual approach with the genomes of 13 related organisms , and we tried to compare all of those , to see what they had in common .	我們也嘗試用更直接的智慧方法 , 用一種方式 , 來找出兩者之間的基因組 , 我們嘗試將它們的基因組結合起來 。
and we got these overlapping circles . and we found only 173 genes common to all 13 organisms .	我們發現 , 只有173個基因共通 , 只有173個基因通通 , 只有173個基因通通 。
the pool expanded a little bit if we ignored one intracellular parasite ; it expanded even more when we looked at core sets of genes of around 310 or so .	如果我們忽略了一顆微生物 , 它就擴大了 , 只要我們忽略了一顆基因 , 大約310 , 就會擴張 。
so we think that we can expand or contract genomes , depending on your point of view here , to maybe 300 to 400 genes from the minimal of 500 .	所以我們認為我們可以擴張或合約300個基因組 , 依據你的觀點來看 , 大概300到400個基因組 , 依據你的觀點 , 或許300到400個基因組 。
the only way to prove these ideas was to construct an artificial chromosome with those genes in them , and we had to do this in a cassettebased fashion .	唯一能證明這些想法的方法是要建立一個人造染色體 , 並且我們必須在基礎上做這種事 。
we found that synthesizing accurate dna in large pieces was extremely difficult .	我們發現合成dna是非常困難的 。
ham smith and clyde hutchison , my colleagues on this , developed an exciting new method that allowed us to synthesize a 5 , 000base pair virus in only a twoweek period that was 100 percent accurate , in terms of its sequence and its biology .	哈姆•史密斯 , 和我的同事 , 開發了一個令人興奮的新方法 , 讓我們能合成5 , 000個鹼基 , 只有兩週期內 , 它的序列和生物學 。
it was a quite exciting experiment when we just took the synthetic piece of dna , injected it in the bacteria and all of a sudden , that dna started driving the production of the virus particles that turned around and then killed the bacteria .	這是一個令人振奮的實驗 , 我們剛完成了dna , 將病毒粒子轉換成dna , 然後殺害細菌 。
this was not the first synthetic virus a polio virus had been made a year before but it was only one tenthousandth as active and it took three years to do .	這不是第一個合成病毒的病毒在一年前被做過 , 但只有一個小兒麻痺症病毒 , 只有一個十分之一的病毒 , 才剛才完成 。
this is a cartoon of the structure of phi x 174 .	這是phix174的漫畫 。
this is a case where the software now builds its own hardware , and that's the notions that we have with biology .	這是個軟體現在正在建構它自己的硬體 , 這就是我們和生物學有關的概念 。
people immediately jump to concerns about biological warfare , and i had recent testimony before a senate committee , and a special committee the u . s . government has set up to review this area .	人們立刻開始評估這個區域 , 特別的委員會委員會在委員會議員 , 特別委員會在委員會議員 , 委員會在參議院委員會委員會議員 。
and i think it's important to keep reality in mind , versus what happens with people's imaginations .	我認為 , 要讓人們的想像力是很重要的 , 會發生什麼事 。
basically , any virus that's been sequenced today that genome can be made .	基本上 , 任何病毒都是由基因組所組成的 。
and people immediately freak out about things about ebola or smallpox , but the dna from this organism is not infective .	人們馬上會對伊波拉或小小的恐慌感到驚訝 , 但dna從這個機體中 , 沒有感染 。
so even if somebody made the smallpox genome , that dna itself would not cause infections .	所以即使某人製造了小型基因組 , dna本身不會造成感染 。
the real concern that security departments have is designer viruses .	真正的安全部門是設計師病毒 。
and there's only two countries , the u . s . and the former soviet union , that had major efforts on trying to create biological warfare agents .	只有兩個國家 , 美國和前蘇聯盟 , 在那裡 , 美國和前蘇聯盟 , 做了很多努力 , 來創造生物戰火 。
if that research is truly discontinued , there should be very little activity on the knowhow to make designer viruses in the future .	如果這研究真的被關閉 , 應該要讓設計師病毒在未來的最佳情況下降低 。
i think singlecell organisms are possible within two years .	我認為單細胞生物在兩年內就有可能了 。
and possibly eukaryotic cells , those that we have , are possible within a decade .	可能是可能性細胞 , 在十年內 , 我們有的可能性 。
so we're now making several dozen different constructs , because we can vary the cassettes and the genes that go into this artificial chromosome .	所以我們現在已經做了幾十種不同的建構 , 因為我們可以把卡塞特和基因放進這個人工染色體 。
the key is , how do you put all of the others ?	關鍵是 , 你如何把所有其他人都放進去 ?
we start with these fragments , and then we have a homologous recombination system that reassembles those into a chromosome .	我們從這些碎片開始 , 然後我們有一組合適的組合系統 , 把這些碎片放到染色體中 。
this is derived from an organism , deinococcus radiodurans , that can take three million rads of radiation and not be killed .	這是從有機體的durans中 , 可以將三百萬輻射的輻射射殺 , 不被殺死 。
it reassembles its genome after this radiation burst in about 12 to 24 hours , after its chromosomes are literally blown apart .	它將它的基因組排放到24小時後 , 染色體的基因組在這個輻射爆炸後的基因組 。
this organism is ubiquitous on the planet , and exists perhaps now in outer space due to all our travel there .	這個生物在地球上存在 , 可能在外太空中 , 存在於我們的旅行之中 。
this is a glass beaker after about half a million rads of radiation .	這是一張玻璃碎片 , 大約有500萬個雷射輻射 。
the glass started to burn and crack , while the microbes sitting in the bottom just got happier and happier .	玻璃開始燃燒和破裂 , 雖然微生物在底部的微生物會變得更快樂 , 更快樂 。
here's an actual picture of what happens: the top of this shows the genome after 1 . 7 million rads of radiation .	這裡有一個實際的圖片 , 顯示出基因組發生的結果 , 大約有七百萬輻射的輻射 。
the chromosome is literally blown apart .	染色體的染色體則是完全分裂的 。
and here's that same dna automatically reassembled 24 hours later .	這是同一個dna自動組裝在24小時後 。
it's truly stunning that these organisms can do that , and we probably have thousands , if not tens of thousands , of different species on this planet that are capable of doing that .	真正令人驚訝的是這些生物可以做到這一點 , 我們可能有數千個物種 , 可能有數以千計的物種 , 可能有生物可以做到 。
after these genomes are synthesized , the first step is just transplanting them into a cell without a genome .	在這些基因組合成之後 , 第一步就是把它們移植到細胞 , 不是基因組 。
so we think synthetic cells are going to have tremendous potential , not only for understanding the basis of biology but for hopefully environmental and society issues .	所以我們認為合成細胞將會有巨大的潛力 , 不僅僅是了解生物學的基礎 , 還能帶來巨大的潛力 , 不僅僅是了解生物學的基礎 , 還能帶來巨大的潛力 , 不僅僅是了解生物學的基礎 。
for example , from the third organism we sequenced , methanococcus jannaschii it lives in boiling water temperatures ; its energy source is hydrogen and all its carbon comes from co2 it captures back from the environment .	舉例來說 , 來自於二氧化碳的二氧化碳 , 來自於環境中的二氧化碳 。
so we know lots of different pathways , thousands of different organisms now that live off of co2 , and can capture that back .	所以我們知道許多不同的路徑 , 數以千計的生物 , 可以捕捉到它 。
so instead of using carbon from oil for synthetic processes , we have the chance of using carbon and capturing it back from the atmosphere , converting that into biopolymers or other products .	所以 , 用碳從大氣中抽取 , 用碳從大氣中轉換成生物聚合物 , 或其他產品 。
we have one organism that lives off of carbon monoxide , and we use as a reducing power to split water to produce hydrogen and oxygen .	我們有一個有機體 , 來自碳的氧氣 , 而我們使用的是一種減少能量來製造氫和氧 。
also , there's numerous pathways that can be engineered metabolizing methane .	還有 , 有很多道路可以用來製造出甲烷 。
and dupont has a major program with statoil in norway to capture and convert the methane from the gas fields there into useful products .	由於挪威的大型農場 , 用在挪威 , 來捕捉並將甲烷從氣體中轉換成有用的物品 。
within a short while , i think there's going to be a new field called " combinatorial genomics , " because with these new synthesis capabilities , these vast gene array repertoires and the homologous recombination , we think we can design a robot to make maybe a million different chromosomes a day .	在短期內 , 我認為 , 我們可以設計一個叫做 「 組合基因組合機 」 的新領域 , 因為這些新領域 , 叫做 「 組合基因組合 」 , 因為這些新型的基因組合 , 認為我們可以設計一個機器人 , 可以創造一百萬個不同的染色體 。
and therefore , as with all biology , you get selection through screening , whether you're screening for hydrogen production , or chemical production , or just viability .	因此 , 所有生物學 , 都可以通過篩選 , 不論你在螢幕上 , 或化學產品 , 或化學生產 , 或化學產品 , 或其他生物學 。
to understand the role of these genes is going to be well within reach .	要了解這些基因的角色 , 要了解這些基因的重要性 。
we're trying to modify photosynthesis to produce hydrogen directly from sunlight .	我們正在嘗試修改光合作用 , 來製造氫氣直接從陽光合作 。
photosynthesis is modulated by oxygen , and we have an oxygeninsensitive hydrogenase that we think will totally change this process .	光合作用氧氣 , 我們有氧氣濃度的氫氣 , 我們認為它會完全改變這個過程 。
we're also combining cellulases , the enzymes that break down complex sugars into simple sugars and fermentation in the same cell for producing ethanol .	我們也結合了細胞 , 製造出乙醇 , 酵素分裂成簡單糖和酵素 , 結合細胞 , 製造出乙醇 。
pharmaceutical production is already under way in major laboratories using microbes .	藥物生產已經在大型實驗室使用微生物 。
the chemistry from compounds in the environment is orders of magnitude more complex than our best chemists can produce .	在環境裡的化學 , 比我們最好的化學家所製造出的化學還要複雜 。
i think future engineered species could be the source of food , hopefully a source of energy , environmental remediation and perhaps replacing the petrochemical industry .	我認為未來的工程物種可以是食物的源源 , 可能是食物的源源 , 希望能提供能源、環境的回憶 , 或取代化學工程 。
let me just close with ethical and policy studies .	讓我用倫理和政策研究來結合 。
we delayed the start of our experiments in 1999 until we completed a yearandahalf bioethical review as to whether we should try and make an artificial species .	我們從1999年開始實驗開始實驗 , 直到我們完成一個人工物種 。
every major religion participated in this .	每個主要宗教都參與這個 。
it was actually a very strange study , because the various religious leaders were using their scriptures as law books , and they couldn't find anything in them prohibiting making life , so it must be ok . the only ultimate concerns were biological warfare aspects of this , but gave us the go ahead to start these experiments for the reasons we were doing them .	這其實是個很奇怪的研究 , 因為許多宗教領袖使用他們的雕塑 , 來做這些實驗 , 例如說 , 若要做這些實驗 , 我們就要做這些實驗 。 唯一的結論是生物戰場的一小部分 。
right now the sloan foundation has just funded a multiinstitutional study on this , to work out what the risk and benefits to society are , and the rules that scientific teams such as my own should be using in this area , and we're trying to set good examples as we go forward .	現在 , sloan基金會已經資助了一系列的科學團隊 , 像我自己的應該要在這個領域上做 , 我們試著把好的例子放進去 。
these are complex issues .	這些都是複雜的問題 。
except for the threat of bioterrorism , they're very simple issues in terms of , can we design things to produce clean energy , perhaps revolutionizing what developing countries can do and provide through various simple processes .	除了恐怖主義的威脅 , 生物恐怖主義的威脅 , 它們很簡單 , 我們能設計東西來製造乾淨能源 , 也許革命化開發中國家能做什麼 , 以及提供各種簡單的處理方式 。
psychologist philip zimbardo says happiness and success are rooted in a trait most of us disregard: the way we orient toward the past , present and future . he suggests we calibrate our outlook on time as a first step to improving our lives .	心理學家philipzimbardo說幸福和成功 , 我們很遺憾地說 , 幸福和成功 。 他建議我們一直以來改善我們的生活方式 。
brain , business , happiness , mind , psychology , science	大腦 , 企業 , 快樂 , 心靈 , 心理學 , 科學 。
philip zimbardo prescribes a healthy take on time	philipzimbardo預設了一個健康 。
i want to share with you some ideas about the secret power of time , in a very short time .	我想和大家分享一些想法 , 關於秘密力量 , 很短的時間 。
video: all right , start the clock please . 30 seconds studio .	影片:沒錯 , 開始阻擋 , 請三十秒 。
keep it quiet please . settle down .	保持安靜 , 安靜下來 。
it's about time . end sequence . take one .	是時候 , 結束序列 。 最後序列 。
10 , nine , eight , seven , six , five , four , three , two . . .	十、九、八、七、六、五、四、三、二......
philip zimbardo: let's tune into the conversation of the principals in adam's temptation .	菲利浦•辛巴爾:咱們來談談伊斯蘭教學的對話 。
" come on adam , don't be so wishywashy . take a bite . " " i did . "	「 來吧 ! 阿姆 , 別這麼吃飯 。 」 「 我做過 。 」
" one bite , adam . don't abandon eve . "	「 亞當 , 亞當 , 亞當 , 別忘了 。 」
" i don't know , guys .	「 我不知道 , 大家 。
i don't want to get in trouble . "	我不想麻煩 。 」
" okay . one bite . what the hell ? "	「 好吧 , 一滴 , 什麼 ? 」
life is temptation . it's all about yielding , resisting , yes , no , now , later , impulsive , reflective , present focus and future focus .	生命是誘惑的 , 是的 , 不 , 現在 , 再來 , 反思 , 反思 , 專注和未來的焦點 。
promised virtues fall prey to the passions of the moment .	受歡迎的熱情 , 讓大家知道 。
of teenage girls who pledged sexual abstinence and virginity until marriage thank you george bush the majority , 60 percent , yielded to sexual temptations within one year .	青少年女孩的性愛情感 , 直到婚姻謝謝 , 喬治在一年內生產出性愛滋病和維持性 。
and most of them did so without using birth control .	大部分的人都沒有使用生育控制 。
so much for promises .	所以 , 承諾要承諾 。
now lets tempt fouryearolds , giving them a treat .	現在 , 讓四歲的孩子們 , 給他們治療 。
they can have one marshmallow now . but if they wait until the experimenter comes back , they can have two .	牠們可以有一顆棉花糖 , 但如果等到實驗者回來後 , 他們就能有兩隻 。
of course it pays , if you like marshmallows , to wait .	當然 , 如果你喜歡棉花糖 , 等待 。
what happens is twothirds of the kids give in to temptation .	三分之二的孩子在誘惑時會發生什麼事 。
they cannot wait . the others , of course , wait .	他們不能等待 , 當然 , 等等 。
they resist the temptation . they delay the now for later .	他們會抗拒誘惑 , 之後 , 他們退休了 。
walter mischel , my colleague at stanford , went back 14 years later , to try to discover what was different about those kids .	我的同事在史丹佛大學 , 在史丹佛大學的同事 , 花了14年的時間 , 試圖發現與這些孩子有什麼不同 。
there were enormous differences between kids who resisted and kids who yielded , in many ways .	在許多方面 , 孩子有很大的差異 。
the kids who resisted scored 250 points higher on the sat .	拯救了250位的孩童 , 保留了250點 。
that's enormous . that's like a whole set of different iq points .	這很巨大 。 這就像一整套不同的智商標準 。
they didn't get in as much trouble . they were better students .	他們沒有遇到麻煩 。 他們是比較好的學生 。
they were selfconfident and determined . and the key for me today , the key for you , is , they were futurefocused rather than presentfocused .	他們有自信和決心 , 關鍵是 , 我今天的鑰匙是 , 你的鑰匙是 , 他們是未來的 , 而不是現在的鑰匙 。
so what is time perspective ? that's what i'm going to talk about today .	所以 , 時間是怎樣的呢 ? 這就是我今天要談的 。
time perspective is the study of how individuals , all of us , divide the flow of your human experience into time zones or time categories .	觀點是 , 人類體驗的方式 , 分裂了你人類體驗的方式 , 分裂了你人類體驗的過程 , 或時間分裂 。
and you do it automatically and nonconsciously .	而且你會自動和無意識地進行 。
they vary between cultures , between nations , between individuals , between social classes , between education levels .	在社會階級之間 , 社會階級之間 , 教育層面之間的差異 。
and the problem is that they can become biased , because you learn to overuse some of them and underuse the others .	問題是 , 牠們會變得偏見 , 因為你學會會造成偏見 。
what determines any decision you make ?	你要決定什麼決定 ?
you make a decision on which you're going to base an action .	你做出一個決定 , 你要做一個決定 。
for some people it's only about what is in the immediate situation , what other people are doing and what you're feeling .	對某些人來說 , 其他人正在做的事 , 以及你所感受到的是什麼 。
and those people , when they make their decisions in that format we're going to call them " presentoriented , " because their focus is what is now .	而這些人 , 當他們做出決策時 , 我們會稱他們為 「 現代 」 , 因為他們焦點就是現在 。
for others , the present is irrelevant .	對其他人來說 , 現況是不相關的 。
it's always about " what is this situation like that i've experienced in the past ? "	總是說: 「 這是我過去所經歷過的那種情況 ? 」
so that their decisions are based on past memories .	他們的決策是基於過去記憶的 。
and we're going to call those people " pastoriented , " because they focus on what was .	我們會稱之為 「 過去 」 的人們 , 因為他們焦點在哪裡 。
for others it's not the past , it's not the present , it's only about the future .	對於其他人來說 , 這不是過去 , 而是未來 。
their focus is always about anticipated consequences .	他們的焦點總是在預期的後果 。
we're going to call them " futureoriented . " their focus is on what will be .	我們將稱之為 「 未來期望 」 , 他們專注在未來的方向 。
so , time paradox , i want to argue , the paradox of time perspective , is something that influences every decision you make , you're totally unaware of .	所以 , 時間悖論 , 我想要辯論 , 思考的矛盾是 , 每一件事都能影響你所做的決定 , 你完全沒意識到 。
namely , the extent to which you have one of these biased time perspectives .	如同你所擁有的 , 這種偏見的遠景 。
well there is actually six of them . there are two ways to be presentoriented .	其實有六個 , 其中有兩種方式 。
there is two ways to be pastoriented , two ways to be future .	要有兩種方式 , 要是未來的兩種方式 。
you can focus on pastpositive , or pastnegative .	你可以把焦點放在正面或負面上 。
you can be presenthedonistic , namely you focus on the joys of life , or presentfatalist it doesn't matter , your life is controlled .	你是可以被控制的 , 不論你是誰 , 你的人生是有權力的 , 你的人生是被控制的 。
you can be futureoriented , setting goals .	你可以成為未來的目標 , 設定目標 。
or you can be transcendental future: namely , life begins after death .	或者 , 你能超越未來 , 生命是從死亡開始的 。
developing the mental flexibility to shift time perspectives fluidly depending on the demands of the situation , that's what you've got to learn to do .	發展出心理靈活性 , 使時間觀點轉移到時間的觀點 , 不論是你必須學會做的事 。
so , very quickly , what is the optimal time profile ?	所以 , 很快地 , 最樂觀的時刻是什麼 ?
high on pastpositive . moderately high on future .	很高 , 很高 , 未來的高度很高 。
and moderate on presenthedonism .	而現代主義的存在 。
and always low on pastnegative and presentfatalism .	總是低於負面和真實主義 。
so the optimal temporal mix is what you get from the past pastpositive gives you roots . you connect your family , identity and your self .	所以 , 最樂觀的時刻 , 就是你從過去所得到的 , 帶著你的家人、身分、身分和你的自身 。
what you get from the future is wings to soar to new destinations , new challenges .	你從未來的角度 , 新挑戰 , 新的挑戰 。
what you get from the present hedonism is the energy , the energy to explore yourself , places , people , sensuality .	你從現場表達的能量是能量 , 來探索自己、人、人、人、感覺 。
any time perspective in excess has more negatives than positives .	任何時間的觀點 , 都比正面更負面 。
what do futures sacrifice for success ?	未來犧牲成功的原因是什麼 ?
they sacrifice family time . they sacrifice friend time .	他們犧牲家庭時間 , 犧牲朋友的時間 。
they sacrifice fun time . they sacrifice personal indulgence .	他們犧牲個人的婚姻 , 犧牲個人的成人 。
they sacrifice hobbies . and they sacrifice sleep . so it affects their health .	他們犧牲睡眠 , 所以它會影響他們的健康 。
and they live for work , achievement and control .	他們活著工作、成就及控制 。
i'm sure that resonates with some of the tedsters .	我相信 , 和一些tedstersterstersterstersterster 。
and it resonated for me . i grew up as a poor kid in the south bronx ghetto , a sicilian family everyone lived in the past and present .	對我來說 , 我成長了 , 一個貧窮的孩子 , 在南布朗克斯區的貧窮小鎮 , 一個貧窮的孩子 , 來自南布朗克斯區的貧窮小孩子 , 當時是南布朗克斯區的一個貧窮的孩子 。
i'm here as a futureoriented person who went over the top , who did all these sacrifices because teachers intervened , and made me future oriented .	我身為一個年輕人 , 向前邁進 , 做這些犧牲 , 因為老師介入 , 並且讓我未來的目標 。
told me don't eat that marshmallow , because if you wait you're going to get two of them , until i learned to balance out .	告訴我不要吃那棉花糖 , 因為如果你等你等待你會得到兩位 , 直到我學習平衡 。
i've added presenthedonism , i've added a focus on the pastpositive , so , at 76 years old , i am more energetic than ever , more productive , and i'm happier than i have ever been .	我已經加入了專注的焦點 , 在76歲時 , 我比以前更有創意 , 更有生產力 , 我比以往更高興 , 更有生產力 。
i just want to say that we are applying this to many world problems: changing the dropout rates of school kids , combating addictions , enhancing teen health , curing vets' ptsd with time metaphors getting miracle cures promoting sustainability and conservation , reducing physical rehabilitation where there is a 50percent drop out rate , altering appeals to suicidal terrorists , and modifying family conflicts as timezone clashes .	我只是想要說 , 我們正在應用在許多世界的問題上 , 改善了家庭衝突 , 例如:改善貧民區 , 改善家庭衝突 , 如同時間比喻 , 提高了數量 , 改善家庭衝突 , 如同時間比喻 , 提高了數量 , 改善家庭衝突 , 例如 , 增長壽命和保育 。

and what you see is bright and dark regions , and that's about as far as it got for us .	你看到的是明亮和黑暗的區域 , 這對我們來說是很明顯的 。
it was so mystifying: we couldn't make out what we were seeing on titan .	這很令人難以置信:我們無法在土地上看到的 。
when you look closer at this region , you start to see things like sinuous channels we didn't know . you see a few round things .	當你仔細看這個區域 , 你會看到一些圓形的東西 。
this , we later found out , is , in fact , a crater , but there are very few craters on the surface of titan , meaning it's a very young surface .	我們發現 , 其實 , 其實是一隻老鼠 , 但在土衛六的表面上有非常小的表面 。
and there are features that look tectonic .	這裡有一些特徵 , 看起來是tonic 。
they look like they've been pulled apart .	他們看起來就像是被拆開的 。
whenever you see anything linear on a planet , it means there's been a fracture , like a fault .	每當你看到任何線條 , 它意味著 , 有點像是個錯覺 。
and so it's been tectonically altered .	所以 , 它一直在改變 。
but we couldn't make sense of our images , until , six months after we got into orbit , an event occurred that many have regarded as the highlight of cassini's investigation of titan .	但我們無法理解我們的影像 , 直到六個月後 , 我們開始軌道 , 直到六個月後 , 我們變成了軌道 , 一個事件發生了 , 許多人都被視為 「 泰坦 」 的調查 。
and that was the deployment of the huygens probe , the europeanbuilt huygens probe that cassini had carried for seven years across the solar system . we deployed it to the atmosphere of titan , it took two and a half hours to descend , and it landed on the surface .	這正是美國衛星探測器所拍攝的土地 , 它花了2.5小時的時間 , 到達陸地表面 。
and i just want to emphasize how significant an event this is .	我只想強調一下 , 一個活動的重要性 。
this is a device of human making , and it landed in the outer solar system for the first time in human history .	這是人類史上第一次使用太陽能系統的裝置 。
it is so significant that , in my mind , this was an event that should have been celebrated with ticker tape parades in every city across the u . s . and europe , and sadly , that wasn't the case .	很明顯的是 , 在我的腦海裡 , 整個城市都在美國和歐洲 , 很令人驚訝的是 , 這不是案例 。
it was significant for another reason . this is an international mission , and this event was celebrated in europe , in germany , and the celebratory presentations were given in english accents , and american accents , and german accents , and french and italian and dutch accents .	對另一方面來說 , 這很有意義 。 這是個國際任務 。 這是個國際任務 。 這是個國際任務 , 和德國人的演講 , 和德國人的演講 , 和德國聯盟 , 和德國人的演講 , 和德國聯盟 , 和德國人的演講 , 和德國人的演講 , 和德國的演講 , 和德國人的演講 。
it was a moving demonstration of what the words " united nations " are supposed to mean: a true union of nations joined together in a colossal effort for good .	這是 「 聯合國聯合國 」 的協議 , 真正的聯合國集合起來 , 成為 「 聯合國 」 的聯合國 。
and , in this case , it was a massive undertaking to explore a planet , and to come to understand a planetary system that , for all of human history , had been unreachable , and now humans had actually touched it .	在這個案例中 , 要去探索一個星球 , 要來了解一個行星系統 , 人類已經不可思議了 , 而現在人類也真的碰到它 。
so it was i mean , i'm getting goose bumps just talking about it .	所以這就是我說的 , 我會拿起雞蛋白 , 只是說話 。
it was a tremendously emotional event , and it's something that i will personally never forget , and you shouldn't either .	那是個很激烈的情緒活動 , 也是我個人永遠永遠不會忘記的 , 你也不應該這麼做 。
but anyway , the probe took measurements of the atmosphere on the way down , and it also took panoramic pictures .	但無論如何 , 探測器在下面進行測量大氣層的變化 , 同時也拍攝了大氣層的照片 。
and i can't tell you what it was like to see the first pictures of titan's surface from the probe . and this is what we saw .	我無法告訴各位 , 看到這張圖片的第一張照片 , 這是我們看到的 。
and it was a shocker , because it was everything we wanted those other pictures taken from orbit to be .	這很令人震驚 , 因為我們想要的其他照片從軌道上運轉 。
it was an unambiguous pattern , a geological pattern .	這是個不可思議的模式 , 一個邏輯模式 。
it's a dendritic drainage pattern that can be formed only by the flow of liquids .	它是一種動態的流動液體 , 可以用液體來形成 。
and you can follow these channels and you can see how they all converge .	你可以追蹤這些頻道 , 可以看到它們如何運作 。
and they converge into this channel here , which drains into this region .	然後他們將這邊緣轉換成這個區域 。
you are looking at a shoreline .	你正在看著海岸線 。
was this a shoreline of fluids ? we didn't know .	這是液體的流體嗎 ? 我們不知道 。
but this is somewhat of a shoreline .	但這有點像是海岸線 。
this picture is taken at 16 kilometers .	這張照片是16公里 。
this is the picture taken at eight kilometers , ok ? again , the shoreline .	這張照片是8公里的照片 , 好嗎 ? 再一次 , 海岸線 。
okay , now , 16 kilometers , eight kilometers this is roughly an airline altitude .	好 , 現在 , 16公里 , 大約是6公里 , 8公里大約是空氣線 。
if you were going to take an airplane trip across the u . s . , you would be flying at these altitudes .	假如你將飛機在美國的飛機上飛行 , 你就會在這些高度上飛行 。
so , this is the picture you would have at the window of titanian airlines as you fly across the surface of titan .	這張照片是你在泰坦航空飛行器官飛行的窗戶 。
and then finally , the probe came to rest on the surface , and i'm going to show you , ladies and gentlemen , the first picture ever taken from the surface of a moon in the outer solar system .	最後 , 在外太陽系裡 , 我會告訴各位 , 各位先生女士 , 第一張照片從外太陽系的表面上拍攝 。
and here is the horizon , ok ?	這是地平線 , 好嗎 ?
these are probably water ice pebbles , yes ?	這些可能是水冰泡 , 是嗎 ?
and obviously , it landed in one of these flat , dark regions and it didn't sink out of sight . so it wasn't fluid that we landed in .	很明顯地 , 在這個平面上 , 黑暗的區域 , 沒有被放射到的地方 。 所以它不是液體 。
what the probe came down in was basically the titan equivalent of a mud flat .	原來的底部 , 基本上就是泥巴的平面 。
this is an unconsolidated ground that is suffused with liquid methane .	這是一種未被溶解的土地 , 被困在液態甲烷中 。
and it's probably the case that this material has washed off the highlands of titan through these channels that we saw , and has drained over billions of years to fill in lowlying basins .	可能是這種材料被浪費在低地底下 , 以至於我們所見到的土地 , 數十億年來填補在低水池裡 。
and that is what the huygens probe landed in .	這就是 「 嗡嗡 」 的起源 。
but still , there was no sign in our images , or even in the huygens' images , of any large , open bodies of fluids .	但 , 我們的影像中沒有任何大型、開放的身體 , 甚至是大型的流體 。
where were they ? it got even more puzzling when we found dunes .	他們在哪裡呢 ? 在我們找到沙丘時 , 更令人困惑 。
ok , so this is our movie of the equatorial region of titan , showing these dunes . these are dunes that are 100 meters tall , separated by a few kilometers , and they go on for miles and miles and miles .	好 , 這是我們在土衛六的一百公里外的部落 , 那裡有一百公尺高速 , 距離距離幾公里 , 距離距離幾公里 , 遠離距離 。

this is the saharan desert of titan .	這是撒哈拉沙漠 。
it's obviously a place which is very dry , or you wouldn't get dunes .	很明顯地 , 那裡很乾燥 , 或是你不會得到沙丘 。
so again , it got puzzling that there were no bodies of fluid , until finally , we saw lakes in the polar regions .	所以 , 再一次 , 難以置信的是 , 直到最後 , 我們看到湖泊在北極地區 。
and there is a lake scene in the south polar region of titan .	在南極地區有一個湖景 。

and then , only a week and a half ago , we flew over the north pole of titan and found , again , we found a feature here the size of the caspian sea .	然後 , 一週半前 , 我們飛越北極點 , 再次發現 , 我們在土地上找到了一系列的大小 。
so it seems that the liquids , for some reason we don't understand , or during at least this season , are apparently at the poles of titan .	所以 , 似乎是液體 , 有些原因我們不了解 , 至少這季 , 很明顯地在土地的南部 。
and i think you would agree that we have found titan is a remarkable , mystical place . it's exotic , it's alien , but yet strangely earthlike , and having earthlike geological formations and a tremendous geographical diversity , and is a fascinating world whose only rival in the solar system for complexity and richness is the earth itself .	大家會同意 , 我們發現泰坦是個很奇妙的現象 , 但奇怪地理相反 , 地球本身 , 和豐富的地球本身 , 相反地理多樣性 , 卻是地球本身 。
and so now we go onto enceladus . enceladus is a small moon , it's about a tenth the size of titan . and you can see it here next to england , just to show you the size . this is not meant to be a threat .	所以現在我們來到英國的大小 , 你可以看到它在英格蘭的大小 , 你可以看到它在英格蘭的大小 , 要告訴你大小的大小 , 這不是代表威脅的大小 。
and enceladus is very white , it's very bright , and its surface is obviously wrecked with fractures .	土衛二是很明顯的 , 它的表面很明顯地被破碎了 。
it is a very geologically active body .	它是個非常地質的活躍身體 。
but the mother lode of discoveries on enceladus was found at the south pole and we're looking at the south pole here where we found this system of fractures .	但在南極 , 我們在南極找到了這個系統 , 我們發現的是南極點 , 我們在南極看到南極 , 我們發現的是南極點 。
and they're a different color because they're a different composition .	它們是不同的顏色 , 因為它們是不同的顏色 。
they are coated . these fractures are coated with organic materials .	它們是有機物質的 。 這些碎片是由有機物質所產生 。
moreover , this whole , entire region , the south polar region , has elevated temperatures . it's the hottest place on the planet , on the body .	此外 , 整個區域 , 南極區域 , 整個區域 , 南極區域 , 整個區域 , 非常溫度 , 這是地球上最熱的地方 。
that's as bizarre as finding that the antarctic on the earth is hotter than the tropics .	這很奇怪 , 地球上的南極點比熱帶星還要熱 。
and then , when we took additional pictures , we discovered that from these fractures are issuing jets of fine , icy particles extending hundreds of miles into space .	接著 , 當我們拿了其他的圖片時 , 我們發現 , 這些碎片是來自這些碎片 , 冰粒在數百英里外的太空中形成 。
and when we colorcode this image , to bring out the faint light levels , we see that these jets feed a plume that , in fact , we see , in other images , goes thousands of miles into the space above enceladus .	當我們把這張圖片放到太空中 , 我們會看到這些噴射的光量 , 會看到這些噴射的光量 , 我們可以看到 , 這些噴射的光量相當於幾千英里外的太空船 。
my team and i have examined images like this , and like this one , and have thought about the other results from cassini .	我和我的團隊已經檢查過像這樣的圖像 , 像這樣 , 並且從cassini的影像中找到了 。
and we have arrived at the conclusion that these jets may be erupting from pockets of liquid water under the surface of enceladus .	我們得到了結論 , 這些噴泉可能是來自土衛二的液態水底下的液態水 。
so we have , possibly , liquid water , organic materials and excess heat .	所以 , 我們有有機物質、有機物質、有機物質 , 和過熱 。
in other words , we have possibly stumbled upon the holy grail of modern day planetary exploration , or in other words , an environment that is potentially suitable for living organisms .	換句話說 , 我們可能在現代天行星探索的環境中 , 或其他字體中 , 有可能適合生命的環境 。
and i don't think i need to tell you that the discovery of life elsewhere in our solar system , whether it be on enceladus or elsewhere , would have enormous cultural and scientific implications .	我不認為我需要告訴各位 , 在我們的太陽系中 , 在太陽系裡的發現 , 無論是土衛二 , 或其他地方 , 都會有巨大的文化和科學上的發現 。
because if we could demonstrate that genesis had occurred not once , but twice , independently , in our solar system , then that means , by inference , it has occurred a staggering number of times throughout the universe and its 13 . 7 billion year history .	因為如果我們能證明 , 基因沒有發生過 , 那就意味著 , 在我們的太陽系中 , 這意味著 , 在我們的太陽系中 , 這意味著 , 在我們的太陽系中 , 這意味著 , 在我們的太陽系中 , 它已經發生了幾次 , 經過了數次的宇宙 , 和其它137億年的歷史 。
right now , earth is the only planet still that we know is teeming with life .	目前 , 地球是唯一的星球 , 我們知道的生命存在 。
it is precious , it is unique , it is still , so far , the only home we've ever known .	它很珍貴 , 它是獨一無二的 , 它是我們所知的唯一的家 。
and if any of you were alert and coherent during the 1960s and we'd forgive you , if you weren't , ok you would remember this very famous picture taken by the apollo 8 astronauts in 1968 .	如果在1968年 , 在1968年 , 美國太空人在1968年時 , 你會記得這位非常有名的照片 。
it was the first time that earth was imaged from space , and it had an enormous impact on our sense of place in the universe , and our sense of responsibility for the protection of our own planet .	這是第一次地球是從太空中拍攝的 , 它對我們有著巨大的影響 , 在宇宙中 , 和我們對地球的安全感應有著巨大的影響 。
well , we on cassini have taken an equivalent first , a picture that no human eye has ever seen before .	嗯 , 我們在cassini拍攝了一場人類眼前的照片 , 沒有人眼睛的照片 。
it is a total eclipse of the sun , seen from the other side of saturn .	它是來自土星的太陽 , 來自土星的一面 。
and in this impossibly beautiful picture , you see the main rings backlit by the sun , you see the refracted image of the sun and you see this ring created , in fact , by the exhalations of enceladus .	在這張照片中 , 你看到的是太陽的光線 , 你看到了太陽的圖像 , 你看到這張圖片 , 看到了太陽的圖片 , 你看到這張圖片 , 看到了太陽的重覆 , 實際上 , 由於荷蘭的高度 。
but as if that weren't brilliant enough , we can spot , in this beautiful image , sight of our own planet , cradled in the arms of saturn's rings .	但 , 若不夠聰明 , 我們就能在土星的畫面上作出一個美麗的影像 , 和我們自己的星球在土星的火星上拍攝的照片 。
now , there is something deeply moving about seeing ourselves from afar , and capturing the sight of our little , blueocean planet in the skies of other worlds .	現在 , 有一些深刻的看法 , 把我們的小小、藍色星球的星球 , 和其他世界的視覺連結起來 。
and that , and the perspective of ourselves that we gain from that , may be , in the end , the finest reward that we earn from this journey of discovery that started half a century ago .	而我們從這個旅程發現的觀點 , 可能是最後 , 我們從這個旅程發現的起源 , 可能是最後的一世紀 。
as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped . this slows the delivery of aid after a disaster and hides the economic potential of unused lands and unknown roads . in this short talk , google's lalitesh katragadda demos map maker , a group mapmaking tool that people around the globe are using to map their world .	2005年 , 世界上只有15%的人會在這個短期內 , 發表了一系列的資料 , 例如說 , 谷歌的globe使用地圖和未知道路 。 這段短篇的演講 , 谷歌的globe博士地圖 , 用地圖繪製工具 , 讓世界各地的人都使用地圖 。
collaboration , design , map , technology	合作、設計、地圖、科技 。
lalitesh katragadda: making maps to fight disaster , build economies	拉里斯•卡爾加達:製作地圖來打破災難 , 建立經濟體 。
in 2008 , cyclone nargis devastated myanmar .	在2008年 , 西克羅尼納爾尼納爾吉斯爆炸了 。
millions of people were in severe need of help .	數百萬人都需要幫助 。
the u . n . wanted to rush people and supplies to the area .	聯合國想要把人民和供應轉移到地區 。
but there were no maps , no maps of roads , no maps showing hospitals , no way for help to reach the cyclone victims .	但沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖顯示醫院 , 沒有任何地圖 , 沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖
when we look at a map of los angeles or london , it is hard to believe that as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped to a geocodable level of detail .	當我們看到洛杉磯或倫敦的地圖時 , 它很難相信 , 在2005年 , 只有15%的地圖是世界的地圖 。
the u . n . ran headfirst into a problem that the majority of the world's populous faces: not having detailed maps .	聯合國阿拉伯國會提出一個問題:沒有細節地圖 。
but help was coming .	但 , 協助來了 。
at google , 40 volunteers used a new software to map 120 , 000 kilometers of roads , 3 , 000 hospitals , logistics and relief points .	在谷歌 , 40個志工用一個新的軟體來繪製一萬公里路、三千個醫院、邏輯和信念 。
and it took them four days .	他們花了四天的時間 。
the new software they used ? google mapmaker .	他們用的新軟體嗎 ? google地圖 。
google mapmaker is a technology that empowers each of us to map what we know locally .	google地圖 , 每個人都能在地圖上繪製出我們所知的地方 。
people have used this software to map everything from roads to rivers , from schools to local businesses , and video stores to the corner store .	人們用這個軟體來繪製這些軟體 , 從路到河流 , 從路到河流 , 到學校 , 到商店 , 到街坊 。
nobel prize nominee hernando de soto recognized that the key to economic liftoff for most developing countries is to tap the vast amounts of uncapitalized land .	諾貝爾獎得主 , 諾貝爾獎得主 , 大部分發展中國家 , 都要把大量的未知的鑰匙轉移到經濟利益 。
for example , a trillion dollars of real estate remains uncapitalized in india alone .	舉例來說 , 一兆美元的土地 , 沒有在印度獨立的 。
in the last year alone , thousands of users in 170 countries have mapped millions of pieces of information , and created a map of a level of detail never thought viable .	去年 , 僅僅有數以千計的使用者在170個國家擁有了數以千計的使用者 , 創造出了一連串的資料 , 創造出一個不可思議的細節 。
and this was made possible by the power of passionate users everywhere .	由於熱情使用者的力量 , 熱情的使用者 。
let's look at some of the maps being created by users right now .	現在我們來看看一些地圖 , 是由使用者所做的 。
so , as we speak , people are mapping the world in these 170 countries .	所以 , 正如我們所說的 , 人們在這些170個國家裡 , 把世界放進去 。
you can see bridget in africa who just mapped a road in senegal .	你可以看到非洲的橋樑 , 位在塞內加爾的橋樑 。
and , closer to home , chalua , an n . g . road in bangalore .	更接近家鄉 , 路易斯.路易斯.羅拉 。
this is the result of computational geometry , gesture recognition , and machine learning .	這就是計算幾何學的結果 , 以及機器學習 。
this is a victory of thousands of users , in hundreds of cities , one user , one edit at a time .	這是數以千計的使用者 , 一個使用者 , 有一百個城市 , 一個使用者 , 一個編輯 。
this is an invitation to the 70 percent of our unmapped planet .	這是我們未預期的百分之七十的證據 。
welcome to the new world .	歡迎來到新世界 。
in 2003 , the palestinian village of budrus mounted a 10monthlong nonviolent protest to stop a barrier being built across their olive groves . did you hear about it ? didn't think so . brazilian filmmaker julia bacha asks why we only pay attention to violence in the israelpalestine conflict and not to the nonviolent leaders who may one day bring peace .	在2003年 , 巴西亞電影makeruliabacha問了為什麼我們只關注暴力的領袖而非暴力的領導者 , 不論是哪裡的巴西人 , 都會問為什麼我們只關注暴力的暴力行為 , 不是那些非暴力的領袖 , 會問為什麼我們只關注暴力的領導者 , 不論是哪裡 ?
arts , communication , compassion , entertainment , film , peace , violence , war	藝術、溝通、慈悲、娛樂、電影、和平、暴力、戰爭 。
julia bacha: pay attention to nonviolence	茱莉亞:注意到非暴力 。
for the last 8 years , i have dedicated my life to documenting the work of israelis and palestinians who are trying to end the conflict using peaceful means .	過去8年來 , 我已經把我的人生記錄到以色列和巴勒斯坦人試圖結束衝突與巴勒斯坦人的合作 , 試圖結束衝突和平的意義 。
when i travel with my work across europe and the united states , one question always comes up: where is the palestinian gandhi ?	當我在歐洲和美國旅行時 , 有一個問題總是出現: 「 巴勒斯坦甘地 ? 」
why aren't palestinians using nonviolent resistance ?	為什麼不是巴勒斯坦人使用非暴力抗議呢 ?
the challenge i face when i hear this question is that often i have just returned from the middle east where i spent my time filming dozens of palestinians who are using nonviolence to defend their lands and water resources from israeli soldiers and settlers .	當我聽到這個問題時 , 我所聽到的問題是 , 通常我剛從中東 , 到我花了幾十歲的巴勒斯坦人 , 他們使用非暴力武器來防護他們的土地和水資源 , 用非暴力來防護他們的土地和水資源 。
these leaders are trying to forge a massive national nonviolent movement to end the occupation and build peace in the region .	這些領導者試圖要把大規模的國家非暴力運動結合起來 , 並建立和平 。
yet , most of you have probably never heard about them .	然而 , 大部分的人可能從來沒有聽過他們 。
this divide between what's happening on the ground and perceptions abroad is one of the key reasons why we don't have yet a palestinian peaceful resistance movement that has been successful .	在地面和平面上發生的事情 , 對於地面和平的影響 , 造成了很大的影響 , 其中一個關鍵原因之一 , 是因為我們沒有一個巴勒斯坦和平的抗議運動 , 已經成功 。
so i'm here today to talk about the power of attention , the power of your attention , and the emergence and development of nonviolent movements in the west bank , gaza and elsewhere but today , my case study is going to be palestine .	所以今天我來談談注意力的力量 , 你注意力的力量 , 關注的力量 , 以及在西非暴力運動的力量 , 加薩和其他地方 , 但現在 , 我的案例研究是巴勒斯坦 。
i believe that what's mostly missing for nonviolence to grow is not for palestinians to start adopting nonviolence , but for us to start paying attention to those who already are .	我相信 , 最為巴勒斯坦人開始採取非暴力的方式 , 而是為了我們開始關注這些人 。
allow me to illustrate this point by taking you to this village called budrus .	讓我來說明一下這個村落叫布德魯斯 。
about seven years ago , they faced extinction , because israel announced it would build a separation barrier , and part of this barrier would be built on top of the village .	大約七年前 , 他們面臨滅絕 , 因為以色列宣布 , 要建設一個隔離障礙 , 其中一部分會在村落裡建造一個隔離障礙 。
they would lose 40 percent of their land and be surrounded , so they would lose free access to the rest of the west bank .	他們會失去40%的土地 , 所以他們失去了40%的土地 , 所以他們失去了40%的土地 。
through inspired local leadership , they launched a peaceful resistance campaign to stop that from happening .	透過激勵當地的領導力 , 他們發起了一個和平抗議活動 , 阻止發生 。
let me show you some brief clips , so you have a sense for what that actually looked like on the ground .	讓我給你們看一些短片 , 所以你有感覺到地面上看起來的樣子 。
palestinian woman: we were told the wall would separate palestine from israel .	巴勒斯坦婦女:我們被告知牆會把巴勒斯坦的巴勒斯坦婦女分開 。
here in budrus , we realized the wall would steal our land .	在布德魯斯 , 我們意識到牆壁會偷我們的土地 。
israeli man: the fence has , in fact , created a solution to terror .	以色列人來說 , 事實上 , 創造了一個解決方案 。
man: today you're invited to a peaceful march .	男子:今天你被邀請去和平的遊行 。
you are joined by dozens of your israeli brothers and sisters .	你已經加入了數十位以色列兄弟姐妹 。
israeli activist: nothing scares the army more than nonviolent opposition .	以色列行動主義者:沒有暴力反對 , 比非暴力反對 。
woman: we saw the men trying to push the soldiers , but none of them could do that .	女子:我們看到男人試圖把軍人打開 , 但沒有人能做到 。
but i think the girls could do it .	但我認為女孩們可以做到 。
fatah party member: we must empty our minds of traditional thinking .	fatah黨員:我們必須擁抱我們的傳統思維 。
hamas party member: we were in complete harmony , and we wanted to spread it to all of palestine .	哈瑪斯•派對:我們是完全和諧的 , 我們想要把它帶到巴勒斯坦 。
chanting: one united nation .	主題:一個聯合國 。
fatah , hamas and the popular front !	fatah , 哈馬斯和普通的前面 !
news anchor: the clashes over the fence continue .	新聞報導員: 「 沿著海岸繼續下去 。 」
reporter: israeli border police were sent to disperse the crowd .	記者:以色列邊境警察被送去散播人群 。
they were allowed to use any force necessary .	他們被允許使用任何必要的力量 。
man: these are live bullets .	男子:這些都是肝臟 。
it's like fallujah . shooting everywhere .	像是瓦哈 , 每次拍攝 。
israeli activist: i was sure we were all going to die .	以色列行動主義者:我肯定我們會死去 。
but there were others around me who weren't even cowering .	但 , 也有其他的我還沒在同事 。
israeli soldier: a nonviolent protest is not going to stop the [unclear] .	以色列士兵:非暴力抗議不會阻止它 。
protester: this is a peaceful march .	教徒:這是和平的遊行 。
there is no need to use violence .	不需要使用暴力 。
chanting: we can do it ! we can do it !	:我們能做到 ! 我們可以做到 ! 我們可以做到 !
julia bacha: when i first heard about the story of budrus , i was surprised that the international media had failed to cover the extraordinary set of events that happened seven years ago , in 2003 .	朱利亞•巴基:當我第一次聽到關於布德魯的故事時 , 我很驚訝 , 國際媒體已經失敗了 , 在2003年之前 , 在2003年時 , 我很驚訝 。
what was even more surprising was the fact that budrus was successful .	更令人驚訝的是布德魯斯成功了 。
the residents , after 10 months of peaceful resistance , convinced the israeli government to move the route of the barrier off their lands and to the green line , which is the internationally recognized boundary between israel and the palestinian territories .	居民 , 在10個月後 , 與巴勒斯坦的國際組織建立了以色列和巴勒斯坦的國際組織 , 以以色列與巴勒斯坦之間的地位 , 以以色列與巴勒斯坦之間的距離 。
the resistance in budrus has since spread to villages across the west bank and to palestinian neighborhoods in jerusalem .	巴勒斯坦的社區在耶路撒冷的抗議中 , 布德魯斯的抗議已經散播到整個西岸和巴勒斯坦街區 。
yet the media remains mostly silent on these stories .	但媒體仍然在這些故事中保持沉默 。
this silence carries profound consequences for the likelihood that nonviolence can grow , or even survive , in palestine .	這種沉默會造成很嚴重的後果 , 不暴力可能會成長 , 或甚至生存在巴勒斯坦 。
violent resistance and nonviolent resistance share one very important thing in common ; they are both a form of theater seeking an audience to their cause .	暴力抗爭和非暴力抗爭 , 它們是一種劇場 , 會讓觀眾看到它們的形式 。
if violent actors are the only ones constantly getting frontpage covers and attracting international attention to the palestinian issue , it becomes very hard for nonviolent leaders to make the case to their communities that civil disobedience is a viable option in addressing their plight .	如果暴力的演員是唯一的一員 , 才能讓那些公民獨立的團體變成非常困難的 , 非暴力的領導者 , 會讓這些民眾歧視 , 變成非常困難的 , 非暴力的領袖 , 讓她們的團體變得非常困難 , 非暴力的領導者 , 讓她們的團體變成非常困難的 , 非暴力的領導者 , 讓她們的團體變成非常困難的 , 非暴力的領導者 , 讓她們的團體變得非常困難 。
the power of attention is probably going to come as no surprise to the parents in the room .	注意力的注意力可能會發生在房間裡的不陌生人
the surest way to make your child throw increasingly louder tantrums is by giving him attention the first time he throws a fit .	要讓你的孩子變得更大膽 , 很快就會把注意力放在第一次 , 把他的注意力帶給注意力 。
the tantrum will become what childhood psychologists call a functional behavior , since the child has learned that he can get parental attention out of it .	細菌會變成兒童心理學家所謂的功能性行為 , 因為孩童的心理學家稱之為功能行為 , 因為孩子已經學會兒童心理學家稱之為功能行為 。
parents can incentivize or disincentivize behavior simply by giving or withdrawing attention to their children .	父母可以鼓勵或把注意力轉移到孩子身上 。
but that's true for adults too .	但對成人也是如此 。
in fact , the behavior of entire communities and countries can be influenced , depending on where the international community chooses to focus its attention .	事實上 , 整個社區的行為和國家都能受到影響 , 依賴國際社群選擇聚焦注意力 。
i believe that at the core of ending the conflict in the middle east and bringing peace is for us to transform nonviolence into a functional behavior by giving a lot more attention to the nonviolent leaders on the ground today .	我相信 , 在中東和平的關鍵行為 , 將非暴力的領導者帶給我們 , 來改變非暴力的行為 , 讓大家更關注於非暴力的領導者 。
in the course of taking my film to villages in the west bank , in gaza and in east jerusalem , i have seen the impact that even one documentary film can have in influencing the transformation .	在我的電影裡 , 在加薩和東耶路撒冷的村落中 , 我也看到了影響 , 甚至一部電影可以影響到這個轉變 。
in a village called wallajeh , which sits very close to jerusalem , the community was facing a very similar plight to budrus .	在一個村莊叫做瓦拉jeh , 位置非常相似 , 位於布德魯斯 。
they were going to be surrounded , lose a lot of their lands and not have freedom of access , either to the west bank or jerusalem .	他們會被圍繞著 , 失去了許多土地 , 而沒有自由取得的土地 , 或耶路撒冷 。
they had been using nonviolence for about two years but had grown disenchanted since nobody was paying attention .	兩年來 , 因為沒有人在注意力 , 因為沒有人注意力 。
so we organized a screening .	所以我們組織了螢幕 。
a week later , they held the most wellattended and disciplined demonstration to date .	一週後 , 他們重建了最好的示範 , 和其他的示範 。
the organizers say that the villagers , upon seeing the story of budrus documented in a film , felt that there were indeed people following what they were doing , that people cared .	組織者說 , 村民們在電影裡看到布德魯斯的紀錄片 , 感覺到人們在乎他們在做的事 , 人們在乎他們在做的事 。
so they kept on going .	所以他們繼續繼續下去 。
on the israeli side , there is a new peace movement called solidariot , which means solidarity in hebrew .	以色列來說 , 有一個新的和平運動 , 叫做索利亞利亞 , 它是來自伊斯蘭國的新和平運動 。
the leaders of this movement have been using budrus as one of their primary recruiting tools .	這種運動的領導者正常用布德魯斯作為一個主要的工具之一 。
they report that israelis who had never been active before , upon seeing the film , understand the power of nonviolence and start joining their activities .	他們報導了非暴力的力量 , 開始加入他們的活動 。
the examples of wallajeh and the solidariot movement show that even a smallbudget independent film can play a role in transforming nonviolence into a functional behavior .	華拉jeh和solidajeh的例子 , 甚至是小型的獨立電影可以扮演角色 , 改變非暴力行為 。
now imagine the power that big media players could have if they started covering the weekly nonviolent demonstrations happening in villages like bil'in , ni'lin , wallajeh , in jerusalem neighborhoods like sheikh jarrah and silwan the nonviolent leaders would become more visible , valued and effective in their work .	現在 , 想像一下 , 強大媒體玩家的力量 , 只要他們開始覆蓋整個週遭的非暴力行為 , 像是布林、華爾、福利 , 和巴林 , 在耶路撒冷的社區裡 , 像布爾普林、華爾、福利 , 那些非暴力的領導者會變得更有價值 , 並且有效地運作 。
i believe that the most important thing is to understand that if we don't pay attention to these efforts , they are invisible , and it's as if they never happened .	我相信最重要的事情是要了解如果我們不注意這些努力 , 他們是隱形的 , 就像從未發生過 。
but i have seen first hand that if we do , they will multiply .	但 , 首先 , 我先舉手 , 若我們這麼做 , 他們就會跨越 。
if they multiply , their influence will grow in the overall israelipalestinian conflict .	如果他們多 , 他們的影響會成長在巴勒斯坦的衝突中 。
and theirs is the kind of influence that can finally unblock the situation .	他們的影響力可以終於阻擋這個情況 。
these leaders have proven that nonviolence works in places like budrus .	這些領導人證明非暴力工作在像布德魯斯那樣的地方 。
let's give them attention so they can prove it works everywhere .	讓我們給他們注意力 , 讓他們可以證明它在哪裡運作 。
simon sinek has a simple but powerful model for inspirational leadership all starting with a golden circle and the question " why ? " his examples include apple , martin luther king , and the wright brothers . . .	西蒙•沙克有個很簡單但很強大的模型 , 鼓舞人心領導者 , 馬丁•路德•金恩博士 , 他的案例包括蘋果、馬丁•路德•金恩 , 和 「 為什麼 ? 」
bullseye , business , entrepreneur , leadership , sales , selling , success	bullseye , 企業家 , 領導 , 銷售 , 成功 , 企業家 , 領導 , 銷售 , 成功 。
simon sinek: how great leaders inspire action	西蒙•斯坦克:偉大的領導者鼓勵行動 。
how do you explain when things don't go as we assume ?	你要如何解釋當事情不如我們假設時 , 會怎麼解釋 ?
or better , how do you explain when others are able to achieve things that seem to defy all of the assumptions ?	或更好的 , 你要如何解釋當其他人能夠達成這些假設時 , 會怎麼解釋 ?
for example: why is apple so innovative ?	例如:為什麼蘋果這麼創新 ?
year after year , after year , after year , they're more innovative than all their competition .	一年後 , 一年後 , 他們比所有的競爭都更創新 。
and yet , they're just a computer company .	然而 , 他們只是一台電腦公司 。
they're just like everyone else .	他們就像其他人一樣 。
they have the same access to the same talent , the same agencies , the same consultants , the same media .	他們有相同的顧問 , 同一群體 , 同一類的顧問 , 同樣的媒體 。
then why is it that they seem to have something different ?	為什麼他們似乎有不同的東西 ?
why is it that martin luther king led the civil rights movement ?	為什麼是馬丁路德•金恩領導民權運動 ?
he wasn't the only man who suffered in a precivil rights america , and he certainly wasn't the only great orator of the day .	他不是唯一的美國人 , 他肯定不是唯一的美國人 , 他當然不是唯一的受害者 , 而他肯定不是唯一的美國人 。
and why is it that the wright brothers were able to figure out controlled , powered man flight when there were certainly other teams who were better qualified , better funded . . .	原因是 , 萊特兄弟能夠找出控制權力 , 權力飛行的人 , 更好的資金 , 更好的資金 。
and they didn't achieve powered man flight , and the wright brothers beat them to it .	他們沒有達成權力的飛行員 , 萊特兄弟打敗他們 。
there's something else at play here .	這裡還有其他東西 。
about three and a half years ago i made a discovery .	大約三年半前 , 我做了一個發現 。
and this discovery profoundly changed my view on how i thought the world worked , and it even profoundly changed the way in which i operate in it .	這個發現深深地改變了我對世界運作的方式 , 甚至徹底改變了我的觀點 。
as it turns out , there's a pattern .	結果發現 , 有一種模式 。
as it turns out , all the great and inspiring leaders and organizations in the world whether it's apple or martin luther king or the wright brothers they all think , act and communicate the exact same way .	結果發現 , 所有偉大且激勵領袖和組織在世界各地 , 不管是蘋果或馬丁路德金 , 或馬丁路德•金 , 或他們都認為 , 行為和組織 , 也是如此 。
and it's the complete opposite to everyone else .	這是完全相反的 。
all i did was codify it , and it's probably the world's simplest idea .	我所做的就是把這個世界最簡單的想法 。
i call it the golden circle .	我稱它為黃金圓 。
why ? how ? what ?	為什麼 ? 如何 ?
this little idea explains why some organizations and some leaders are able to inspire where others aren't .	這個小點子解釋了為什麼有些組織和一些領袖能夠啟發其他的組織和一些領袖 。
let me define the terms really quickly .	讓我定義一下 。
every single person , every single organization on the planet knows what they do , 100 percent .	地球上的每一個組織 , 都知道他們做什麼 , 百分之百 。
some know how they do it , whether you call it your differentiated value proposition or your proprietary process or your usp .	有些人知道他們怎麼做 , 不論你稱之為 「 不論你是如何 」 、 「 不論 」 、 「 新型 」 、 「 新型的 」 、 「 不論 」 、 「 不論 」
but very , very few people or organizations know why they do what they do .	但 , 非常少人或組織都知道為什麼他們會這麼做 。
and by " why " i don't mean " to make a profit . "	「 為何 」 , 我並不表示 「 為何 」 帶來利潤 。
that's a result . it's always a result .	這是結果 。 結果總是會結果 。
by " why , " i mean: what's your purpose ?	「 為什麼 」 , 我的意思是:你的目的是什麼 ?
what's your cause ? what's your belief ?	你的信念是什麼 ? 你的信念是什麼 ?
why does your organization exist ?	為什麼你的組織存在 ?
why do you get out of bed in the morning ?	為什麼你早上早上起床 ?
and why should anyone care ?	為何要有人在乎 ?
well , as a result , the way we think , the way we act , the way we communicate is from the outside in .	結果 , 我們所做的 , 就是從外面來看 , 溝通的方式 。
it's obvious . we go from the clearest thing to the fuzziest thing .	這很明顯 , 我們從最清楚的事物到最明確的 。
but the inspired leaders and the inspired organizations regardless of their size , regardless of their industry all think , act and communicate from the inside out .	但激勵領袖和鼓舞人士 , 不論他們的產業都認為 , 激勵領袖和鼓舞人士 , 不管他們的產業 , 都能想像 , 激勵領袖和鼓舞人士 。
let me give you an example .	讓我舉個例子 。
i use apple because they're easy to understand and everybody gets it .	我使用蘋果 , 因為他們很容易理解 , 每個人都得到它 。
if apple were like everyone else , a marketing message from them might sound like this: " we make great computers .	如果蘋果就像每個人一樣 , 一個行銷的訊息 , 可能會聽起來像這樣: 「 我們做了很棒的電腦 。
they're beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	它們是美麗的設計 , 簡單使用和使用者友善 。
want to buy one ? " " meh . "	想買一個 ? " 啊 ! "
and that's how most of us communicate .	這是我們大多數人溝通的方式 。
that's how most marketing is done , that's how most sales is done and that's how most of us communicate interpersonally .	這是最大的銷售量 , 這是大部分的銷售量 , 這是我們最多人溝通的方式之一 。
we say what we do , we say how we're different or how we're better and we expect some sort of a behavior , a purchase , a vote , something like that .	我們會說 , 我們是怎麼樣的 , 我們會說我們是怎麼樣的 , 或我們怎麼做 , 我們會說我們是怎麼樣的 , 或我們如何做得比較好 , 我們會說我們是怎麼樣的 , 或我們如何做得比較好 , 我們會說我們是怎樣的 。
here's our new law firm: we have the best lawyers with the biggest clients , we always perform for our clients who do business with us .	這是我們的新法律 , 我們有最好的律師 , 最好的律師 , 我們總是給客戶做商業 。
here's our new car: it gets great gas mileage , it has leather seats , buy our car .	這是我們的新車:它有天氣層面 , 上面有較棒的電梯 , 可以買我們的車 。
here's how apple actually communicates .	這是蘋果的溝通方式 。
" everything we do , we believe in challenging the status quo .	「 我們所做的一切 , 我們相信挑戰現狀 。
we believe in thinking differently .	我們相信不同的思考方式 。
the way we challenge the status quo is by making our products beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	我們挑戰現狀的方式是讓我們的產品很簡單、使用和使用者友善 。
we just happen to make great computers .	我們只是做好的電腦 。
want to buy one ? "	想買一個嗎 ? 」
totally different right ? you're ready to buy a computer from me .	完全不同了嗎 ? 你準備好要買一台電腦 。
all i did was reverse the order of the information .	我所做的只是把這些資訊傳遞給資訊 。
what it proves to us is that people don't buy what you do ; people buy why you do it .	它證明我們是人們不買你做的事 , 人們買了你做的事 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要做 。
this explains why every single person in this room is perfectly comfortable buying a computer from apple .	這解釋為何在這個房間裡的每個人都非常舒服買電腦蘋果 。
but we're also perfectly comfortable buying an mp3 player from apple , or a phone from apple , or a dvr from apple .	但我們也很好地購買一個來自蘋果電腦的蘋果電腦 , 或來自蘋果的手機 , 或來自蘋果電腦的手機 。
but , as i said before , apple's just a computer company .	但 , 如同我之前所說的 , 蘋果只是電腦公司 。
there's nothing that distinguishes them structurally from any of their competitors .	沒有任何一個比喻的競爭者都能分辨出來 。
their competitors are all equally qualified to make all of these products .	他們的競爭者對這些產品有所貢獻 。
in fact , they tried .	事實上 , 他們試試了 。
a few years ago , gateway came out with flat screen tvs .	幾年前 , 高速公車開了一台電視 。
they're eminently qualified to make flat screen tvs .	他們的品質很高 , 可以製造平面螢幕電視 。
they've been making flat screen monitors for years .	幾年來 , 他們都在製作螢幕螢幕 。
dell came out with mp3 players and pdas , and they make great quality products , and they can make perfectly welldesigned products and nobody bought one .	迪爾出版的生產品質產品 , 銷售價格高品質產品 , 而且他們做得很好品質產品 , 而且他們能做出完美的產品 , 且沒有人買 。
in fact , talking about it now , we can't even imagine buying an mp3 player from dell .	事實上 , 談到現在 , 我們甚至無法想像購買一個mp3玩家 。
why would you buy an mp3 player from a computer company ?	為什麼你會買一台電腦公司的mp3玩家呢 ?
but we do it every day .	但我們每天都這麼做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要做 。
the goal is not to do business with everybody who needs what you have .	目標並不是要和所有需要你有的人一起工作 。
the goal is to do business with people who believe what you believe .	目標是要和那些相信你相信的人一起做商業 。
here's the best part: none of what i'm telling you is my opinion .	這是最好的部分:沒有我告訴你的 , 是我的意見 。
it's all grounded in the tenets of biology .	它是生物學的基礎 。
not psychology , biology .	不是心理學、生物學 。
if you look at a crosssection of the human brain , looking from the top down , what you see is the human brain is actually broken into three major components that correlate perfectly with the golden circle .	如果你仔細觀察人類腦部的功能 , 會發現大腦其實是分裂成三個主要的零件 , 和黃金圈相比 。
our newest brain , our homo sapien brain , our neocortex , corresponds with the " what " level .	我們最新的大腦 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的新大腦 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的新大腦 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的新大腦 , 我們的新皮層 ,
the neocortex is responsible for all of our rational and analytical thought and language .	新皮層是負責所有我們理性、分析思想和語言的新皮質 。
the middle two sections make up our limbic brains , and our limbic brains are responsible for all of our feelings , like trust and loyalty .	中間兩個區塊會讓我們的腦部負責 , 我們的肢體大腦負責所有我們的感覺 , 像是信任和忠誠 。
it's also responsible for all human behavior , all decisionmaking , and it has no capacity for language .	它也負責所有人類行為、決策 , 且沒有能力 。
in other words , when we communicate from the outside in , yes , people can understand vast amounts of complicated information like features and benefits and facts and figures .	換句話說 , 當我們從外面交流時 , 是的 , 人們可以理解大量複雜的資訊 , 比如特徵、利益、事實和事實 。
it just doesn't drive behavior .	它只是沒有驅動行為 。
when we can communicate from the inside out , we're talking directly to the part of the brain that controls behavior , and then we allow people to rationalize it with the tangible things we say and do .	當我們能從外面交流時 , 我們會直接對大腦控制行為的大腦控制行為 , 然後我們會讓人們可以用我們所說的和做的方式來分析它 。
this is where gut decisions come from .	這是腸道的決策 。
you know , sometimes you can give somebody all the facts and figures , and they say , " i know what all the facts and details say , but it just doesn't feel right . "	你知道 , 有時候你會給某人的事實和細節 , 說: 「 我知道所有事實和細節 , 都可以給別人 , 但那只是感覺不好 。 」
why would we use that verb , it doesn't " feel " right ?	為什麼我們會用這個詞 , 不是 「 感覺 」 是的 ?
because the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking doesn't control language .	因為大腦的一部分 , 控制決策並不控制語言 。
and the best we can muster up is , " i don't know . it just doesn't feel right . "	最好的辦法是: 「 我不知道 , 感覺不好 。 」
or sometimes you say you're leading with your heart , or you're leading with your soul .	有時候你會說你是你的心臟 , 或是你會帶著你的心靈去 。
well , i hate to break it to you , those aren't other body parts controlling your behavior .	嗯 , 我討厭你們 , 那些不是其他身體部件控制你的行為 。
it's all happening here in your limbic brain , the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking and not language .	它在你的肢體大腦裡發生了 , 大腦的部分是控制決策和非語言的部分 。
but if you don't know why you do what you do , and people respond to why you do what you do , then how will you ever get people to vote for you , or buy something from you , or , more importantly , be loyal and want to be a part of what it is that you do .	但如果你不知道為什麼你會這麼做 , 而人們會為你做的事 , 或更重要的是 , 忠誠 , 想要成為你所做的事 。
again , the goal is not just to sell to people who need what you have ; the goal is to sell to people who believe what you believe .	同樣地 , 目標不僅僅是賣給那些你相信的人 , 目標是要賣給那些相信你相信的人 。
the goal is not just to hire people who need a job ; it's to hire people who believe what you believe .	目標不僅僅是僱用一個工作的人 , 而是要僱用那些相信你相信的人 。
i always say that , you know , if you hire people just because they can do a job , they'll work for your money , but if you hire people who believe what you believe , they'll work for you with blood and sweat and tears .	我總是說 , 你知道 , 如果你僱用人 , 他們會為你工作 , 但如果你僱用那些相信你所相信的人 , 他們會為你的錢做工作 , 但如果你僱用那些相信你的人 , 他們會為你的錢做工作 , 但如果你僱用人 , 他們會為你的錢做工作 , 但如果你僱用人 , 他們會為你工作 。
and nowhere else is there a better example of this than with the wright brothers .	另外還有一個更好的例子 , 比萊特兄弟更好 。
most people don't know about samuel pierpont langley .	大部分的人不知道samuelpontlangley
and back in the early 20th century , the pursuit of powered man flight was like the dot com of the day .	回到20世紀初期 , 電力飛行的追求力量飛行就像是日常的飛行 。
everybody was trying it .	每個人都在嘗試 。
and samuel pierpont langley had , what we assume , to be the recipe for success .	samuelpierpontlangley , 我們所假設的就是成功的成功 。
i mean , even now , you ask people , " why did your product or why did your company fail ? "	我的意思是 , 即使現在 , 你問人們: 「 為什麼你的產品或為什麼你的公司失敗了 ? 」
and people always give you the same permutation of the same three things: undercapitalized , the wrong people , bad market conditions .	人們總是給你相同的三樣東西: 「 不好的市場條件 」 、 「 壞市場條件 」 。
it's always the same three things , so let's explore that .	它總是一樣的三件事 , 所以我們來探索 。
samuel pierpont langley was given 50 , 000 dollars by the war department to figure out this flying machine .	samuelpierpontlangley是5萬美金的飛行機器
money was no problem .	錢沒有問題 。
he held a seat at harvard and worked at the smithsonian and was extremely wellconnected ; he knew all the big minds of the day .	他在smithsonian和smithsmithsonian做了一個非常好的調查 , 他知道所有的大心靈 。
he hired the best minds money could find and the market conditions were fantastic .	他僱用了最好的智慧金錢能找到和市場條件很棒 。
the new york times followed him around everywhere , and everyone was rooting for langley .	紐約時報追蹤了他 , 每個人都在根深蒂固 。
then how come we've never heard of samuel pierpont langley ?	我們從來沒有聽過samuelpontlangley ?
a few hundred miles away in dayton ohio , orville and wilbur wright , they had none of what we consider to be the recipe for success .	幾百英里遠 , 在天頓俄亥俄州 , 俄亥俄州 , 俄亥俄州 , 我們認為是成功的成功 。
they had no money ; they paid for their dream with the proceeds from their bicycle shop ; not a single person on the wright brothers' team had a college education , not even orville or wilbur ; and the new york times followed them around nowhere .	他們沒有錢 , 也沒有錢 ; 他們從他們的腳踏車店裡賺錢 ; 而紐約時報追蹤他們沒有錢 。
the difference was , orville and wilbur were driven by a cause , by a purpose , by a belief .	差異是 , 由一個目的 , 由一個目的而來的 , 由一個信念來驅動 。
they believed that if they could figure out this flying machine , it'll change the course of the world .	他們相信如果他們能想出這個飛行機器 , 它會改變世界 。
samuel pierpont langley was different .	samuelpontlangley是不同的
he wanted to be rich , and he wanted to be famous .	他想要有錢 , 他想要有名 。
he was in pursuit of the result .	他在追求結果 。
he was in pursuit of the riches .	他在追求富裕的追求 。
and lo and behold , look what happened .	然後 , 看看發生了什麼事 。
the people who believed in the wright brothers' dream worked with them with blood and sweat and tears .	那些相信萊兄弟的夢想 , 與他們血汗、汗淚和淚水有關 。
the others just worked for the paycheck .	其他人則只是為了付錢而做 。
and they tell stories of how every time the wright brothers went out , they would have to take five sets of parts , because that's how many times they would crash before they came in for supper .	他們會說 , 每次 , 老兄弟出去時 , 他們會花五組零件 , 因為那是他們花了五個組件 , 因為那是多次他們會拿到五組零件 。
and , eventually , on december 17th , 1903 , the wright brothers took flight , and no one was there to even experience it .	最後 , 在1903年12月17日 , 萊特兄弟飛行了 , 沒有人會去體驗它 。
we found out about it a few days later .	我們在幾天後就發現了 。
and further proof that langley was motivated by the wrong thing: the day the wright brothers took flight , he quit .	更進一步的證明 , 萊恩的憤怒被誤解了 , 萊特兄弟飛行了 , 他辭掉了 。
he could have said , " that's an amazing discovery , guys , and i will improve upon your technology , " but he didn't .	他可以說: 「 那是個驚人的發現 , 我會改善你的科技 。 」 但他沒有 。
he wasn't first , he didn't get rich , he didn't get famous so he quit .	他不是第一次 , 他沒有賺錢 , 他沒有很有名 , 所以他辭掉了 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要做 。
and if you talk about what you believe , you will attract those who believe what you believe .	如果你談到你相信的東西 , 你就會吸引那些相信你相信的人 。
but why is it important to attract those who believe what you believe ?	但為什麼要吸引那些相信你相信的人呢 ?
something called the law of diffusion of innovation , and if you don't know the law , you definitely know the terminology .	一種稱為 「 法律 」 的法律 , 如果你不知道法律 , 你絕對知道 「 法律 」 。
the first two and a half percent of our population are our innovators .	我們的人口中有1%的人口是創新者 。
the next 13 and a half percent of our population are our early adopters .	接下來的13.5%人口是我們的早期採用者 。
the next 34 percent are your early majority , your late majority and your laggards .	接下來的34%是你的早期大量 , 你的大量和你的早期 。
the only reason these people buy touch tone phones is because you can't buy rotary phones anymore .	人們買到手機的唯一原因是 , 因為你不能買到手機 。
we all sit at various places at various times on this scale , but what the law of diffusion of innovation tells us is that if you want massmarket success or massmarket acceptance of an idea , you cannot have it until you achieve this tipping point between 15 and 18 percent market penetration , and then the system tips .	我們都坐在各個不同的地方 , 各式各樣的情況都一樣 , 但 , 除非創新告訴我們 , 如果你想要大規模市場的執行 , 或大規模市場的執行 , 你不能直到你達成這個目標 , 直到你達成這個目標 , 到達十五到18%的市場爆炸 。
and i love asking businesses , " what's your conversion on new business ? "	我很喜歡問企業: 「 你的版本在新商業發生什麼事 ? 」
and they love to tell you , " oh , it's about 10 percent , " proudly .	他們很喜歡告訴你: 「 喔 , 大概10% 。 」
well , you can trip over 10 percent of the customers .	嗯 , 你可以試驗超過10%的客戶 。
we all have about 10 percent who just " get it . "	我們都有大約10%的人 , 只是 「 得到 」 。
that's how we describe them , right ?	這就是我們描述他們的方式 , 對吧 ?
that's like that gut feeling , " oh , they just get it . "	那就像是腸道般的感覺: 「 喔 , 他們就去了 。 」
the problem is: how do you find the ones that get it before you're doing business with them versus the ones who don't get it ?	問題是:你在做商業之前 , 和他們對他們做生意的人 , 沒有什麼 ?
so it's this here , this little gap that you have to close , as jeffrey moore calls it , " crossing the chasm " because , you see , the early majority will not try something until someone else has tried it first .	所以這就是這個小小的差距 , 你看到的 , 最早的大部份不會嘗試 , 直到有人嘗試過它 , 首先 。
and these guys , the innovators and the early adopters , they're comfortable making those gut decisions .	這些人 , 創新者和早期的採訪者 , 他們很舒適地做這些決定 。
they're more comfortable making those intuitive decisions that are driven by what they believe about the world and not just what product is available .	他們更舒適地做出這些直覺的決策 , 是因為他們相信世界 , 而不只是產品的產品 。
these are the people who stood in line for six hours to buy an iphone when they first came out , when you could have just walked into the store the next week and bought one off the shelf .	這些人站在六個小時買一台iphone , 當他們第一次出櫃時 , 你只要走進店裡 , 買一台iphone , 然後買了一台iphone , 只要走進店裡 , 就可以走進店裡 , 買了一台iphone 。
these are the people who spent 40 , 000 dollars on flat screen tvs when they first came out , even though the technology was substandard .	這些人花了四萬美元在平面電視上 , 直到他們出去時 , 即便科技是被標記出來的 。
and , by the way , they didn't do it because the technology was so great ; they did it for themselves .	順便一提 , 他們沒有這麼做 , 因為科技太棒了 , 他們也為自己做 。
it's because they wanted to be first .	因為他們想要成為第一個 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it and what you do simply proves what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你做什麼 ; 他們買了你為什麼做的事 , 以及你所做的是證明你所相信的 。
in fact , people will do the things that prove what they believe .	事實上 , 人們會做那些證明他們相信的事 。
the reason that person bought the iphone in the first six hours , stood in line for six hours , was because of what they believed about the world , and how they wanted everybody to see them: they were first .	人們買了iphone在六個小時內 , 是因為他們所相信的世界 , 以及他們如何希望每個人看到他們:他們是第一個 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要做 。
so let me give you a famous example , a famous failure and a famous success of the law of diffusion of innovation .	讓我給各位一個有名的例子 , 一個有名的例子 , 一個有名的成功 , 一個有名的成功 。
first , the famous failure .	首先 , 有名的失敗 。
it's a commercial example .	這是一個商業的例子 。
as we said before , a second ago , the recipe for success is money and the right people and the right market conditions , right ? you should have success then .	正如我們剛剛說的 , 第一個成功是金錢和權利的市場條件 , 對吧 ? 你應該成功 。
from the time tivo came out about eight or nine years ago to this current day , they are the single highestquality product on the market , hands down , there is no dispute .	直到19年前 , 直到今日 , 他們是市場上最高品質的產品 , 沒錯 。
they were extremely wellfunded .	他們非常受歡迎 。
market conditions were fantastic .	市場條件很棒 。
i mean , we use tivo as verb .	我的意思是 , 我們用 「 反彈 」 的詞 。
i tivo stuff on my piece of junk time warner dvr all the time .	我把東西放在我的垃圾場裡 , 每次都在垃圾場上 。
but tivo's a commercial failure .	但tivo是個商業失敗 。
they've never made money .	他們從來沒有賺錢 。
and when they went ipo , their stock was at about 30 or 40 dollars and then plummeted , and it's never traded above 10 .	當他們進入ipo時 , 他們的股票大約是30、40美元 , 而且從來沒有貿易到30到40美元 。
in fact , i don't think it's even traded above six , except for a couple of little spikes .	事實上 , 我不認為它已經超過六分之一 , 除了幾個小的小行星上 。
because you see , when tivo launched their product they told us all what they had .	因為你看到 , 當tivo發出他們的產品時 , 他們告訴我們他們所擁有的一切 。
they said , " we have a product that pauses live tv , skips commercials , rewinds live tv and memorizes your viewing habits without you even asking . "	他們說: 「 我們有一個產品 , 暫停生活電視 , 錄音機 , 電視節目 , 收集電視 , 記住電視 , 記住電視 , 記錄你的觀看習慣 , 沒有你會問 。 」
and the cynical majority said , " we don't believe you .	古典人說: 「 我們不相信你 。
we don't need it . we don't like it .	我們不需要它 。 我們不需要它 。
you're scaring us . "	你害怕我們 。 」
what if they had said , " if you're the kind of person who likes to have total control over every aspect of your life , boy , do we have a product for you .	如果他們說: 「 如果你是這樣的人 , 無論你生活中的每一個面向 , 或男孩 , 我們有產品給你 。
it pauses live tv , skips commercials , memorizes your viewing habits , etc . , etc . "	它暫停生活的電視 , 紀錄片 , 記者 , 記住你看待習慣等等等等 。 」

in the summer of 1963 , 250 , 000 people showed up on the mall in washington to hear dr . king speak .	1963年夏天 , 有25萬人在華盛頓特區去聽見金恩博士演講 。
they sent out no invitations , and there was no website to check the date .	他們寄出沒有邀請 , 也沒有網站去查查日子 。
how do you do that ?	你該怎麼做 ?

and lo and behold , 250 , 000 people showed up on the right day at the right time to hear him speak .	很快的 , 有25 , 000人在右邊的時間聽他說話 。
how many of them showed up for him ?	在座有多少人給他看 ?
they showed up for themselves .	他們向自己展示 。
it's what they believed about america that got them to travel in a bus for eight hours to stand in the sun in washington in the middle of august .	他們相信美國 , 讓他們在八個小時站在八個小時站在華盛頓特區旁邊的太陽 。

dr . king believed that there are two types of laws in this world: those that are made by a higher authority and those that are made by man .	金恩博士相信有兩種法律在這個世界:那些是由一個較高權威的法律所組成的 。
and not until all the laws that are made by man are consistent with the laws that are made by the higher authority will we live in a just world .	直到所有法律 , 由人類的法律所構成的法律 , 都是由我們所擁有的法律所構成的 , 由於我們所擁有的法律 , 都是由更高的權威所造成的 。
it just so happened that the civil rights movement was the perfect thing to help him bring his cause to life .	正是如此 , 民權運動是完美的 , 幫助他帶來生命的原因 。
we followed , not for him , but for ourselves .	我們追求他 , 而不是為了自己 。
