how do you remember where you parked your car ? how do you know if you're moving in the right direction ? neuroscientist neil burgess studies the neural mechanisms that map the space around us , and how they link to memory and imagination .	你怎麼記得你停車在哪裡 ? 你怎麼記得你停車在哪裡 ? 你怎麼記得你停車在哪裡 ? 你怎麼記得你停車在哪裡 ? 你怎麼記得你停車在哪裡 ? 你怎麼記得你停車在哪裡 ? 你怎麼記得你停車在哪裡 ? 你怎麼記得你停車在哪裡 ? 你怎麼記得你停車在哪裡 ? 你怎麼記得你停車在哪裡 ? 你怎麼記得你停車在哪裡 ?
brain , cognitive science , exploration , neuroscience , science	大腦、認知科學、探索、神經科學 。
neil burgess: how your brain tells you where you are	尼爾瓦格斯:你的大腦如何告訴你你在哪裡 。
when we park in a big parking lot , how do we remember where we parked our car ?	當我們在公園大停車時 , 我們要如何記得我們停車在哪裡 ?
here's the problem facing homer .	這裡有一個問題 ,
and we're going to try to understand what's happening in his brain .	我們要試著了解他腦內發生了什麼事 。
so we'll start with the hippocampus , shown in yellow , which is the organ of memory .	我們先從海馬迴開始 , 海馬體是記憶的器官 。
if you have damage there , like in alzheimer's , you can't remember things including where you parked your car .	如果你有傷害 , 比如阿茲海默症 , 你無法記住東西包括你停車在哪裡 。
it's named after latin for " seahorse , " which it resembles .	在拉丁文 「 海馬 」 之後 , 它的名字是 「 海馬 」 。
and like the rest of the brain , it's made of neurons .	就像其他的大腦一樣 , 它是由神經元組成的 。
so the human brain has about a hundred billion neurons in it .	人類的大腦有大約一百億個神經元 。
and the neurons communicate with each other by sending little pulses or spikes of electricity via connections to each other .	神經元會互相溝通 , 互相交流 , 傳遞出一些脈衝 , 或連接彼此的電荷 。
the hippocampus is formed of two sheets of cells , which are very densely interconnected .	海馬體是由兩個細胞組成的 , 它們非常密切相互連結 。
and scientists have begun to understand how spatial memory works by recording from individual neurons in rats or mice while they forage or explore an environment looking for food .	科學家已經開始了解 , 藉由個人神經元傳播、老鼠、老鼠 , 或老鼠 , 來探索環境尋找食物 。
so we're going to imagine we're recording from a single neuron in the hippocampus of this rat here .	所以 , 我們會想像我們正在記錄一個神經元在海馬體的海馬體 。
and when it fires a little spike of electricity , there's going to be a red dot and a click .	當它發出電力時 , 會有一個紅點和點點 。
so what we see is that this neuron knows whenever the rat has gone into one particular place in its environment .	所以 , 我們看到的是這個神經元知道 , 當這個神經元知道 , 當這個神經元知道時 , 牠的環境中就會產生一個特定的環境 。
and it signals to the rest of the brain by sending a little electrical spike .	它訊號到大腦的訊號 , 傳送一個小電動脈 。
so we could show the firing rate of that neuron as a function of the animal's location .	所以我們可以看到神經元的功能是動物的位置 。
and if we record from lots of different neurons , we'll see that different neurons fire when the animal goes in different parts of its environment , like in this square box shown here .	如果我們從不同類的神經元發射 , 我們會發現不同神經元的不同部分 , 如同在這個平方盒子的圖表 , 會看到不同的神經元 。
so together they form a map for the rest of the brain , telling the brain continually , " where am i now within my environment ? "	所以 , 他們把這張地圖放到大腦的地圖上 , 說: 「 我現在在哪裡 ? 」
place cells are also being recorded in humans .	細胞也被記錄在人類身上
so epilepsy patients sometimes need the electrical activity in their brain monitoring .	所以癲癇患有時需要電動活動在他們的大腦監控 。
and some of these patients played a video game where they drive around a small town .	有些病人在小鎮上玩電玩遊戲 。
and place cells in their hippocampi would fire , become active , start sending electrical impulses whenever they drove through a particular location in that town .	當它們穿過一個特定的位置 , 就會開始發送電脈衝 , 只要在那鎮上 , 就會開始傳送電脈衝 。
so how does a place cell know where the rat or person is within its environment ?	所以 , 一個細胞知道哪個位置是哪裡的 , 哪個位置是哪個細胞 ?
well these two cells here show us that the boundaries of the environment are particularly important .	這兩個細胞告訴我們 , 環境的界線非常重要 。
so the one on the top likes to fire sort of midway between the walls of the box that their rat's in .	所以 , 最頂端的頂端 , 像是在箱子裡的空氣中 , 打開空氣的牆壁 。
and when you expand the box , the firing location expands .	當你擴展到這個盒子時 , 就會擴大的空間 。
the one below likes to fire whenever there's a wall close by to the south .	一旦被到南邊的山脈衝擊時 , 就會消失 。
and if you put another wall inside the box , then the cell fires in both place wherever there's a wall to the south as the animal explores around in its box .	如果你把另一個牆放進盒子裡 , 另一邊牆就在盒子裡 , 另外一面牆在盒子裡 , 另一壁在盒子裡 , 就會有一面牆 , 在盒子裡 。
so this predicts that sensing the distances and directions of boundaries around you extended buildings and so on is particularly important for the hippocampus .	所以 , 這種預測會讓海馬體的距離和分裂 , 讓海馬體變得非常重要 。
and indeed , on the inputs to the hippocampus , cells are found which project into the hippocampus , which do respond exactly to detecting boundaries or edges at particular distances and directions from the rat or mouse as it's exploring around .	實際上 , 針對海馬體的推動 , 到海馬體 , 牠們會發現到海馬體的特定位置 , 牠們會在海馬迴的軌跡中發現 , 牠會在海馬迴中發現 , 牠會在海馬迴中找到牠的位置 , 牠們會發現牠在海馬迴的位置 。
so the cell on the left , you can see , it fires whenever the animal gets near to a wall or a boundary to the east , whether it's the edge or the wall of a square box or the circular wall of the circular box or even the drop at the edge of a table , which the animals are running around .	左邊的細胞 , 你可以看到 , 它的火流在周圍的牆壁上 , 不管是邊緣或牆壁 , 或邊緣的牆壁 , 或邊緣的牆壁 , 不管是邊緣或是牆壁 , 或邊緣的牆壁 , 都可以看見 。
and the cell on the right there fires whenever there's a boundary to the south , whether it's the drop at the edge of the table or a wall or even the gap between two tables that are pulled apart .	右邊的那張圖片 , 右邊的電池 , 不管是在桌面上或牆壁或牆壁之間的差距 , 還是牆壁 , 甚至是兩張桌子之間的距離 。
so that's one way in which we think place cells determine where the animal is as it's exploring around .	這是我們認為細胞決定動物在哪裡做的事 。

and what you see , for example , if the flag was where that cross was in a small square environment , and then if you ask people where it was , but you've made the environment bigger , where they think the flag had been stretches out in exactly the same way that the place cell firing stretched out .	舉例來說 , 如果旗幟在一個小型平方環境中 , 在那裡 , 你可以看到 , 如果旗幟在一個小平方環境下 , 你就會看到 , 例如 , 如果旗幟在一個小平方環境下 , 你就會看到 , 例如 , 如果旗幟在一個小平方環境下 , 你就會看到 , 例如 , 如果旗幟在一個小平方環境中 , 會發生什麼事 , 然後如果你問他們 , 你會看到什麼 。
it's as if you remember where the flag was by storing the pattern of firing across all of your place cells at that location , and then you can get back to that location by moving around so that you best match the current pattern of firing of your place cells with that stored pattern .	正如你所想像的 , 那個地點在地位的位置 , 可以回到那個地方的位置 , 然後你就可以回到那個地方的位置 , 然後你就可以回到那個位置 , 然後你就可以回到那個位置 , 然後你就可以回到那個地方的位置 , 然後你就可以回到那個地方的位置 , 然後你就可以回到那個地方的位置 , 然後你就可以回到那個地方的位置 , 然後你就可以回到那個地方的位置 。
that guides you back to the location that you want to remember .	這指導你回到你想要記住的位置 。
but we also know where we are through movement .	但我們也知道我們正在經歷運動 。
so if we take some outbound path perhaps we park and we wander off we know because our own movements , which we can integrate over this path roughly what the heading direction is to go back .	所以 , 若我們能把這條路徑往往往往方向的方向 , 我們就能整合這條路徑 , 才能整合這條路徑 , 才能整合這條路徑 , 才能整合這條路徑 , 以往往往往往方向方向的方向 。
and place cells also get this kind of path integration input from a kind of cell called a grid cell .	細胞也得到了一種類似的細胞 , 叫做 「 網絡細胞 」 。
now grid cells are found , again , on the inputs to the hippocampus , and they're a bit like place cells .	網格細胞在輸入海馬迴時 , 它們有點像細胞 。
but now as the rat explores around , each individual cell fires in a whole array of different locations which are laid out across the environment in an amazingly regular triangular grid .	現在 , 當老鼠探險時 , 每個個別的細胞都會開火 , 各個不同的地點 , 都在一個很奇妙的頻繁地點下 。
and if you record from several grid cells shown here in different colors each one has a gridlike firing pattern across the environment , and each cell's gridlike firing pattern is shifted slightly relative to the other cells .	如果你從幾個格格細胞的網格圖案中 , 每一個細胞的網格圖案 , 每個細胞的網格圖案 , 每個細胞的網格圖案就會轉變為其他細胞 。
so the red one fires on this grid and the green one on this one and the blue on on this one .	所以 , 紅色的綠色在這個上面 , 藍色在這個上面 。
so together , it's as if the rat can put a virtual grid of firing locations across its environment a bit like the latitude and longitude lines that you'd find on a map , but using triangles .	所以 , 結合起來 , 像老鼠可以在地圖上找到一個虛擬的網絡 , 可以在地圖上找到一個虛擬的網絡 , 可以在地圖上找到一張地圖 , 但用三角形 。
and as it moves around , the electrical activity can pass from one of these cells to the next cell to keep track of where it is , so that it can use its own movements to know where it is in its environment .	隨著它移動 , 電動活動可以從一個細胞到下一個細胞 , 到下一個細胞 , 到下一個細胞 , 可以通過這個細胞來追蹤它的位置 , 所以它可以用它的動作來保持追蹤 。
do people have grid cells ?	人們有網絡細胞嗎 ?
well because all of the gridlike firing patterns have the same axes of symmetry , the same orientations of grid , shown in orange here , it means that the net activity of all of the grid cells in a particular part of the brain should change according to whether we're running along these six directions or running along one of the six directions in between .	由於這些特定的神經活動 , 代表網格細胞的特定部位 , 代表網格細胞的位置 , 也就是說網格細胞的位置 , 也就是說 , 網格細胞的特定部分 , 表示 , 網格細胞的每一部分都有相同的指標 , 也就是說 , 網格細胞的每一部分都有相同的指標 , 也就是說 , 網格細胞的每一部分都有相同的數量 , 也就是說 , 每一根網格 , 每一根都有相同的數量 , 也就是說 , 網格細胞的位置是六個方向的一部分 。
so we can put people in an mri scanner and have them do a little video game like the one i showed you and look for this signal .	所以 , 我們可以把人放進核磁共振掃描儀裡 , 看看這個訊號 。
and indeed , you do see it in the human entorhinal cortex , which is the same part of the brain that you see grid cells in rats .	的確 , 你可以看到在人類皮質上 , 大腦的一部分是大腦的一部分 , 你可以看到細胞在同一部分 。
so back to homer .	回到家鄉 。
he's probably remembering where his car was in terms of the distances and directions to extended buildings and boundaries around the location where he parked .	他可能記得他的車子在距離和方向的位置 , 讓他停留在地點的位置 。
and that would be represented by the firing of boundarydetecting cells .	這就代表了 , 細胞的邊緣細胞 。
he's also remembering the path he took out of the car park , which would be represented in the firing of grid cells .	他還記得他從車停車站出來的路徑 , 它會代表在網格細胞的路上 。

so beyond spatial memory , if we look for this gridlike firing pattern throughout the whole brain , we see it in a whole series of locations which are always active when we do all kinds of autobiographical memory tasks , like remembering the last time you went to a wedding , for example .	所以 , 超越空間記憶 , 只要我們在整個大腦中看到它 , 我們就會看到它在整個腦部的位置 , 我們看到它 , 在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它
so it may be that the neural mechanisms for representing the space around us are also used for generating visual imagery so that we can recreate the spatial scene , at least , of the events that have happened to us when we want to imagine them .	所以 , 可能是神經機制 , 代表我們周遭的環境 , 可能是用來產生視覺影像 , 使我們能夠重現特殊的事件 , 如同我們所見到的事件發生在我們身邊何處 。
so if this was happening , your memories could start by place cells activating each other via these dense interconnections and then reactivating boundary cells to create the spatial structure of the scene around your viewpoint .	所以 , 如果發生了 , 你的記憶可以從細胞開始 , 讓細胞在你的記憶中 , 透過這些密集的空間結構 , 來創造出你周遭的空間結構 。
and grid cells could move this viewpoint through that space .	而網格細胞可以移動這個觀點 。
another kind of cell , head direction cells , which i didn't mention yet , they fire like a compass according to which way you're facing .	另一種類型的細胞 , 例如 , 我沒有提到的 , 腦部的方向細胞 , 正如你所面臨的一樣 。
they could define the viewing direction from which you want to generate an image for your visual imagery , so you can imagine what happened when you were at this wedding , for example .	他們可以定義你所看到的景象 , 以你的視覺影像 , 所以你可以想像你在這個婚禮時會發生什麼事 。
so this is just one example of a new era really in cognitive neuroscience where we're beginning to understand psychological processes like how you remember or imagine or even think in terms of the actions of the billions of individual neurons that make up our brains .	這只是一個例子 , 一個新時代的大腦 , 我們開始了解心理過程 , 例如你記得或想像 , 甚至思考一下 , 腦部的數十億個神經元的形成 。
thank you very much .	謝謝大家
imagine a global security driven by collaboration among agencies , government , the private sector and the public . that's not just the distant hope of opensource fans , it's the vision of james stavridis , the supreme commander of nato , who shares vivid moments from recent military history to explain why security of the future should be built with bridges rather than walls .	想像一下 , 全球安全的開放原始碼 , 它是jamsssteavridissteavridissteavridissteavridissteavridissteavridissteavridissteavridissteavridissteavridissteavridissteavridissteavridissteavridissteavridissteavridissteavridissteavridissteavridissteavridissteavridissteavridissteavridissteavridissteavridissteavridissteavridissteavridissteavridisstevessstevessssteveridissteavridissteavridissteavridissteavridissteavridissteavridissteavridissteavridissteavridisstevid
collaboration , global issues , opensource , peace , politics , social media , violence , war	合作 , 全球議題 , 開放資源、公開資源、和平、政治、社群媒體、暴力、戰爭 。
james stavridis: how nato's supreme commander thinks about global security	詹姆斯•史維里迪斯:納多•史維里迪斯:納多•史維里迪斯:納多•史維里迪斯:納多•史維里迪斯:如何
i'm gonna talk a little bit about opensource security , because we've got to get better at security in this 21st century .	我要談談開放資源安全的安全 , 因為我們在這個21世紀的安全更好了 。
let me start by saying , let's look back to the 20th century , and kind of get a sense of how that style of security worked for us .	讓我開始說 , 咱們來看看二十世紀 , 感覺一下 , 我們來看看二十世紀 , 感覺對我們來說是安全的運作方式 。
this is verdun , a battlefield in france just north of the nato headquarters in belgium .	這是在北方 , 法國北部的一個戰場 , 位於北方的北方 。
at verdun , in 1916 , over a 300day period , 700 , 000 people were killed , so about 2 , 000 a day .	在1916年 , 約有70萬人死了 , 大約有2 , 000人死亡 。
if you roll it forward 20thcentury security into the second world war , you see the battle of stalingrad , 300 days , 2 million people killed .	如果你在第二次世界大戰結束時 , 你看到戰爭 , 三百天 , 兩百萬人死亡 。
we go into the cold war , and we continue to try and build walls .	我們進入冷戰 , 我們繼續嘗試建造牆壁 。
we go from the trench warfare of the first world war to the maginot line of the second world war , and then we go into the cold war , the iron curtain , the berlin wall .	我們從第一次世界大戰的戰場開始 , 進入冷戰 , 伊隆曲線 , 第二次世界大戰的戰場 , 然後我們進入冷戰的戰場 。
my thesis for us today is , instead of building walls to create security , we need to build bridges .	我今天的演講是 , 我們不需要建造橋樑 , 也需要建立橋樑 。
this is a famous bridge in europe .	這是歐洲的橋樑 。
it's the bridge over the drina river , the subject of a novel by ivo andrić , and it talks about how , in that very troubled part of europe and the balkans , over time there's been enormous building of walls .	它是來自於華盛頓特區的一座大樓 , 一個小說 , 和巴爾卡河的大樓 , 和巴爾幹半島的一小部分 , 和巴爾斯坦的橋樑 , 很不可思議的是 , 歐洲和巴爾幹半島 。
more recently , in the last decade , we begin to see these communities start , hesitatingly , to come together .	最近 , 幾十年來 , 我們開始看到這些社區開始 , 開始見到這些社區 , 開始 , 開始見到這些社區 。
i would argue , again , opensource security is about connecting the international , the interagency , the privatepublic , and lashing it together with strategic communication , largely in social networks .	我會說 , 開放的資源安全是關聯國際網路 , 公開資源安全 , 與策略性溝通 , 在社交網絡中 。
so let me talk a little bit about why we need to do that , because our global commons is under attack in a variety of ways , and none of the sources of threat to the global commons will be solved by building walls .	所以 , 讓我來談談我們為什麼要做這件事 , 因為我們全球公共的資源受到威脅 , 全球公眾都受到攻擊 , 並且沒有任何威脅到全球共同點 , 來解決建築牆 。
now , i'm a sailor , obviously .	當然 , 我是個帆船員 。
this is a ship , a liner , clipping through the indian ocean .	這是一艘船 , 一艘船 , 橫跨印度洋 。
what's wrong with this picture ?	這張照片有什麼問題 ?
it's got concertina wire along the sides of it .	這裡有塞爾蒂娜•路線 。
that's to prevent pirates from attacking it .	要防止海盜來防止海盜 。
piracy is a very active threat today around the world . this is in the indian ocean .	piracy是非常全球的威脅 , 這是在印度洋 。
piracy is also very active in the strait of malacca .	piracy也在馬拉克卡的歷史上非常活躍 。
it's active in the gulf of guinea .	它是活躍在瓜地南亞 。
we see it in the caribbean .	我們在加勒比海看到它 。
it's a $10billionayear discontinuity in the global transport system .	這是在全球運輸系統中百分之十的百分比 。
last year , at this time , there were 20 vessels , 500 mariners held hostage .	去年 , 在這個時候 , 有20個船員 , 500名馬丁爾斯特 。
this is an attack on the global commons .	這是全球常見的攻擊 。
we need to think about how to address it .	我們需要考慮如何處理它 。
let's shift to a different kind of sea , the cyber sea .	讓我們轉換到不同的海洋 , 網路海 。
here are photographs of two young men .	這是兩個年輕人的照片 。
at the moment , they're incarcerated .	那時 , 他們被監禁 。
they conducted a credit card fraud that netted them over 10 billion dollars .	他們做了一項信用卡詐欺 , 給他們超過十億美金 。
this is part of cybercrime which is a $2trillionayear discontinuity in the global economy .	這是網路犯罪的一部分 , 這是網路犯罪的一部分 , 它是全球經濟的二分之一 。
two trillion a year .	每年兩兆美元 。
that's just under the gdp of great britain .	這只是在英國的gdp 。
so this cyber sea , which we know endlessly is the fundamental piece of radical openness , is very much under threat as well .	所以這個網路的海洋 , 我們所知無止是徹底的基礎 , 很明顯的基礎是徹底的基礎 。
another thing i worry about in the global commons is the threat posed by trafficking , by the movement of narcotics , opium , here coming out of afghanistan through europe over to the united states .	另一件我擔心的事情是威脅 , 來自非洲的威脅 , 通過歐洲來到美國 。
we worry about cocaine coming from the andean ridge north .	我們擔心古柯鹼來自北方的古柯鹼 。
we worry about the movement of illegal weapons and trafficking . above all , perhaps , we worry about human trafficking , and the awful cost of it .	我們擔心的是非法武器和販賣的風險 。 最重要的是 , 我們擔心人們販賣的價值 , 和販賣的重要性 。
trafficking moves largely at sea but in other parts of the global commons .	交易運行在海中運行 , 但在全球公共的另一部分 。
this is a photograph , and i wish i could tell you that this is a very hightech piece of us navy gear that we're using to stop the trafficking .	這是一張照片 , 我希望我能告訴各位這是一個非常高科技的美國海軍隊員 , 希望能告訴你們這是一個非常高科技的美國海軍隊員 , 希望能告訴你們這是個非常高科技的美國海軍隊伍軍隊 。
the bad news is , this is a semisubmersible run by drug cartels .	壞消息是 , 這是一半被毒販賣的毒品店 。
it was built in the jungles of south america .	它是南美洲的叢林 。
we caught it with that lowtech raft — — and it was carrying six tons of cocaine .	我們拿了六噸的古柯鹼 。
crew of four . sophisticated communications sweep .	四個複雜的溝通 。
this kind of trafficking , in narcotics , in humans , in weapons , god forbid , in weapons of mass destruction , is part of the threat to the global commons .	這種販賣 , 在武器上 , 人類 , 武器 , 大規模毀滅的威脅 , 都是威脅全球公眾的一部分 。
and let's pull it together in afghanistan today .	讓我們一起在阿富汗舉行 。
this is a field of poppies in afghanistan .	這是阿富汗的一場 。
eighty to 90 percent of the world's poppy , opium and heroin , comes out of afghanistan .	世界上90%的貧民窟和海洛因 , 來自阿富汗 。
we also see there , of course , terrorism .	我們也看到 , 當然 , 恐怖主義
this is where al qaeda is staged from .	這是基地組織的基礎 。
we also see a very strong insurgency embedded there .	我們也看到一個非常強烈的緊急狀況 。
so this terrorism concern is also part of the global commons , and what we must address .	所以 , 恐怖主義擔憂是全球常見的一部分 , 我們必須處理 。
so here we are , 21st century .	所以 , 這是21世紀 。
we know our 20thcentury tools are not going to work .	我們知道20世紀的工具並不會成功 。
what should we do ?	我們該怎麼做 ?
i would argue that we will not deliver security solely from the barrel of a gun .	我會說 , 我們不會把安全帶到槍枝的安全之下 。
we will not deliver security solely from the barrel of a gun .	我們不會把安全帶入槍枝的安全 。
we will need the application of military force .	我們需要應用軍隊力量 。
when we do it , we must do it well , and competently .	當我們這麼做時 , 我們必須做得很好 , 很快 。
but my thesis is , opensource security is about international , interagency , privatepublic connection pulled together by this idea of strategic communication on the internet .	但我的結論是 , 公開資源安全是國際、私人和網路的聯繫 。
let me give you a couple of examples of how this works in a positive way .	讓我舉幾個例子 , 說明它是如何運作的 。
this is afghanistan . these are afghan soldiers .	這是阿富汗 。 這些是阿富汗 。
they are all holding books .	他們全都包含書 。
you should say , " that's odd . i thought i read that this demographic , young men and women in their 20s and 30s , is largely illiterate in afghanistan . "	你應該說: 「 這很奇怪 , 我以為我讀了這個人口統計 , 年輕男性和女性 , 二十三十歲的年輕人 , 和女性在阿富汗 。 」
you would be correct .	你是正確的 。
eightyfive percent cannot read when they enter the security forces of afghanistan .	85%無法閱讀當他們進入安全武器時 。
why ? because the taliban withheld education during the period of time in which these men and women would have learned to read .	為什麼 ? 因為塔利班的教育期待在那期間 , 這些男人和女人都學會閱讀 。
so the question is , so , why are they all standing there holding books ?	所以 , 問題是 , 為什麼他們都站在書裡 ?
the answer is , we are teaching them to read in literacy courses by nato in partnership with private sector entities , in partnership with development agencies .	答案是 , 我們在教導他們讀書 , 用私人部門和開發機構合作 , 和開發機構合作 。
we've taught well over 200 , 000 afghan security forces to read and write at a basic level .	我們已經教導了超過200 , 000個阿富汗安全部隊要閱讀和寫字 。
when you can read and write in afghanistan , you will typically put a pen in your pocket .	當你閱讀和寫在阿富汗 , 你通常會把筆放在你的口袋裡 。
at the ceremonies , when these young men and women graduate , they take that pen with great pride , and put it in their pocket .	在當這些年輕男性和女性畢業時 , 他們拿著一筆錢 , 拿著一筆錢 , 然後把它放在口袋裡 。
this is bringing together international — there are 50 nations involved in this mission — interagency — these development agencies — and privatepublic , to take on this kind of security .	這裡有五十個國家參與這個任務 , 這些發展機構和私人公共機構 , 來處理這種安全 。
now , we are also teaching them combat skills , of course , but i would argue , opensource security means connecting in ways that create longer lasting security effect .	現在 , 我們也教他們對抗技能 , 當然 , 但我會說 , 開放資源的安全性 , 是一種連結方式 , 創造更久的安全性 。
this is a us navy warship .	這是美國海軍戰艦 。
it's called the comfort .	它叫做舒適 。
there's a sister ship called the mercy .	有個姐妹的船叫做 「 默斯特船 」 。
they are hospital ships .	他們是醫院的船 。
this one , the comfort , operates throughout the caribbean and the coast of south america conducting patient treatments .	此外 , 舒適圈 , 營運在加勒比海和南美洲的海岸 , 造成病人的治療 。
on a typical cruise , they'll do 400 , 000 patient treatments .	在一般的情況下 , 他們會有40萬個病人治療 。
it is crewed not strictly by military but by a combination of humanitarian organizations: operation hope , project smile .	它不是被軍隊所包容的 , 而是由軍隊所組成 , 人道組織的結合:手術希望 , 微笑 。
other organizations send volunteers .	其他組織志願者 。
interagency physicians come out .	醫療人員出來了 。
they're all part of this .	他們都是這樣 。
to give you one example of the impact this can have , this little boy , eight years old , walked with his mother two days to come to the eye clinic put on by the comfort .	給你們一個例子 , 來看看這個小男孩 , 八歲 , 和他的母親兩天來到眼睛診所 , 來到眼睛診所 。
when he was fitted , over his extremely myopic eyes , he suddenly looked up and said , " mama , veo el mundo . "	當他被送入時 , 他突然被看出來 , 說: 「 媽媽 , 維奧爾•梅拉 。 」
" mom , i see the world . "	「 媽 , 我看到世界 。 」
multiply this by 400 , 000 patient treatments , this privatepublic collaboration with security forces , and you begin to see the power of creating security in a very different way .	通過四十萬個病人治療 , 這種公共和安全的力量 , 你開始看到創造安全力量的力量 。
here you see baseball players .	這裡你看到棒球玩家 。
can you pick out the two us army soldiers in this photograph ?	你能否選出兩位美國軍隊士兵 ?
they are the two young men on either side of these young boys . this is part of a series of baseball clinics , where we have explored collaboration between major league baseball , the department of state , who sets up the diplomatic piece of this , military baseball players , who are real soldiers with real skills but participate in this mission , and they put on clinics throughout latin america and the caribbean , in honduras , in nicaragua , in all of the central american and caribbean nations where baseball is so popular , and it creates security .	他們是兩位年輕男孩的一部分 。 這是一系列的一部分 , 我們在聯合國會議 , 開辦了一場大型聯合國會議員 , 他們是一群大型的合作 , 美國和加勒比海地區 , 國內部門 , 大型聯盟軍事棒球隊員 , 和加勒比海 , 在那裡 , 美國和加勒比海地區 , 在那裡 , 美國和加勒比海地區 , 都在加勒比海 , 美國和加勒比海地區 , 在那裡 , 世界各地的美國和加勒比海 , 都在加勒比海 , 美國和加勒比海地區 , 都是如此受歡迎的 , 同時也創造了安全 。
it shows role models to young men and women about fitness and about life that i would argue help create security for us .	它展現了年輕男性和女性的關係 , 關於生活 , 我會爭論為我們創造安全 。
another aspect of this partnership is in disaster relief .	這個夥伴關係的另一面是災難 。
this is a us air force helicopter participating after the tsunami in 2004 which killed 250 , 000 people .	這是美國空軍直升機在2004年 , 殺死了250 , 000人 。
in each of these major disasters — the tsunami in 2004 , 250 , 000 dead , the kashmiri earthquake in pakistan , 2005 , 85 , 000 dead , the haitian earthquake , about 300 , 000 dead , more recently the awful earthquaketsunami combination which struck japan and its nuclear industry — in all of these instances , we see partnerships between international actors , interagency , privatepublic working with security forces to respond to this kind of natural disaster .	在所有這些事件中 , 大約3000000000 , 000個死亡 , 在巴基斯坦的兩萬五千人死亡 , 在巴基斯坦的兩萬五千人之間 , 在巴基斯坦的兩萬五千人死亡 , 海地地震 , 海地地震 , 大約30000000 , 000死 , 即將發生在巴基斯坦的一場巨大災難 , 海地地震 , 海地地震 , 海地地震 , 海地地震 , 海地地震 , 甚至是海地地震 。

no . this is a graphic of the world according to twitter .	不 , 這是世界根據推特的圖表 。

why do we want to get in these nets ?	為何我們要在這些蚊帳裡呢 ?

we talked earlier about the arab spring , and the power of all this .	我們剛剛談到阿拉伯之春 , 所有這一切的力量 。
i'll give you another example , and it's how you move this message .	我再舉另一個例子 , 就是你如何移動這個訊息 。
i gave a talk like this in london a while back about this point . i said , as i say to all of you , i'm on facebook . friend me .	我在倫敦的一場演說 , 正如我所說的 , 我在臉書上說話 , 我跟你們說 , 我在臉書上朋友 。

got picked up in two places in the world: finland and indonesia .	在世界各地有兩個地方:芬蘭和印尼 。

i would close by saying that we heard earlier today about wikipedia . i use wikipedia all the time to look up facts , and as all of you appreciate , wikipedia is not created by 12 brilliant people locked in a room writing articles .	今天 , 我用維基百科 , 維基百科 , 維基百科 , 維基百科 , 維基百科不是用維基百科所拍攝的 。 我用維基百科 , 維基百科 , 維基百科 , 只有12個聰明的人被鎖在一個房間裡寫文章 。
